{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-466}} “That cognition is precisely what is called the being Whose nature is the supreme joy. Forms of light identical to his own body emanate forth, Flooding the expanse of the sky. {2.3.22}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-467}} “Once the practitioner has absorbed them, drawing them back into his heart, He should become Heruka—one whose nature is hatred. {2.3.23}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-468}} “In the center of the expanse of the sky He should visualize a sun disk. Then from the syllable hūṁ atop the sun disk he arises, Reddish-blue in color, and adorned with all kinds of jewelry. {2.3.24}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-469}} “He has two arms, one face, Three eyes, and yellow, upward-flowing hair. With an angry gaze, and the body of a sixteen year old, He stands astride Bhairava. {2.3.25}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-470}} “With a vajra khaṭvāṅga in his left arm, A skull cup in his left hand, And a black vajra scepter in his right hand, Whose nature is to make the sound hūṁ , {2.3.26}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-471}} “The lord frolics in a charnel ground, Surrounded by the eight goddesses. The practitioner should visualize in this way The lord who is the supreme ambrosia of all practices. {2.3.27}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-472}} “He alone is the blessed practice of the union— The tathāgata Vajrasattva. {2.3.28}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-473}} “He should then assume the form of the angry Heruka Adorned with four arms, Meaning that he is the nature of the four joys And is purified of the four Māras. {2.3.29}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-474}} “Standing in the previously described maṇḍala circle, He has transformed from the seed syllable hūṁ. In his left hand there is a skull cup Filled with the blood of gods and demigods. {2.3.30}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-475}} “In his right hand he holds a flame-like vajra scepter, Frightening even fear itself. With his other two arms he is embracing the consort (prajñā), Who, for her part, is embracing him. {2.3.31}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-476}} “He should visualize her form As the Blessed Vajravārāhī. {2.3.32}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-477}} “First, he should meditate on emptiness. Then, on the pericarp {{note:{index:98,id:UT22084-079-008-478}}} of a lotus He should visualize a full moon disk, And in the center of this moon disk, the syllable hūṁ . {2.3.33} {{page:{number:32,folio:F.89.a}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-479}} “He should visualize the form of the deity With three faces and six arms. The first {{note:{index:99,id:UT22084-079-008-480}}} face is black, The right one is white and peaceful, {2.3.34}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-481}} “And the left one is red in color. The lord has three eyes that are sublime in appearance. He is replete with all the adornments, And stands on a skull cup platform. {2.3.35}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-482}} “In his hands he is holding a skull cup Filled with excrement, urine, semen, and blood; A bow and arrow; A vajra scepter; and a bell. {2.3.36}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-483}} “The first right hand has a blazing vajra scepter, And the third, a trident. The glorious one is embraced by his consort (prajñā) And adorned by a knot of matted hair. {2.3.37}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-484}} “He should repeatedly radiate blazing light With scintillating clouds composed of buddhas. {{note:{index:100,id:UT22084-079-008-485}}} The practitioner should then visualize Himself in the center of a bhaga. {2.3.38}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-486}} “Then he should visualize the consort (mudrā) As united with the main deity. {{note:{index:101,id:UT22084-079-008-487}}} On the lotus petals, he should draw the goddesses Standing on skull cup platforms. {2.3.39}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-488}} “Their forms, of different colors, are pleasing to the mind And they each have one face and four arms. First, {{note:{index:102,id:UT22084-079-008-489}}} he should draw the beautiful consort (vidyā) Who holds an arrow and bow, {2.3.40}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-490}} “A skull cup filled with semen, And a goad. Second, he should draw the goddess who has in her hands a spear, {{note:{index:103,id:UT22084-079-008-491}}} A skull cup filled with blood, {2.3.41}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-492}} “A vajra scepter, and a noose. He should draw her on the southern petal. {{note:{index:104,id:UT22084-079-008-493}}} Third, on the northern petal, {{note:{index:105,id:UT22084-079-008-494}}} he should draw The goddess who has in her hands a sword, {2.3.42}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-495}} “A skull cup filled with water, A vajra scepter, and a bell. He should draw the fourth goddess On the western petal. {{note:{index:106,id:UT22084-079-008-496}}} {2.3.43}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-497}} “In her left hands she is holding A khaṭvāṅga and a skull cup, And in her right hands A ‘flame thrower’ and a triple banner. {2.3.44}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-498}} “The fifth goddess has a staff {{note:{index:107,id:UT22084-079-008-499}}} in her hand And holds a skull cup with another. She also holds a lotus and a ḍamaru. He should draw her in the northeastern quarter. {{note:{index:108,id:UT22084-079-008-500}}} {2.3.45}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-501}} “In the northwestern corner he should draw {{note:{index:109,id:UT22084-079-008-502}}} The sixth goddess with a lotus in her hand. She also holds a skull cup filled with fat, A mirror, and an axe. {2.3.46}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-503}} “The seventh goddess has a lance in her hand. She also holds a conch shell, a discus weapon, And a skull cup filled with blood. He should draw her in the southwestern quarter. {{note:{index:110,id:UT22084-079-008-504}}} {2.3.47}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-505}} “The eighth goddess he should draw In the southeastern quarter. {{note:{index:111,id:UT22084-079-008-506}}} She is holding in her hands A pitcher, a vajra scepter, a bell, {2.3.48}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-507}} “And a skull cup filled with substances, Covered with human skin. {{page:{number:33,folio:F.89.b}}} He should draw these goddesses on the petals And the lord Mahāsukha on the pericarp. {2.3.49}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-508}} “He should draw, in the secret maṇḍala, Various musical instruments. He should draw the gate keepers— A goddess holding a goad, {2.3.50}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-509}} “And likewise, one with a vajra noose, a chain, And a vajra bell. He should visualize himself in the center of a vulva, And later begin mantra recitation. {2.3.51}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-510}} “ Hūṁ pertains to Vajrasattva; Oṁ is distinctiveness of tone; Aḥ , which is of the color of pure crystal, Is perfectly endowed with speech. {2.3.52}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-511}} “He should add the syllable hrīḥ And also the word svāhā. This mantra has been taught as the one to recite, But, during meditation, it should consist of a single syllable. {{note:{index:112,id:UT22084-079-008-512}}} {2.3.53}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-513}} “The syllable hrīḥ of the goddesses Should then be placed on the petals. It should be joined with the four seed syllables That are the nature of the four types of offerings. {2.3.54}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-514}} “It should be joined with the first sound ( oṁ ), and so forth, And placed on the female gatekeepers all around. Then the practitioner should insert His vajra into the bhaga. {2.3.55}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-516}} “He should, at that point, utter the syllable hūṁ, And also the syllable hrīḥ. He should orally ingest the semen, Mixing it with the blood, when the woman is menstruating. {2.3.56}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-517}} “He should make offerings of flowers and fragrances To himself and also to the bhaga. At this point he should recite the mantra If he wants to attain siddhi. {2.3.57}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-518}} “There is Vajraraudrī And also Vajrabimbā. Vajrarāgī is the third And Vajrasaumyā the fourth. {2.3.58}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-519}} “The fifth is Vajrayakṣī And the sixth Vajraḍākinī. The seventh is Śabdavajrā And Pṛthvīvajrā is the eighth.” {2.3.59}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-520}} Here concludes the third part of the second chapter.
Part 4
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-521}} “Listen well, Vajragarbha, about the preparation Of magical circles and their specifications, as required for Pacifying, enriching, enthralling, and so forth, And also protecting and assaulting. {2.4.1}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-522}} “The wise practitioner should have someone Draw the outline of a wheel, with nine divisions {{note:{index:113,id:UT22084-079-008-523}}} and the rest, And visualize the colors, and so forth, As required for individual rituals involving the circle. {2.4.2}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-524}} “ Oṁ tāre tuttāre ture svāhā . {2.4.3} {{page:{number:34,folio:F.90.a}}}
“The seed syllables of this mantra are all-purpose— The first ( oṁ ) and the last ( svāhā ) are for homage and homa respectively. The target’s name should be included in the middle, Along with the phrase “please protect.” {{note:{index:114,id:UT22084-079-008-526}}} {2.4.4}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-527}} “He should fashion his form From emptiness, by means of the wisdom of equality, And position it within the protective circle, The place of knowing everything as equal. {2.4.5}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-528}} “He should meditate that protection is provided By wisdom beings, so that all dangers are kept at a distance. Accepting the non-reality of sentient beings, He should cultivate the state of deity yoga. {2.4.6}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-529}} “In the center of a moon disk He should visualize a lotus throne And imagine there his own body As the goddess Tārā, who grants all siddhis. {2.4.7}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-530}} “He should visualize the following letters:
“On his head, oṁ tāre svāhā. On the eyes, oṁ tuttāre {{note:{index:115,id:UT22084-079-008-532}}} svāhā. On the nose, oṁ ture {{note:{index:116,id:UT22084-079-008-533}}} svāhā. On the ears, oṁ tu svāhā. On the tongue, oṁ re svāhā. On the chest, oṁ tāriṇi svāhā . {2.4.8}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-534}} “He should always wear this sixfold protection And visualize himself as noble Tārā, With two arms, sitting in the sattvaparyaṅka posture, And adorned with all kinds of jewelry. {2.4.9}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-535}} “Her right hand grants fearlessness to all; Her left one holds a lotus. Among all the deities, he should propitiate The one who is roused by the following king of mantras: {2.4.10}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-536}} “ Oṁ kurukulle hrīḥ svāhā.
“This mantra accomplishes everything. {2.4.11}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-538}} “It protects from being bound by enemies and kings, From poisons dreadful in their ways. It arrests various fevers afflicting the body And removes untimely death due to toxins and so forth. {2.4.12}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-539}} “Wherever there is fear, He should employ this mantra. A dull-witted {{note:{index:117,id:UT22084-079-008-540}}} person will become intelligent. He should write it down and wear it for protection. {2.4.13}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-541}} “This sublime protection Vanquishes every threat. It protects everyone; It is the unsurpassable essence of deity yoga. {2.4.14}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-542}} “He should visualize a sun disk With blazing light rays, And at its center the syllable hrīḥ, Shining with red light. {2.4.15}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-543}} “Then, he should visualize himself In Kurukullā’s form, with one face and four arms, Holding in one pair of her hands an arrow and a bow, And in the other pair, a lotus and a goad. {2.4.16} {{page:{number:35,folio:F.90.b}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-544}} “By merely meditating on this One can enthrall the threefold universe— Kings with one hundred thousand repetitions of the mantra; Ordinary people with ten thousand; {2.4.17}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-545}} “Animals, yakṣas, and so forth with ten million repetitions; Demigods with seven hundred thousand; Gods with two hundred thousand; And followers of Mantra with one hundred. {2.4.18}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-546}} “This yantra-wheel {{note:{index:118,id:UT22084-079-008-547}}} has eight spokes, Is white, and has a beautiful glow. Visualizing it as having the nature of equality, And being in essence the threefold universe, {2.4.19}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-548}} “He should form himself as previously explained With the aforementioned characteristics, And then visualize [Prajñāpāramitā’s] yantra-wheel In the rituals for making wisdom blaze forth. {2.4.20}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-549}} “He should recite, Oṁ prajñe mahāprajñe hūṁ svāhā. {{note:{index:119,id:UT22084-079-008-550}}} {2.4.21}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-551}} “He should visualize himself by means of merging with the essence As Prajñāpāramitā, the very nature of wisdom made manifest, Sitting in the center of a moon disk, And blazing with a profusion of light. {2.4.22}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-552}} “She has two arms and sits in the sattvaparyaṅka posture. Adorned with all kinds of jewelry, Sublime with white radiance, She should be construed as the very nature of wisdom. {2.4.23}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-553}} “When this mantra is recited By those who are dull, or of inferior intellect, Their wisdom will grow like the branch of a tree Through their applying this method for increasing it. {2.4.24}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-554}} “In the center of a moon disk He should place the seed syllable of Vairocana. This syllable changes into the lord with one face and four arms, Sitting in the center of a throne of human skulls. {2.4.25}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-555}} “Of gentle disposition, he holds a wheel, a bell, A human skull, and a noose. He radiates bursts of light all around And is surrounded by a halo of flames. {2.4.26}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-556}} “Following the same procedure, He should visualize Ratnasambhava— Radiant yellow, Resembling molten gold, {2.4.27}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-557}} “Sitting in the center of a throne of human skulls, With one face and four arms, Of heroic disposition, and holding a jewel, a goad, A human skull, and a noose. {2.4.28}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-558}} “Following the same procedure, {{page:{number:36,folio:F.91.a}}} he should visualize The vajra holder of the lotus family (Amitābha), With one face and four arms, Shining like ruby, {2.4.29}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-559}} “Holding a bow and arrow, of heroic disposition, Sitting on a throne of human skulls. Holding in his other pair of hands a lotus and a noose, He is adorned with all kinds of jewelry. {2.4.30}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-560}} “Following the same procedure, he should visualize Amoghasiddhi, a sword in his hand, Sitting in the center of a throne of human skulls, With one face and four arms, {2.4.31}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-561}} “Holding a human skull and a vajra bell, And brandishing a goad in one of his right hands. He is the color of green beryl And adorned with all kinds of jewelry. {2.4.32}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-562}} “In the middle of the expanse of the sky, He should visualize a moon disk. At its center, is the seed syllable bhrūṁ {{note:{index:120,id:UT22084-079-008-563}}} Which changes into the form of Locanā. {2.4.33}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-564}} “Sitting on a throne of human skulls, She is adorned with eight arms And holds in her hands a wheel, A bow and arrow, a vajra scepter, a bell, {2.4.34}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-565}} “A noose, a sword, and a human skull. She has one face and three eyes, And is fully adorned with all kinds of jewelry, Necklaces, and anklets. {2.4.35}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-566}} “She is white and very beautiful, And she is wearing a crown of human skulls. Next he should visualize, in the middle Of the expanse of the sky, a full moon disk. {2.4.36}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-567}} “At its center there is the syllable hūṁ, Which changes into the form of Māmakī, Radiant blue in color, Sitting in the center of a throne of human skulls. {2.4.37}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-568}} “She has three eyes, one face, And is adorned with a garland of human skulls. She holds a bow, an arrow, A goad, a sword, {2.4.38}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-569}} “A noose, a scepter, A bell, a human skull, A wheel, a jewel, a lotus, and a khaṭvāṅga— Twelve articles for her twelve hands. {2.4.39}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-570}} “Next he should draw a secret maṇḍala Adorned with all embellishments. In the center of the bhaga, He should visualize a full moon disk. {2.4.40}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-571}} “There he should visualize the syllable hrīḥ, And generate from it the goddess called Pāṇḍarā. She is sitting on a throne of human skulls {{page:{number:37,folio:F.91.b}}} And blazes forth bright red light. {2.4.41}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-572}} “Replete with all adornments, She is adorned with eight hands, In which she is holding a bow, An arrow, a lotus, a sword, {2.4.42}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-573}} “A skull cup, a vajra scepter, a bell, A noose, and a jewel. She is adorned with all kinds of jewelry, And makes a jingling sound with her necklaces and anklets. {2.4.43}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-574}} “If the practitioner visualizes her as such, He will swiftly attain the state of awakening. Next he should visualize, in the sky above, The disk of a full moon. {2.4.44}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-575}} “At its center there is the syllable tāṁ, Which changes into the form of Tārā, Adorned with eight arms, Sitting on a throne of human skulls. {2.4.45}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-576}} “Impassioned, she holds in her hands a sword, A lotus, a goad, A skull cup filled with blood, A noose, a wheel, {2.4.46}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-577}} “A bow, and an arrow. He should visualize {{note:{index:121,id:UT22084-079-008-578}}} her with one face, Of green color, with three eyes, And adorned with all kinds of jewelry. {2.4.47}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-579}} “If the practitioner meditates in this way, He will become equal to Vajrasattva.” {2.4.48}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-580}} This concludes the sovereign second chapter of the glorious “ Emergence from Sampuṭa ,” so called to reflect the secret foundation of all tantras.
Chapter 3
Part 1
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-581}} “Listen about the practice, as it really is, Of generating Nairātmyā and Heruka, One through which all wicked And violent beings will be tamed. {{note:{index:122,id:UT22084-079-008-582}}} {3.1.1}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-583}} “The transformations effected by the ḍāka {{note:{index:123,id:UT22084-079-008-584}}} and ḍākinīs— All of them I will explain to you. The vajra-holding Heruka, in his identity of Vajrasattva, Will bring on the vajra-like state. {3.1.2}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-585}} “One should assume a wild form in a raging ring of flames; It should be radiating all around. One should next visualize a garland of seed syllables In the center of a moon disk. {3.1.3}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-586}} “Then the vajra-holding Heruka, out of great passion, Melts down along with his consort (vidyā). Subsequently, the vidyās of the retinue exhort him, By offering various songs, to rise again. {3.1.4}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-587}} “Pukkasī:
“ ‘Arise, O lord! You are the essence of compassion! {{note:{index:124,id:UT22084-079-008-589}}} Please save me, Pukkasī. Abandon your void nature! Take me in union, O Great Bliss!’ {3.1.5} {{page:{number:38,folio:F.92.a}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-590}} “Śavarī:
“ ‘Without you I would die. Arise, Hevajra! Abandon the state of the empty nature! Fulfill the desires of Śavarī!’ {3.1.6}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-592}} Caṇḍālī:
“ ‘Invite the world, O lord of pleasure! Why do you remain in the void? I, Caṇḍālī, beseech you. Without you I have no direction.’ {3.1.7}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-594}} Ḍombī:
“ ‘Arise, O magician! May I know your mind! Since I, Ḍombī, am swooning, Do not interrupt your compassion!’ {3.1.8}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-596}} “The great Heruka arises then, in a fluid form, From the syllables aṁ and hūṁ, {{note:{index:125,id:UT22084-079-008-597}}} Spreading his feet on the ground And threatening the gods and demigods. {3.1.9}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-598}} “From the syllables of the lord’s pleasure consort {dga’ ma}— Hūṁ and aṁ {{note:{index:126,id:UT22084-079-008-599}}} —in a frightful blaze of blue, One should generate the goddesses of the retinue From their seed syllables gaṁ, caṁ, vaṁ, ghaṁ, puṁ, {{note:{index:127,id:UT22084-079-008-600}}} śaṁ, laṁ , and ḍaṁ . {3.1.10}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-601}} “In this circle of mothers, the blissful abode, One should visualize the lord as follows: He has eight faces, four legs, And is adorned with sixteen arms. {3.1.11}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-602}} “Standing astride the four Māras, And frightening even fear itself, He expresses the moods of sensuality, heroism, Disgust, fury, mirth, terror, {3.1.12}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-603}} “Compassion, wonder, and peace— The nine moods of dramaturgy. Wearing a skull-garland necklace, He stands on a sun disk and performs his wild tāṇḍava dance. {3.1.13}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-604}} “Black and frightening, He has a double vajra scepter fastened to the crown of his head. He emits the syllable hūṁ from his mouth And his body is smeared with ashes. {3.1.14}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-605}} “Joined with Nairātmyā, He is engaged in pleasurable union. Motionless, he is attaining bliss; {{note:{index:128,id:UT22084-079-008-606}}} Motionless, he dwells in his own nature. {3.1.15}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-607}} “His main face is black and smiling. His right one is the color of a jasmine blossom. His left face is red and very frightening, And his top face is terrifying with its bared fangs. {3.1.16}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-608}} “He has twenty-four eyes altogether, And his remaining faces are the color of bees. {{note:{index:129,id:UT22084-079-008-609}}} In his right hands he holds a vajra scepter, a sword, An arrow, a wheel, {3.1.17}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-610}} “A goblet, a staff, A trident, and {{page:{number:39,folio:F.92.b}}} a goad. In his left hands he has a bell and a lotus, And brandishes a bow and a khaṭvāṅga. {3.1.18}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-611}} “He also holds a skull cup, a jewel, And a noose, and displays a threatening gesture. He is surrounded by clouds of buddhas, Radiating different colored lights all around. {3.1.19}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-612}} “In this way, one should then follow the routine Of visualizing Gaurī, and so forth.
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-613}} “Gaurī is white in color and is engaged {{note:{index:130,id:UT22084-079-008-614}}} In the act of drawing a bow and arrow. Her other implements are a skull cup full of blood And a knife with a vajra handle. {3.1.20}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-615}} “Caurī is red in color, And is known to hold a wheel, a goad, A skull cup, and a ḍamaru drum. One should visualize her as divinely beautiful. {3.1.21}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-616}} “Pramohā is black in color. She holds a skull cup, a goblet, A ploughshare for turning up the earth, And in her right hand she brandishes a trident. {3.1.22}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-617}} “Vetalī is light yellow in color, With wine and water in two of her hands, And a sword and a skull cup in her other hands. One should visualize her with an alluring form. {3.1.23}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-618}} “Pukkasī is yellow in color. She holds a tendril of the wish-fulfilling tree, A skull bowl filled with meat, and a jewel. She displays a boon-granting mudrā. {3.1.24}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-619}} “Caṇḍālī is blue in color And holds a wind-cloth. {{note:{index:131,id:UT22084-079-008-620}}} In her other two hands she holds A skull cup and a white lotus. {{note:{index:132,id:UT22084-079-008-621}}} {3.1.25}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-622}} “Ghasmarī is yellowish green in color. She holds a vajra-fire pit and an axe in two of her hands, Has a skull cup filled with fat in her other left hand, And displays a gesture of granting fearlessness with her other right hand. {3.1.26}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-623}} “Śavarī is white in color, With a khaṭvāṅga, a skull cup, A vajra scepter, and a noose. One should visualize [these goddesses’] forms in all their diversity. {3.1.27}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-624}} “They each have a creature: Gaurī, a rohita fish; Caurī, a wild boar; Pramohā, a tortoise; Vetalī, a snake; Pukkasī, a lion; Caṇḍālī, a tiger; Ghasmarī, a jackal; and Śavarī, a bear. {{note:{index:133,id:UT22084-079-008-625}}} {3.1.28}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-626}} “They are in the eight skull cups, respectively, Of Gaurī, and so forth, in the right order. These goddesses are adorned with all kinds of jewelry And express the moods of sensuality, and so forth. {3.1.29} {{page:{number:40,folio:F.93.a}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-627}} “There are also the following goddesses: The horse-faced, the pig-faced, the dog-faced, and the lion-faced. All have four arms and four faces, And are adorned with serpent jewelry. {3.1.30}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-628}} “Also present are Vaṃśā, the flute goddess, Vīṇā, the lute goddess, Mukundā, the kettle-drum goddess, and Murajā, the tambourine goddess. They each have two arms, one face, And are adorned with all types of jewelry. {3.1.31}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-629}} “The faces—main, right, left—of the horse-faced goddess Are, respectively, black, white, and yellow, with the upper face being green. Those of the pig-faced goddess are—in the same order— Yellow, black, and white, with the upper face being red. {3.1.32}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-630}} “The faces of the dog-faced goddess Are red, black, and white, with the upper face being yellow. Those of the lion-faced goddess Are green, black, and white, with the upper face being the color of flames. {3.1.33}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-631}} “Each of the goddesses has blazing, upward-flowing hair And stands astride a corpse, her left leg extended and her right slightly bent. They all have three eyes and are to be visualized With faces expressing the moods of anger, sensuality, and mirth.” {3.1.34}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-632}} This concludes the first part of the third chapter, on generating Heruka.
Part 2
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-633}} “Listen, Vajragarbha, O powerful king, About the practice of Jñānaḍākinī, Which is for those who abandon dualistic notions And gain the wisdom of phenomena as nondual. {3.2.1}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-634}} “One should recite the following formula of purification At the beginning of every practice three times:
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-635}} “All phenomena are pure by nature; I am pure by nature. All phenomena have the pure nature of vajra; I have the pure nature of vajra. All phenomena have the pure nature of the union; I have the pure nature of the union. {{note:{index:134,id:UT22084-079-008-636}}} {{note:{index:135,id:UT22084-079-008-637}}} {3.2.2}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-638}} “Having thus recited, the practitioner Should meditate on the same. He should then commence the meditation proper In a place pleasing to the mind. {3.2.3}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-639}} “He should spread out a canopy, Hang fabrics of various colors from it, And hoist up streamers and banners. All around, throughout the ten directions, {3.2.4}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-640}} “He should strew various perfumes and flowers, And then form a maṇḍala of scented powders. There, through an instantaneous transformation, He should visualize his own form as the deity. {3.2.5}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-641}} “Thus visualizing himself as Jñānaḍākinī, The wise practitioner should first worship her with offerings. {{page:{number:41,folio:F.93.b}}} He should accordingly generate, According to proper procedure, an ocean of wisdom. {3.2.6}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-642}} “He should then visualize Mount Meru, With the four directions surrounding its peak having four different colors. Atop the peak is a golden palace, Bright and colorful with the seven types of jewels. {3.2.7}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-643}} “Around it are garlands of wind chime bells, Spread all around as desired. He should also visualize a lion throne In each of the five places. {3.2.8}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-644}} “Then, visualizing a sun disk Adorned with a white parasol, He should, with the exhalation of his breath, Project Jñānaḍākinī into its center. {3.2.9}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-645}} “She has three faces and six arms, And sits in the sattvaparyaṅka posture. She is adorned with loose, disheveled hair And the five buddhas atop her head. {3.2.10}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-646}} “Blue in color, and with a terrifying form, She is bedecked with adornments made of snakes. Expressing the moods of mirth, anger, and sensuality, She has three eyes, and is divinely beautiful. {3.2.11}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-647}} “She is laughing loudly, baring her fangs, And beautiful in her red apparel. She holds up a khaṭvāṅga, And in her second hand, an axe. {3.2.12}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-648}} “In her third hand she has a vajra scepter. In her first left hand, she has a bell; In her second left hand, an alms bowl; And in her third, she holds a sword. {3.2.13}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-649}} “The wise practitioner should visualize her in the middle, Radiating manifold rays of light. To the east of Jñānaḍākinī, he should project, With his outgoing breath, Vajraḍākinī. {3.2.14}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-650}} “She is white and exquisite, Adorned with loose, disheveled hair, Bedecked with adornments made of snakes, And expressing the mood of sensuality. {3.2.15}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-651}} “She is bedecked with exquisite garments And adorned with two arms. He should visualize Vajraḍākinī Carrying a khaṭvāṅga and a yogic alms bowl. {3.2.16}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-652}} “To the north of Jñānaḍākinī, projected with his outgoing breath, He should visualize Ghoraḍākinī, With two arms, sitting in the sattvaparyaṅka posture, Resplendent with the color of molten gold. {3.2.17}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-653}} “She carries a khaṭvāṅga and a yogic alms bowl, {{page:{number:42,folio:F.94.a}}} Is adorned with loose, disheveled hair, And her limbs are adorned with ornaments made of snakes. Her figure is bedecked with exquisite garments.
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-654}} “Thus should he visualize The goddess called Ghoraḍākinī. {3.2.18}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-655}} “To the west of Jñānaḍākinī He should project Vetalī. Again, {{note:{index:136,id:UT22084-079-008-656}}} she has two arms and sits in the sattvaparyaṅka posture. She is blue in color and exquisite. {3.2.19}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-657}} “She holds a khaṭvāṅga and a yogic bowl, And is adorned with loose, disheveled hair. Snakes form her body ornaments, And exquisite clothes embellish her figure. {3.2.20}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-658}} “To the south of Jñānaḍākinī He should project the red Caṇḍālī, Who holds a khaṭvāṅga and a yogic bowl, And is adorned with loose, disheveled hair. {3.2.21}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-659}} “She has two arms, one face, And is adorned with different ornaments. The practitioner should thus visualize this pentad of goddesses, Himself endowed with perfect beauty and form. {3.2.22}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-660}} “In the northeast he should visualize The goddess Siṃhinī with the face of a lion. She is white and yellow, and stands with her right leg outstretched And the left slightly bent, on a pedestal fashioned from the lord of nāgas. {3.2.23}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-661}} “She holds a vajra goad {{note:{index:137,id:UT22084-079-008-662}}} and, in her other hand, a noose in a threatening gesture. She is nicely attired in exquisite garments. He should visualize her body radiating With a manifold blaze of light rays. {3.2.24}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-663}} “In the southeast there is the goddess called Vyāghrī On a supreme throne made of seven types of jewels. She has two arms, is blue and white in color, And is beautifully attired and adorned with jewelry. {3.2.25}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-664}} “She holds a blazing vajra goad and a noose, While forming a threatening gesture with her fingers. He should visualize her body radiant With a manifold blaze of light rays. {3.2.26}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-665}} “In the southwest there is the goddess Jambukī, Laughing loudly and inspiring fear. She is mounted on a buffalo. Her body is red and black in color. {3.2.27}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-666}} “Her body is attired with exquisite garments And she has two arms. Her implements are a noose held with a threatening gesture and a goad. She is adorned with ornaments made of snakes. {3.2.28}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-667}} “In the northwest there is the goddess Ulūkā, Yellow and red in color. She sits on a snake throne And snakes, too, should be visualized as her ornaments. {3.2.29}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-668}} “She has two arms and sits in the sattvaparyaṅka posture. {{page:{number:43,folio:F.94.b}}} Her implements are a goad and a noose held with a threatening gesture. One should visualize her body radiant With a manifold blaze of light rays. {3.2.30}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-669}} “There are eight ḍākinīs in the center And four on the outside. Having visualized in this way the order of their distribution, He should subsequently assign each one a place. {3.2.31}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-670}} “The royal goddess in the east, Ḍākinī, Has two arms and is white in color. She sits on a corpse {{note:{index:138,id:UT22084-079-008-671}}} And is adorned with snakes as ornaments. {3.2.32}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-672}} “She is wild, with disheveled hair, And her splendor is like that of a blazing fire. Radiant, she raises her hands To her mouth, laughing loudly. {3.2.33}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-673}} “In the north there is the royal goddess Dīpinī, Wild, and yellow in color. Frightening in form and baring her teeth, She is attired in exquisite garments. {3.2.34}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-674}} “She sits on a corpse; Her splendor is like that of a blazing fire. Her two hands are folded together at her forehead, Resembling the flame of a lamp. {3.2.35}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-675}} “In the west there is the goddess Cūṣiṇī, Red in color and inspiring fear. She sits on a corpse, Attired in exquisite garments. {3.2.36}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-676}} “From her cupped hands she drinks blood, Trickling in the form of a red thread. Fierce and with the splendor of a blazing fire, Cūṣiṇī is indeed a powerful deity. {3.2.37}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-677}} “In the south there is the goddess called Kambojī, Shiny black in color. She sits on a corpse, Adorned with disheveled hair. {3.2.38}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-678}} “She looks resplendent in her red clothes And is adorned with ornaments of snakes. In her hands she holds a javelin and displays a threatening gesture. She makes everyone’s mind free from delusion. {3.2.39}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-679}} “The all-knowing practitioner should always visualize Each of them as wild and radiating like a blazing fire. In front of these forms and images, The pledge substances should be displayed accordingly. {{note:{index:139,id:UT22084-079-008-680}}} {3.2.40}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-681}} “Taking the seventh syllable from the syllable of wind and the seventh from fire, He should impel the latter seventh with the seed syllable of Vajrī. This should be crowned by the anunāsika and supported by the sound ū. This combination is known as the torrent of ambrosia.” {{note:{index:140,id:UT22084-079-008-682}}} {3.2.41}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-683}} This concludes the second part of the third chapter. {{page:{number:44,folio:F.95.a}}}
Part 3
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-684}} “Now I will teach the practice of Nairātmyā, Briefly, as has been taught. In the middle of space One should visualize a sun disk, {3.3.1}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-685}} “Then the maṇḍala with its arrangement of elements In the order of the appearance of the deities. Before the maṇḍala comes earth and water, And then fire, in their due order. {3.3.2}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-686}} “Then comes the great wind, and the symbols, Which correspond to the order of the appearance of the deities. {{note:{index:141,id:UT22084-079-008-687}}} The maṇḍala, which arises out of the dharmodaya, Has two pure and perfect overlapping areas: {3.3.3}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-688}} “One is formed by the circle of lotus filaments, And the other is the supreme three bodies of the vajra holder. One should visualize a corpse there, Which is the seat for each of the fifteen goddesses. {3.3.4}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-689}} “Above it there is a moon disk, And above the moon disk is the seed syllable; Resting upon that is a sun disk. From the meeting of these two disks comes great bliss. {3.3.5}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-690}} “The moon is then transformed into the vowels And the sun into the consonants. The meeting of the sun and the moon Is also known to be Gaurī and the other goddesses. {3.3.6}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-691}} “The moon represents mirror-like wisdom, And the sun, the wisdom of equality. The symbols of the chosen deity along with their seed syllables Are said to be discriminating wisdom. {3.3.7}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-692}} “The unity of all of these is action-accomplishing wisdom, Which corresponds to the purity of the deity’s full form. The wise practitioner should cultivate these five aspects According to the sequence just described. {3.3.8}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-693}} “The union of the vowels and consonants Constitutes the seat of Vajrasattva. Since the deity embryo arises from a letter, {{note:{index:142,id:UT22084-079-008-694}}} The syllables hūṁ and phaṭ are not necessary. {3.3.9}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-695}} “He should visualize the chief deity of the maṇḍala As arising from the syllable, which is the reflection of its essence. With their faces, attributes, and so forth, as before, With the radiance of the moon-stone gem, {3.3.10}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-696}} “All the goddesses manifest in full From the nature of skillful means and wisdom. The vowels are wisdom and the consonants, means, Reflecting the distinction between the moon and sun. {3.3.11}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-697}} “Since Gaurī and the others should appear one by one, {{note:{index:143,id:UT22084-079-008-698}}} Following the division of the colors, He should make every effort To correctly execute the maṇḍala procedure. {3.3.12} {{page:{number:45,folio:F.95.b}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-699}} “The following five yoginīs are positioned Within the inner enclosure; The yoga adept should always conceive them to be, In their natures, the five aggregates: {3.3.13}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-700}} “Vajrā is in the east; Gaurī is in the south; Vāriyoginī is in the west; Vajraḍākinī is in the north; And the yoginī Nairātmyā is in the center. {3.3.14}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-701}} “Within the outer circle there are the following:
“Gaurī, Caurī, and Vetalī; So too, Ghasmarī and Pukkasī. Further, there are Śavarī and Caṇḍālī, With Ḍombī completing the octet. {3.3.15}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-703}} “Down below and up above are known to be, Respectively, Bhūcarī and Khecarī— The first, moving, the other, stationary. They have the nature of saṃsāra and nirvāṇa respectively. {3.3.16}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-704}} “All these goddesses can be described as follows:
“They are different colors, very wild, And adorned with the five mudrās. They have one face, four arms, Three eyes, and are divinely beautiful. {3.3.17}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-706}} “They each wear a choker, earrings, A wrist bracelet, and a waist chain. They are adorned with the five buddhas, Which constitute their five pure seals. {3.3.18}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-707}} “Each of them is said to look Like the yoginī Nairātmyā, Who, on her left side, holds a yogic alms bowl And an upward-pointing khaṭvāṅga. {3.3.19}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-708}} “On her right side she holds a blue vajra scepter And a flaying knife. She stands on a corpse, ablaze with flames, With red eyes and yellow, upward-flowing hair. {3.3.20}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-709}} “She is blue, brilliantly luminous, And her hips are wrapped with a tiger skin. She sits there in her divine beauty, Glowing like the fire during the final destruction. {{note:{index:144,id:UT22084-079-008-710}}} {3.3.21}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-711}} “To her right there is a yellow and blue {{note:{index:145,id:UT22084-079-008-712}}} goddess, Khecarī; To her left there is a red and blue one, Bhūcarī. {{note:{index:146,id:UT22084-079-008-713}}} They each have two arms, a single face, And are adorned with all types of jewelry. {3.3.22}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-714}} “They all extend forward their left hands, which hold skull cups, And hold in their right hands flaying knives. They express the moods of mirth, anger, and sensuality, {{note:{index:147,id:UT22084-079-008-715}}} Abiding in the nature of reverence for him. {{note:{index:148,id:UT22084-079-008-716}}} {3.3.23}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-717}} “The wise practitioner should visualize himself in the center As the identity of the natures of the three tattvas, Radiating all around light of different colors, Composed of scintillating clouds of buddhas.” {3.3.24}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-718}} This concludes the third part of the third chapter. {{page:{number:46,folio:F.96.a}}}
Part 4
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-719}} “Now I will teach The supreme great maṇḍala, Which has the form of the vajradhātu And is known as the vajradhātu itself. {3.4.1}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-720}} “One should purify the maṇḍala site, Making it into a place of the great seal. The follower of Mantra should execute the following, Watching over every detail: {3.4.2}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-721}} “The wise practitioner should delimit the maṇḍala, To the best of his ability, using a thread That is new, well woven, Of the right length, and beautiful. {3.4.3}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-722}} “The maṇḍala should have four corners and four doors, And be finely adorned with porticos. It should be provided with four threads {{note:{index:149,id:UT22084-079-008-723}}} And adorned with fine fabrics and flower garlands {3.4.4}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-724}} “On all its sides, Which are provided with gate-turrets, He should delimit the outer maṇḍala With lines of jewel-studded vajra scepters. {3.4.5}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-725}} “He should then enter the inner court, Which has the shape of a circle; {{note:{index:150,id:UT22084-079-008-726}}} It is strewn with vajra threads And adorned with eight pillars. {3.4.6}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-727}} “It is adorned with five circles Situated atop the vajra pillars. {{note:{index:151,id:UT22084-079-008-728}}} Then, in the center of the maṇḍala, He should place an image of the Buddha. {3.4.7}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-729}} “Now I will explain to you the practice Connected with the maṇḍala procedure just described.
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-730}} “Starting precisely from there, the follower of Mantra should enter this dwelling of the deity and visualize a moon disk transformed from the letter a . Above the disk, he should visualize a white, five-pointed vajra scepter, according to procedure. Having then made offerings to all the tathāgatas, and so forth, he should prostrate himself, and say the following: {3.4.8}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-731}} “ ‘May all buddhas and bodhisattvas please keep me in their heart! From now until I sit on the throne of liberation, I, named such and such,
“ ‘Give rise to the altruistic aspiration set on awakening— Supreme and unsurpassable— Just as the buddhas of the three times Made their firm resolve to attain perfect awakening. {3.4.9} {{page:{number:47,folio:F.96.b}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-733}} “ ‘I will firmly observe each of the three kinds of bodhisattva ethics: The training in ethical discipline, The gathering of wholesome qualities, And the ethics of acting for the benefit of beings. {3.4.10}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-734}} “ ‘From now onward I will firmly uphold The vow, {{note:{index:152,id:UT22084-079-008-735}}} born from the union with the buddhas, Of Buddha, Dharma, and Saṃgha, The three foremost and unsurpassable jewels. {3.4.11}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-736}} “ ‘Within the fold of the great vajra family, I will firmly uphold the vajra, bell, and hand gestures According to their true nature. I will commit myself to the master. {3.4.12}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-737}} “ ‘Within the great jewel family, as is fitting, I shall bounteously give the four kinds of gifts, Performing this six times each day As my delightful samaya. {3.4.13}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-738}} “ ‘Within the great pure lotus family, Which emerges from great awakening, I shall uphold the true Dharma— The exoteric and esoteric dimensions pertaining to the three vehicles. {3.4.14}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-739}} “ ‘Within the fold of the great activity family I shall uphold, in every respect, The all-encompassing vow And perform the act of worship to the best of my ability. {3.4.15}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-740}} “ ‘Now that I have given rise to the altruistic aspiration set on awakening— Supreme and unsurpassable— And taken all the vows For fulfilling the needs of all beings, {3.4.16}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-741}} “ ‘I shall ferry across those that have not yet crossed, I shall liberate those that have not been liberated, And I shall give comfort to the desolate, Establishing all beings in nirvāṇa.’ ” {3.4.17}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-742}} Then the lord entered the meditative absorption called “that which arises from the pinnacle of all vajra holders” and gave this inspiring teaching: {3.4.18}
“Now, staying in a place suitable for meditation, he should observe the absence of intrinsic identity in all phenomena. Everything of an external and internal nature is imputed by mind. There is nothing else that exists beyond mind. Since all phenomena, being luminous, have never arisen in the first place, he should mentally declare them to be unproduced. Then he {{page:{number:48,folio:F.97.a}}} should perceive his own mind, which is luminous by nature, in the form of a moon disk, while reciting the following mantra with enthusiasm: {{note:{index:153,id:UT22084-079-008-744}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-745}} “ ‘ Oṁ , I penetrate my mind.’ {{note:{index:154,id:UT22084-079-008-746}}} {3.4.19}
“This mind is like the sky— Stainless despite the presence of clouds. {{note:{index:155,id:UT22084-079-008-748}}} It is free from all dejection, {{note:{index:156,id:UT22084-079-008-749}}} Being utterly devoid of mental constructs. {3.4.20}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-750}} “First it is visualized as the moon, Cleansed of all the dirt of afflictions. Therein enter all the qualities of the awakened ones In the form of the short letter a , and so forth: {3.4.21}
“ a ā i ī u ū ṛ ṝ ḷ ḹ e ai o au aṃ aḥ .” {3.4.22}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-752}} Vajragarbha then asked:
“What qualities, O Blessed One, Make this moon disk unique?” {3.4.23}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-754}} The Blessed One said:
“It has three corners, {{note:{index:157,id:UT22084-079-008-756}}} is big in size, and is A receptacle for the qualities of all awakened ones.
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-757}} “These qualities of the awakened ones enter into it in the form of the letter a , and the rest. Possessing the luster of a crystal or the moon, they come in atop the moon disk, causing the mind, which is luminous by nature, to expand. {{note:{index:158,id:UT22084-079-008-758}}} The follower of Mantra should then generate the altruistic aspiration for awakening with the following mantra: {{note:{index:159,id:UT22084-079-008-759}}}
“ Oṁ , I give rise to bodhicitta. {{note:{index:160,id:UT22084-079-008-761}}} {3.4.24}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-762}} “This bodhicitta arises from having performed this rite, And it begets kindness toward all beings. It is replete with wholesome qualities And destroys all afflictions. {3.4.25}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-763}} “In the center of the moon disk There is a second one—the moon of awakening. {3.4.26}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-764}} “Here, too, the qualities of the the awakened ones enter like stars in the form of the syllables ka , and so forth, by means of the qualities being reflected in the syllables. These syllables are:
“ ka kha ga gha ṅa ca cha ja jha ña ṭa ṭha ḍa ḍha ṇa ta tha da dha na pa pha ba bha ma ya ra la va śa ṣa sa ha kṣaḥ . {3.4.27}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-766}} “This maṇḍala procedure has not been taught in its entirety in other tantras. Here, in addition, in order to stabilize the generation of the mind of Samantabhadra, {{page:{number:49,folio:F.97.b}}} he should visualize himself in the image of a radiant, white vajra scepter there in the middle of the aforementioned moon disk, while reciting the following mantra: {{note:{index:161,id:UT22084-079-008-767}}}
“ Oṁ vajra! Please remain. {{note:{index:162,id:UT22084-079-008-769}}} {3.4.28}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-770}} “This conduct of awakening is unsurpassable. Its basis, it should be well understood, Is pristine, stainless wisdom without karmic stains. {3.4.29}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-771}} “In the center of the moon disk He should visualize a vajra scepter. {3.4.30}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-772}} “A follower of Mantra should visualize himself with a vajra body that extends throughout the entire expanse of space. {{note:{index:163,id:UT22084-079-008-773}}} {3.4.31}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-774}} “Then, while practicing the radiation and absorption Of tiny vajra scepters, he should recite the following mantra:
Oṁ , I am of the nature of vajra. {{note:{index:164,id:UT22084-079-008-776}}} {3.4.32}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-777}} “This vajra, which is the body of all the buddhas, Has neither appearance nor abode. It is unborn, unfabricated, pure, And devoid of nonexistence, and so forth. {3.4.33}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-778}} “It is unbreakable, indivisible, and ungraspable; It is the dharmakāya free of attributes; It arises as the nature of vajra {{note:{index:165,id:UT22084-079-008-779}}} and is therefore The unsurpassable vajra body.” {3.4.34}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-780}} Vajragarbha then asked, “How do I further meditate on this vajra, O Blessed One?” {3.4.35}
The Blessed One said, “May all the tathāgatas listen! One should again visualize Vajrasattva—the reflection of the buddhas endowed with the supreme of all characteristics—while reciting the following mantra:
“ Oṁ , I am just like all the tathāgatas. {{note:{index:166,id:UT22084-079-008-783}}} {3.4.36}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-784}} “The buddha body, its secret nature, and the conduct, The range of experience, and the awakening to reality— These are the five aspects of perfect awakening, The pure nature of all the buddhas.” {3.4.37}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-785}} Then the great bodhisattvas, led by Vajragarbha, addressed the Blessed One yet again:
“What, O Blessed One, are the secret vajra and lotus families?” {3.4.38}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-787}} The lord said:
“The vajra family abides in all tathāgatas; The lotus family includes great goddess deities. That is why the vajra scepter is positioned above the lotus flower— From there issue forth all the tathāgatas. {3.4.39}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-789}} “In this manner, one should generate oneself as Vairocana, visualizing, above and below, the syllables of the mantra. {{page:{number:50,folio:F.98.a}}} Following the usual procedure, one should then emanate Mount Sumeru and a vast triangle, adorned with a maṇḍala of different colored lights. One should visualize, arising there, a beautiful palace, and in it, the syllable paṁ , which transforms into a multicolored lotus with a sun disk atop it. This is adorned with the syllables ya, ra, la , and va , in conjunction with the maṇḍalas of wind, fire, and so forth. Then, above that, with the appropriate mantra, {{note:{index:167,id:UT22084-079-008-790}}} one should visualize a temple palace surmounted with a vajra-jewel pinnacle, shining with various jewels and gems, and adorned with colorful streamers and banners with tiny bells attached to them, shaken by the wind. The palace is further adorned with garlands, chaplets, multi-string chains of pearls, and moon crescents. It is praised and glorified by all the tathāgatas inhabiting it. While visualizing this one should recite the mantra hūṁ . {3.4.40}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-791}} “Having placed this mantra, hūṁ , on a moon disk in one’s heart, one should visualize that it transforms into a five-pronged vajra scepter. One should repeatedly radiate from it five-pronged vajra scepters, and absorb them all back as buddhas. Next, one should visualize that the very same vajra scepter transforms into Vajrasattva, radiant like the color of the moon, and endowed with the supreme of all characteristics. {3.4.41}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-792}} “Sitting on a moon disk, And adorned with all kinds of adornments, The hero, handsome in his singular wisdom and joy, Is holding a vajra scepter, a bell, {3.4.42}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-793}} “A sword, a goad, A skull cup, and a noose. The face on the right is black, And the one on the left, red. {3.4.43}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-794}} “He has three faces and six arms And is divinely beautiful, with three eyes on each of his faces. One should visualize him in a maṇḍala of pleasure, Nestled in the lotus of his consort (vidyā). {3.4.44}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-795}} “One should imagine that he is endowed with all the supreme Characteristics consistent with his being the lord of the maṇḍala. {{note:{index:168,id:UT22084-079-008-796}}} {3.4.45}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-797}} “In the east there is Vairocana; In the south, Ratnasambhava; In the west, Amitābha; And in the north, Amoghasiddhi. {3.4.46} {{page:{number:51,folio:F.98.b}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-798}} “In the northeast there is Locanā; In the southeast, Māmakī; In the southwest, Pāṇḍaravāsinī; And in the northwest, Tārā. {3.4.47}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-799}} “In the outer circle,
“White Raudrī in the east, Yellow Vajrabimbā in the south, Red Rāgavajrā in the west, And green Vajrasaumyā in the north. {3.4.48}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-801}} “In the northeast there is white and yellow Vajrayakṣī; In the southeast, yellow and red Vajraḍākinī; In the southwest, red and blue Śabdavajrā; And in the northwest, green and white Pṛthivīvajrā. {3.4.49}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-802}} “In the outer circle, {{note:{index:169,id:UT22084-079-008-803}}}
“In the northeast, Vaṃśā;In the southeast, Vīṇā; In the southwest, Mukundā; And in the northwest, Murajā. {3.4.50}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-805}} “Vaṃśā and the other three have two arms and a single face. {3.4.51}
“On the outer rim there should be placed the yoginīs of the maṇḍala, each holding her respective emblem—the flower, and so forth. They likewise have two arms. {3.4.52}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-807}} “At the eastern gate one should draw the goddess Vajrāṃkuśī, the color of dark sky, with her right and left faces black and white respectively. In her first hand she holds a goad, in the second she brandishes a sword, and in the third she holds a discus. Her left hands hold a noose, display a threatening gesture, and hold a bell. These are the emblems in her six hands. {3.4.53}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-808}} “At the southern gate one should draw the white and yellow mother, {{note:{index:170,id:UT22084-079-008-809}}} Vajrapāśī, whose right and left faces are black and red respectively. In her right hands she brandishes a noose, a vajra scepter, and a sword. In her left hands she holds a discus and a bell, and holds a noose while forming a threatening gesture. These are the emblems in her six hands. {3.4.54}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-810}} “At the western gate one should draw Vajrasphoṭā, {{note:{index:171,id:UT22084-079-008-811}}} red in color and with great brilliance. Her right and left faces are black and white respectively. In her six hands she is holding, on the right, a fettering chain, a vajra scepter, and a sword, and on the left, a discus, a bell, and a goad. These are the emblems in her six hands. {3.4.55} {{page:{number:52,folio:F.99.a}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-812}} “At the northern gate there is the terrifying Vajraghaṇṭā. She has three faces: the middle one is green, the right one black, and the left one white. In her six hands she holds a bell, a vajra scepter, a sword, a discus, a goad, and a noose. {3.4.56}
“All should be visualized standing on a sun disk upon a multicolored lotus, with their blazing hair flowing upward. {3.4.57}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-814}} “In the intermediate directions, starting from the southeast, there are yoginīs who hold their respective emblems—the flower, and so forth. They are typically known to possess two arms. {3.4.58}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-8108}} “At the gates starting from the east, there are yoginīs holding a goad, a noose, a fettering chain, and a bell. Thus the maṇḍala is provided with gatekeepers. {3.4.59}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-816}} “The syllables jaḥ, hūṁ, vaṁ , and hoḥ are taught to be their respective heart mantras; there is no doubt about this. Through being arranged, fashioned, and so forth in this manner, this is the outer maṇḍala of glorious Vajrasattva, replete with the emblems and gestures. {3.4.60}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-8109}} “Inside the outer maṇḍala, the same design as before, is another, half its size—the maṇḍala of the wind element, in the shape of a half-moon disk, adorned with eight pillars, and surrounded on the outside with a quadruple line. {3.4.61}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-818}} “In all the locations assigned to the respective deities, one should arrange Gaurī and the others, along with their thrones, as described. In the center one should visualize the syllable hrīḥ; {{note:{index:172,id:UT22084-079-008-819}}} in the quarter toward the east, the syllable hrīḥ; {{note:{index:173,id:UT22084-079-008-820}}} in the south, the syllable hiḥ; {{note:{index:174,id:UT22084-079-008-821}}} in the west, the syllable gīḥ; {{note:{index:175,id:UT22084-079-008-822}}} in the north, the syllable jiḥ; {{note:{index:176,id:UT22084-079-008-823}}} in the southeast, the syllable taṁ ; in the southwest, the syllable jaṁ ; in the northwest, the syllable maṁ ; and in the northeast, one should place the syllable haṁ . {3.4.62}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-824}} “In the outer circle, in the southeast, one should place the syllable oṁ ; in the southwest, the syllable aṁ; {{note:{index:177,id:UT22084-079-008-825}}} in the northwest, the syllable eṁ; {{note:{index:178,id:UT22084-079-008-826}}} and in the northeast, one should place the syllable aiṁ. {{note:{index:179,id:UT22084-079-008-827}}} {3.4.63}
“At the eastern gate one should place the syllable jaḥ ; at the southern gate, the syllable hūṁ ; at the western gate, the syllable vaṁ ; and at the northern gate, the syllable hoḥ . {3.4.64}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-829}} “Further outside one should visualize, surrounding the maṇḍala, the eight charnel grounds. One should place there the eight great spirits, Indra, and the others, who are very frightened. {3.4.65} {{page:{number:53,folio:F.99.b}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-830}} “In the east one should draw A host of gods sitting upon a bodhi tree. In the south one should draw The powerful lord Yama atop a mango tree. {3.4.66}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-831}} “In the west one should place The king of clouds {{note:{index:180,id:UT22084-079-008-832}}} on an aśoka tree. Likewise, in the north one should situate The army of yakṣas on a bodhi tree. {3.4.67}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-833}} “Similarly, in the southeast one should draw A crowd of ṛṣis upon a pongamia tree. In the southwest, on a jasmine shrub, One should place rākṣasas and the like. {3.4.68}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-834}} “In the northwest one should draw The lord of wind {{note:{index:181,id:UT22084-079-008-835}}} on a crepe jasmine bush. In the northeast one should draw A crowd of pretas on a banyan tree. {3.4.69}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-836}} “One should live covered in ashes Along with Rudra, Indra, Upendra, Candra Arka, and Yama, who were sealed And confounded, and their treasures enjoyed. {{note:{index:182,id:UT22084-079-008-837}}} {3.4.70}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-838}} “Further, diligently practicing skillful means and wisdom, One should carry, on one’s left side, A khaṭvāṅga and a skull cup filled with blood, While gently sounding a bell. {3.4.71}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-839}} “In one’s right hand one should carry A blazing vajra scepter, which frightens even fear itself. Having assumed the ardhaparyaṅka posture, One should press down on one’s left thigh. {{note:{index:183,id:UT22084-079-008-840}}} {3.4.72}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-841}} “Stepping over Brahmā, and so forth, One should enjoy this act in a manly manner. {{note:{index:184,id:UT22084-079-008-842}}} He will give . . . {{note:{index:185,id:UT22084-079-008-843}}} {3.4.73}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-844}} “If the practitioner meditates Visualizing multicolored light all around That takes the form of scintillating clouds of buddhas, He will swiftly gain accomplishment.” {3.4.74}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-845}} This concludes the sovereign third chapter of the glorious “ Emergence from Sampuṭa .”
Chapter 4
Part 1
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-846}} [Vajragarbha said:]
“I would like to hear, O Blessed One, About the characteristics of the external signs. {{note:{index:186,id:UT22084-079-008-848}}} Please tell me, O great sage, This secret of yogins and yoginīs.” {4.1.1}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-849}} The lord then entered the meditative absorption called “the power of ḍākinīs’ conquest” and explained the pledge signs of ḍākinīs. {4.1.2}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-850}} “The vajra (male sexual organ) {{note:{index:187,id:UT22084-079-008-851}}} is in Kollagiri And the lotus (female sexual organ) is in Muṃmuni. The rattle of the wood (hand-drum) is unbroken; It sounds for compassion, not for quarrels. {{note:{index:188,id:UT22084-079-008-852}}} {4.1.3} {{page:{number:54,folio:F.100.a}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-853}} “Here we eat strength (meat) And drink passion (wine) extravagantly. Hey, the Kāliñjaras (worthy ones) may enter here; The emissions (unworthy ones) are excluded. {4.1.4}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-854}} “We ingest the four ingredients {{note:{index:189,id:UT22084-079-008-855}}} (feces)— Also musk (urine), olibanum (menstrual blood), and camphor (semen). Here we eat jasmine wood (condiments) and rice products (human flesh) To our satisfaction. {4.1.5}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-856}} “We do swinging (coming) and phlegm (going) Without thinking in terms of ‘pure’ and ‘impure.’ Our bodies are naked (adorned with bone ornaments). Here we enter the corpse (our refuge). {4.1.6}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-857}} “At the sandalwood (our meeting) we perform the olibanum (sex act); Here small drums (the untouchables) are not shunned. {4.1.7}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-858}} “ Mukhe, ghoghu, gughu, mughu, lughu, duṣṭu —one should enthusiastically utter these code words when the signs of a yoginī are seen. {{note:{index:190,id:UT22084-079-008-859}}} {4.1.8}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-861}} “And also:
“ Ḍā, ḍī, pu, su, mā, yo, bhī, vī, lu, strī, sa (?), pe, phī (?), bha, bhū, pī, dū, ḍī, ma, strī, kū, hā, ja, ke, bha, sva, {{note:{index:191,id:UT22084-079-008-862}}} pra, jā, o, mā, go, rā, de, mā, kā, {{note:{index:192,id:UT22084-079-008-863}}} tri, ko, ka, la, kā, hi, mre (?), śri, sau, su, na, si, ma, ku. {{note:{index:193,id:UT22084-079-008-864}}} {4.1.9}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-865}} “Now I shall explain the outer {{note:{index:194,id:UT22084-079-008-866}}} secret signs In the prescribed order, Through which a [vajra] brother or sister Can be recognized without doubt. {4.1.10}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-867}} “The potaṅgī {{note:{index:195,id:UT22084-079-008-868}}} gesture is answered with the same. Other code words and signs used are gamu, lumba , ‘swallowing,’ ‘wooden vessel,’ ‘heart,’ ‘Kuru woman,’ ‘earring,’ alikaraṇa , ‘boar,’ ‘hearing,’ ‘churning,’ ‘man,’ ‘palm of the hand,’ ‘hell,’ ‘someone,’ kākhilā , ‘sighing,’ ‘enclosure,’ ‘cessation,’ ‘cruel one,’ ‘end,’ ‘scorpion,’ ‘younger sister,’ mudaka , ‘the grasping one’ which means ‘mudrā,’ ‘touching the teeth,’ ‘perfume seller,’ ‘arrival’ which means ‘from what place,’ ‘ray of light,’ ‘hanging down,’ ‘teeth,’ ‘cessation,’ ‘report,’ ‘smoke,’ ‘fond of smoke,’ ‘summit,’ ‘rivulets,’ ‘finger,’ ‘mouth,’ ‘stripe(?),’ ‘eating,’ ‘series,’ ‘intention,’ ‘movement,’ ‘lord of animals,’ ‘circle,’ ‘the same,’ phālguṣa , ‘great syllable,’ chā, nā, go, ma, bhā, hā , ‘makers of offerings(?),’ and ‘remaining.’ A particular message is conveyed when one is touching one’s mouth or one’s teeth. {{page:{number:55,folio:F.100.b}}} ‘Bashful.’ A particular message is conveyed when one is touching space, or touching one’s thighs below. {{note:{index:196,id:UT22084-079-008-869}}} The signs and their responses are thus laid down.” {4.1.11}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-870}} This concludes the first part of the fourth chapter on the secret language of letters and speech.
Part 2
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-871}} “Listen, O most compassionate Vajragarbha, With undivided attention. {4.2.1}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-872}} “Dākinīs are known to be of seven types: Rūpikā, Cumbikā, Lāmā, Parāvṛttā, Samālikā, Anivṛttikā, and Aihikī. {4.2.2}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-873}} “She who gazes with passion And then frowns, Whose beauty seduces at first {{note:{index:197,id:UT22084-079-008-874}}} But later brings ruin, {{note:{index:198,id:UT22084-079-008-875}}} Is known as Rūpikā, the beautiful; She is served {{note:{index:199,id:UT22084-079-008-876}}} in nonduality by the valiant. {4.2.3}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-877}} “She who kisses a child as soon as she sees it, Regardless of whether the child is lovable or not, Is known as Cumbikā, the kisser. This ḍākinī is very congenial. {{note:{index:200,id:UT22084-079-008-878}}} {4.2.4}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-879}} “She who has an animal gaze and an angry expression, Who threatens with her knitted eyebrows, And frightens others with her heavy sighs, Is to be known as Lāmā. {4.2.5}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-880}} “She who frightens away All wild boars, jackals, cats, and horses Is called Parāvṛttā, the one who repels. {{note:{index:201,id:UT22084-079-008-881}}} {4.2.6}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-882}} “She who is happy and laughs gregariously, And who, once gone, never returns Is known as Samālikā. {4.2.7}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-883}} “She by whose touch, when she is upset, one will die— Whether it be by her hand, a clod of earth where she walked, Her foot, the end of her garment, or a stick that she touched— Is called Anivṛttikā. {4.2.8}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-884}} “She who laughs, talks, cries, Or suddenly gets angry Is known as Aihikā, The ḍākinī, mother of yogins. {{note:{index:202,id:UT22084-079-008-885}}} {4.2.9}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-886}} “They each hold a skull cup, an axe, an elephant tusk, a banner made from crocodile skin, a sword, a lance, and a conch, which are known to be their seven respective implements. {{note:{index:203,id:UT22084-079-008-887}}} {4.2.10}
“The adept of yoga should always be able to recognize these signs according to the procedure of sampuṭa.” {{note:{index:204,id:UT22084-079-008-889}}} {4.2.11}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-890}} This concludes the second part of the fourth chapter on the characteristics and signs particular to demon ḍākinīs of charnel grounds.
Part 3
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-891}} “Now I will teach The telltale signs of the lāmās. {{page:{number:56,folio:F.101.a}}} If a woman has a pink complexion, And eyes elongated like lotus leaves, {{note:{index:205,id:UT22084-079-008-892}}} {4.3.1}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-893}} “And if she always prefers white clothes, Smells of fresh sandalwood, Delights in the company of bliss-gone ones, And responds to affectionate glances, {4.3.2}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-894}} “One should draw a lotus in one’s house and worship it, For she belongs to the family of Padmanarteśvara. {{note:{index:206,id:UT22084-079-008-895}}} If a woman has the sign of a trident between her eyebrows, A dark blue face, a white body, {{note:{index:207,id:UT22084-079-008-896}}} {4.3.3}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-897}} “And the hue and scent of a blue lotus, {{note:{index:208,id:UT22084-079-008-898}}} One should draw a vajra scepter in one’s house and always worship it, For she arises from the family of the glorious Heruka And is known as the ‘tranquil {{note:{index:209,id:UT22084-079-008-899}}} ḍākinī.’ {4.3.4}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-900}} “If a woman has red eyes, a pink complexion, Red feet and hands, And is always delighted In the company of goats and chickens, {4.3.5}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-901}} “One should draw a vajra scepter in one’s house And always worship it, For there is no doubt that such ḍākinīs Arise from the family of glorious Heruka. {4.3.6}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-902}} “If a circle is visible On a woman’s forehead or hand; If she has a yellow and dark blue complexion, And always prefers yellow clothes; {4.3.7}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-903}} “And if she is possessed of great beauty and grace, And her head smells of flowers, {{note:{index:210,id:UT22084-079-008-904}}} One should, accordingly, draw a circle in one’s house, For she belongs to the Tathāgata family. {4.3.8}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-905}} “If a woman is black and dark blue, And has prominent, white fangs; If she is beautiful and unremittingly cruel And always wears her hair loose; {4.3.9}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-906}} “And if she enjoys bathing constantly And always talks a lot, One should draw a vajra scepter in one’s house, For such a woman arises from the family of Vajravārāhī. {4.3.10}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-907}} “If a woman is white with a golden hue, Has bright eyes, and is hairy; If a vajra scepter is visible On her forehead or hand; {4.3.11}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-908}} “And if she is of royal stature, {{note:{index:211,id:UT22084-079-008-909}}} Proud, always speaks the truth, And exudes the scent of jasmine, One should draw a vajra scepter in one’s house And worship it continually, {4.3.12}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-910}} “For she is the great queen of yogins, the exalted one, Arisen from the family of Khaṇḍarohā. {{page:{number:57,folio:F.101.b}}} Again, if a woman is fond of eating meat And her eyes are the color of collyrium; {4.3.13}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-911}} “If she has the sign of a spear on her forehead And takes pleasure in cruel acts; If she continually frequents charnel grounds And is neither frightened nor squeamish; {4.3.14}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-912}} “And if she has a convergence of wrinkles {{note:{index:212,id:UT22084-079-008-913}}} on her forehead, One should draw a skull cup in one’s house And always worship it, For she arises from the family of Heruka. {4.3.15}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-914}} “If a woman has the complexion of a rain cloud And uneven teeth, And if she continually commits cruel acts And the teeth in the left side of her mouth protrude, {4.3.16}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-915}} “One should draw an axe in one’s house And always worship it, For there is no doubt that she is a ḍākinī, Arisen from the family of Vināyaka. {4.3.17}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-916}} “If a woman has curly hair And a round face; If she typically has facial hair, Long eyebrows, and body hair; {4.3.18}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-917}} “If she dresses in white, and is pure and gentle; And if she speaks the truth unwaveringly And always delights in the true Dharma, She should be known as Vīrabhāginī, sister of the valiant. {4.3.19}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-918}} “One should make the lotus gesture to her, And again, the tortoise gesture. One should honor the ritual pitcher As this is the prescribed “gesture of response.” {4.3.20}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-919}} “On the tenth lunar day One should draw a lotus in one’s house. Again, if a woman has fleshy lips, and elongated eyes; If her eyes are reddish-yellow; {4.3.21}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-920}} “If she is blessed with good fortune and wealth, And has the complexion of a yellow jade orchid flower; If her body is long, she has long hands, And if she is fond of colorful clothes; {4.3.22}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-921}} “If there are three lines on her forehead Or at the border of her hairline above it; If she laughs and rejoices; If she crosses one’s path, then stops; {4.3.23}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-922}} “And if she is typically fond of stories about People killed in battles, then, If one sees a wanton woman like this, One should show her the spear gesture. {4.3.24}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-923}} “Drawing in one’s left foot, One should perform a dance. A gesture prescribed in response to this Is turning one’s body to the left. {4.3.25}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-924}} “One should worship her on the fourteenth and the eighth lunar days, {{page:{number:58,folio:F.102.a}}} Having drawn the shape of a spear in one’s house— This is to reflect the fact that she belongs To the lāmā goddesses of the family of Amitābha, the lord of the world. {{note:{index:213,id:UT22084-079-008-925}}} {4.3.26}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-926}} “If a woman has a pink complexion And greenish-yellow eyes; If her hair is curly And she wears a hair band; {4.3.27}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-927}} “If a single long line Is etched on her forehead, Extending upward, And she is fond of red clothes; {4.3.28}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-928}} “If she continually laughs, sings, And suddenly gets angry; And if she always delights in quarrels, Showing exceptional fickle-mindedness, {4.3.29}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-929}} “When one sees a wanton woman like this, One should make the lance gesture. A second gesture, that of the bell, Should then be made with care. {{note:{index:214,id:UT22084-079-008-930}}} {4.3.30}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-931}} “Turning one’s body to the left Is the prescribed response gesture. Again, if a woman is short And has thick shins, {4.3.31}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-932}} “And if she is typically fond of yellow clothes And her clothes hang loosely around her neck— When seeing a wanton woman such as this, One should make the wheel gesture. {4.3.32}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-933}} “A second gesture, that of the conch, Should then be given with care. {{note:{index:215,id:UT22084-079-008-934}}} Turning one’s body to the left Is the prescribed response gesture. {4.3.33}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-935}} “One should draw a vajra scepter in one’s house On the fourteenth lunar day, right for her worship. Again, if a woman is hairy all over And has yellowish-black eyes; {4.3.34}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-936}} “If she grimaces frighteningly, baring her teeth; If her face is thick, with a fleshy mouth, Pouting lips, deeply set eyes, And a crooked nose; {4.3.35}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-937}} “If she ever displays gandharva skills; {{note:{index:216,id:UT22084-079-008-938}}} And if she is of the color of dark cloud and has a big belly— When seeing a wanton woman like this, One should make the snake gesture. {4.3.36}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-939}} “A second gesture, that of the lance, Should be given with care. As before, turning one’s body to the left Is the prescribed response gesture. {4.3.37}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-940}} “One should draw teeth in one’s house On the eleventh lunar day, right for her worship, And honor them at all times.” {4.3.38}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-941}} This concludes the third part of the fourth chapter on sign gestures.
Part 4
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-942}} “Now I will teach more on The signs of bodily gestures. If a woman touches the topknot on her head, One should show her one’s head. {4.4.1} {{page:{number:59,folio:F.102.b}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-943}} “If she points at her forehead, One should show her one’s cheek. If she shows her teeth, One should show her one’s tongue. {4.4.2}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-944}} “If she touches her lips, One should point at one’s chin. If she touches her neck, One should show her one’s abdomen. {4.4.3}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-945}} “If she points at her abdomen, One should show her one’s navel. If she shows her bristling bodily hair, {{note:{index:217,id:UT22084-079-008-946}}} One should point at the ground. {4.4.4}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-947}} “If she shows her secret part, One should show her one’s liṅga. If she shows her knee, One should point at one’s shin. {4.4.5}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-948}} “If she shows her hand, One should show her one’s arm. If she shows her foot, One should show her the sole of one’s foot. {4.4.6}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-949}} “If she shows her finger, One should show her a fingernail. If she points at the ground, One should point at the sky. {4.4.7}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-950}} “If she points at the sky, One should point at the sun. If she points at a river, One should point toward the ocean. {4.4.8}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-951}} “If she shows one finger, This means ‘you are welcome.’ If she shows two fingers, This means ‘you are most welcome.’ {4.4.9}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-952}} “If she makes a gesture with her right eyebrow, One should make the same with the left eyebrow— These two gestures signify the two teachers.” {{note:{index:218,id:UT22084-079-008-953}}} {4.4.10}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-954}} This concludes the sovereign fourth chapter on the sign language of vajraḍākinīs in the glorious “ Emergence from Sampuṭa ,” so called to reflect the secret foundation of all tantras.
Chapter 5
Part 1
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-955}} “Now I will teach About the gathering of all sublime people. There, one should consume a dish of good food, Served in a dish with two compartments. {5.1.1}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-956}} Vajragarbha asked, “Blessed One, what places are places of gatherings?” {5.1.2}
The Blessed One said:
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-958}} “There are pīṭhas and auxiliary pīṭhas, And likewise, kṣetras and auxiliary kṣetras. There are also chandohas and auxiliary chandohas, Melāpakas and auxiliary melāpakas. {5.1.3}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-959}} “There are charnel grounds and auxiliary charnel grounds, Pīlavas and auxiliary pīlavas. These are the twelve types of meeting places. {{page:{number:60,folio:F.103.a}}} The lord of the ten bhūmis has not specified Any places other than these twelve.” {5.1.4}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-960}} Vajragarbha asked, “O Blessed One, which places are the pīthas, and so forth? What are the twelve types of places? Please be so kind as to explain, you who are born of greatness.” {5.1.5}
The Blessed One said:
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-962}} “Jālandhara {{note:{index:219,id:UT22084-079-008-963}}} is said to be a pīṭha, And so, too, is Oḍḍiyāna. Pūrṇagiri {{note:{index:220,id:UT22084-079-008-964}}} is a pīṭha, And so is Arbuda. {5.1.6}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-965}} “Godāvarī is said to be an auxiliary pīṭha, And so, too, is Rāmeśvara. Devīkoṭa has been proclaimed to be likewise, And so, too, Mālava. {5.1.7}
