{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-966}} “Kāmarūpa and, likewise, Oḍra Have been proclaimed to be kṣetras. Triśakuni is an auxiliary kṣetra, And so is Kośala. {5.1.8}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-967}} “Kaliṅga is said to be a chandoha, {{note:{index:221,id:UT22084-079-008-968}}} And so, too, is Lampāka. Kāñcī has been declared to be an auxiliary chandoha, And so, too, has Himālaya. {5.1.9}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-969}} “Pretādhivāsinī is a melāpaka, And so is Gṛhadevatā. Sauraṣṭra is an auxiliary melāpaka, As is Suvarṇadvīpa. {5.1.10}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-970}} “Nagara is famed as a charnel ground; So, too, is Sindhu. Maru is said to be an auxiliary charnel ground, And so is Kulatā. {5.1.11}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-971}} “Kāruṇya is said to be a pīlava, And so is Karmārapāṭaka. Harikela is a pīlava, {{note:{index:222,id:UT22084-079-008-972}}} And so is the middle of the salt ocean, Lavaṇasāgara. {5.1.12}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-973}} “Vindhyā and Kaumārapaurikā Are auxiliary pīlavas. {{note:{index:223,id:UT22084-079-008-974}}} Adjacent to them are the charnel grounds Pretasaṃghāta and Udadhitaṭa. {{note:{index:224,id:UT22084-079-008-975}}} Udyāna and Vāpikātīra Are said to be auxiliary charnel grounds. {5.1.13}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-976}} “Now I will explain the manner in which such places are inhabited.
“Viraja is inhabited by a goddess living in a mango tree, Koṅkana is inhabited by one in a somavarṇikā tree, Caritra, by one in a pongamia tree, And Aṭṭahāsa, by one living in a kadamba tree. {5.1.14}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-978}} “Devīkoṭa is inhabited by a goddess living in a banyan tree, Harikela, by one in a hari {{note:{index:225,id:UT22084-079-008-979}}} tree, Uḍḍiyāna, by one in an aśoka tree, And Jālandhara, by one in a thorn apple tree. {{note:{index:226,id:UT22084-079-008-980}}} {5.1.15}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-981}} “A pīṭha is the bhūmi called Joyous, And an auxiliary pīṭha, the bhūmi called Stainless. A kṣetra should be known as the bhūmi Shining, {{page:{number:61,folio:F.103.b}}} And an auxiliary kṣetra as Blazing Wisdom. {5.1.16}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-982}} “A chandoha should be known as the bhūmi Revealed, And an auxiliary chandoha as Difficult to Conquer, {{note:{index:227,id:UT22084-079-008-983}}} A melāpaka as the bhūmi Far Gone, And an auxiliary melāpaka as Immovable. {5.1.17}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-984}} “A charnel ground is the bhūmi Excellent Intelligence, And an auxiliary charnel ground, Cloud of Dharma. The ‘barbarous’ language of the yoginī Thus depicts the bhūmis of the ten perfections. {5.1.18}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-985}} “One should visualize, externally and internally, All these different attributes as has been explained. {{note:{index:228,id:UT22084-079-008-986}}} {5.1.19}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-987}} “In addition, I will explain what days are suitable for a successful gathering of yoginīs.
“The fourteenth and the eighth day Of the moon’s waning fortnight are particularly recommended For consuming someone killed by a banner {{note:{index:229,id:UT22084-079-008-989}}} or a weapon, Or one who has been born seven times. {{note:{index:230,id:UT22084-079-008-990}}} {5.1.20}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-991}} “Generating compassion with ardor, The wise practitioner should perform the act of killing. Since those devoid of compassion will not succeed, One should therefore train in compassion. {5.1.21}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-992}} “ ‘Just as I feel for myself, so too should I for sentient beings. I am just as any other living being.’ Reflecting thus, and remaining in union with the deity, One will swiftly attain success.” {5.1.22}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-993}} This concludes the first part of the fifth chapter on meeting places.
Part 2
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-994}} Vajragarbha said:
“I would like to hear, O lord of knowledge, About the characteristic of the secret lotus. What is its use in the stages of attaining ultimate awakening, In which mind is mingled with gnosis?” {5.2.1}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-996}} The Blessed One said:
“In reliance upon the Catuṣpīṭha Tantra, A vajra holder progressing toward perfect awakening Should give rise to an attitude of equanimity, Casting aside his desires, and so forth. {5.2.2}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-998}} “He should sit on a comfortable seat, In a pleasant place, With thoughts of compassion and benevolence For all animate and inanimate things. {5.2.3}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-999}} “He should then visualize the central channel From top to bottom: the ‘end of sound,’ the secret lotus, And likewise, the different seats With their parts and their different letters. {{note:{index:231,id:UT22084-079-008-1000}}} {5.2.4}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1001}} “Vajra body, speech, and mind, Made manifest from within the sphere of phenomena, Are then brought together, {{note:{index:232,id:UT22084-079-008-1002}}} and through the ‘embryo’ method He becomes Vajrasattva. {5.2.5}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1003}} “In the highest state, Where the elements of water and fire become one taste, {{page:{number:62,folio:F.104.a}}} The natures of means and gnosis are joined in union And the six sense faculties become reflections of the Buddha. {5.2.6}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1004}} “He becomes a teacher of authentic treatises, And a follower of scripture who understands the truth. He will truly reach the other shore— The state of reality, the secret meaning. {{note:{index:233,id:UT22084-079-008-1005}}} {5.2.7}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1006}} “Having cleansed the body of impurities through applying The characteristics of reality, such as emptiness and the like, To all the previous characteristics, {{note:{index:234,id:UT22084-079-008-1007}}} He will win {{note:{index:235,id:UT22084-079-008-1008}}} the stages of perfect awakening. {5.2.8}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1009}} “In the center of a moon disk He should visualize the wisdom being, White as a jasmine flower or the moon, Emanating rays of moonlight. {5.2.9}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1010}} “The wisdom being has two arms And sits on a lotus in sattvaparyaṅka posture. He {{note:{index:236,id:UT22084-079-008-1011}}} is adorned with all kinds of jewelry And with the crown of the five buddhas. {5.2.10}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1012}} “His two hands, which he presses against his chest, Display the gesture of the great seal. He is possessed of great beauty and splendor. Such is the meditation on the wisdom being. {5.2.11}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1013}} “He should visualize a plantain flower at his navel, Endowed with all the aforementioned characteristics And reaching up as far as his heart. It opens there, revealing the original lotus flower. {{note:{index:237,id:UT22084-079-008-1014}}} {5.2.12}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1015}} “The lotus has eight exquisite petals, Filaments, and filament bulbs. He should then place the syllables on the petals [And visualize himself as Vajrasattva] sitting at the center of the maṇḍala. {5.2.13}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1016}} “He should visualize him with two arms and one face, White, divinely beautiful, and without any blemishes. In the center of his body he should visualize [the syllable of] consciousness, Joining it with his own awareness. {5.2.14}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1017}} “On the eastern petal, the petal of Akṣobhya, There is the syllable of Akṣobhya joined with loving kindness. On the petal at the southern gate There is the syllable of Ratnasambhava joined with compassion. {5.2.15}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1018}} “On the petal of the western gate, He should place the syllable of Amitābha, And at the location of the northern gate, The syllable of the mind of mighty Amoghasiddhi. {5.2.16}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1019}} “He should thus arrange the four syllables— Those that begin with a vowel and others, {{note:{index:238,id:UT22084-079-008-1020}}} Adding the sign of candrabindu as required— All adorned with white moonlight. {5.2.17}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1021}} “On the intermediate petals he should place {{page:{number:63,folio:F.104.b}}} The previously mentioned {{note:{index:239,id:UT22084-079-008-1022}}} four neuter syllables ( ṛ, ṝ, ḷ, ḹ ). In the center of them He should add the mind {{note:{index:240,id:UT22084-079-008-1023}}} syllable ( hūṁ ).” {5.2.18}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1024}} Vajragarbha said:
“My curiosity has been aroused, so please tell me, O Blessed One, how is it that despite Everything being empty and without characteristic, There is yoga, and so forth, involving syllables?” {5.2.19}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1026}} The Blessed One said:
“Hear the truth, Vajragarbha, About the emptiness of objects and their properties {{note:{index:241,id:UT22084-079-008-1028}}} — It is like how a plantain tree, itself without essence, Yields fruit that is the ambrosia of essences. {5.2.20}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1029}} “In the center there is cognition-gnosis, Corresponding in nature to formless cognizance. One cannot find there any characteristic, For it is the stainless body of gnosis. {5.2.21}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1030}} “Free of being either entity or non-entity, Syllabic forms emerge from where there are none. At their core is an empty essence, Whose reality the yogin must apprehend. {5.2.22}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1031}} “Once this property has been properly cognized With a mind steeped in the gnosis of equality, It will soon be seen that he is On the path to perfect awakening. {5.2.23}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1032}} “This path relies on the guru’s instructions As it involves the nature of gnosis-consciousness. Its properties are indicated in treatises; Its reality, however, is pointed out by the valiant instructor. {5.2.24}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1033}} “He should always visualize it {{note:{index:242,id:UT22084-079-008-1034}}} As engulfed in white light, And imagine it with the other seed syllables of the [five] ambrosias, In a stūpa with five layers. {{note:{index:243,id:UT22084-079-008-1035}}} {5.2.25}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1036}} “The bodhicitta drop, sublime with the glow of white light, Overflows with a stream of ambrosia. At the heart, in the center of the lotus containing the syllables, Is an orb the size of a thumb. {5.2.26}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1037}} “In its center there are syllables {{note:{index:244,id:UT22084-079-008-1038}}} Embodying all vowels and consonants, Radiant white in color, Emitting rays of moonlight. {5.2.27}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1039}} “At the openings in their center There is a drop, consisting of what is known as consciousness, As fine as one hundredth of a hair tip, In the form of an infinitesimally small particle. {5.2.28}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1040}} “Since it is the nature of the consciousness Of those who cognize objects and their properties, Look into the state of abiding as the drop— It is characterized by non-perception and non-thought. {{note:{index:245,id:UT22084-079-008-1041}}} {5.2.29} {{page:{number:64,folio:F.105.a}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1042}} “The consciousness-gnosis {{note:{index:246,id:UT22084-079-008-1043}}} may be grasped By relying on the guru’s instructions Regarding the descent of the drop From the opening at the fontanel down to the heart. {5.2.30}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1044}} “The outsiders will not find the right path, Which is difficult to find even with the aid of treatises. Such treatises are easy to find, But the practices described therein are difficult to discern. {5.2.31}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1045}} “He should eagerly follow the guru’s instructions, Applying the methods used by yogins. By following the path shown by the guru, a wise practitioner Will be able to discern the practices described in treatises. {5.2.32}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1046}} “Fully collected, he should meditate merging with the essence, Unwavering and untroubled. {{note:{index:247,id:UT22084-079-008-1047}}} Phenomena are preceded by the mind; They are purified by mind and have the swiftness of thought. {5.2.33}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1048}} “It is through the mind, with its king-like grace, That one speaks and acts. Thus, with everything being the nature of mind, The wise one knows that he is born from mind. {5.2.34}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1049}} “The yogin should recite the mantra as he likes, Keeping his attention on his heart, For it is not the principal natures ( tattva ) {{note:{index:248,id:UT22084-079-008-1050}}} that Constitute the cause, but the seed syllables. {5.2.35}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1051}} “Since the seed syllables comprise cause and effect, The principal natures should not be viewed as such. The five syllables to be visualized are The fivefold experience of existence, of form, and so forth. {5.2.36}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1052}} “As he is carried around everywhere, {{note:{index:249,id:UT22084-079-008-1053}}} He should place these syllables in the central channel. {{note:{index:250,id:UT22084-079-008-1054}}} Thus the syllables of gnosis and cognition should be placed At the roots of the three channels that always need to be blocked. {{note:{index:251,id:UT22084-079-008-1055}}} {5.2.37}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1056}} “When he longs for experiences of saṃsāra, {{note:{index:252,id:UT22084-079-008-1057}}} He should join these syllables, in mental recitation, With the ‘sound’ (long ū ) and the ‘drop’ (anunāsika), {{note:{index:253,id:UT22084-079-008-1058}}} Without, however, saying them aloud. {5.2.38}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1059}} “He will definitively and perpetually Come to abide, together with the buddhas, In the state that is always subtle and stainless, And where gnosis and cognition merge. {5.2.39}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1060}} “With its presence as gnosis, cognition may Then be observed in its progression toward perfect awakening. The first sign to be observed For all practitioners is the form of a bright flame. {5.2.40}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1061}} “The second sign {{note:{index:254,id:UT22084-079-008-1062}}} revealed Is sparkling dust resembling fireflies— It will be seen as circular shapes of white powder {{note:{index:255,id:UT22084-079-008-1063}}} Formed throughout the ten direction. {5.2.41}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1064}} “The third sign observed by practitioners Is the disappearance of afflictions. {{page:{number:65,folio:F.105.b}}} The fourth one to be revealed Is the experience of the pleasures of gods from the desire realm. {5.2.42}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1065}} “The fifth sign mentally perceived Is the experience of the delights of the form realm, The sixth is the pleasures of the formless realm, {{note:{index:256,id:UT22084-079-008-1066}}} And the seventh is those experienced by the buddhas. {5.2.43}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1067}} “With the arrival of the eighth sign, practitioners Can experience at will the fruition that is the goal of awakening. {5.2.44}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1068}} “Listen, O most compassionate Vajrasattva, {{note:{index:257,id:UT22084-079-008-1069}}} With undivided attention!
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1070}} “Definitely all things are known To possess purity as their essence. Subsequent to this, the deities are explained, One by one, according to their divisions. {{note:{index:258,id:UT22084-079-008-1071}}} {5.2.45}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1072}} “The aggregates, elements, and sense-fields Of embodied beings are pure by nature. Though veiled by ignorance and afflictions, they can be purified. Being the nature of one’s own awakening, {{note:{index:259,id:UT22084-079-008-1073}}} they are themselves pure, Such that one is not liberated through some extrinsic purity. {5.2.46}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1074}} “With the purity of sense objects, Self-reflexive awareness is the ultimate bliss. Objects of form, and so forth, And whatever else appears to practitioners, {5.2.47}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1075}} “Are all pure by nature, For everything is comprised of wakefulness.” {5.2.48}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1076}} Vajragarbha asked, “O Blessed One, what are the things that are impure?” {5.2.49}
The Blessed One said, “They are form, and so forth. Why are they impure? Because they involve apprehended object and apprehending subject.”
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1078}} Vajragarbha then asked, “Well, what then are apprehended object and apprehending subject?” {{note:{index:260,id:UT22084-079-008-1079}}} {5.2.50}
The Blessed One said,
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1081}} “Form is apprehended by the eye; Sound, by the ear; Odors, by the nose; And taste, by the tongue. {5.2.51}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1082}} “A physical object is felt by the body And the mind apprehends happiness, and so forth. These sense objects ought to be enjoyed After purifying them by removing poison. {{note:{index:261,id:UT22084-079-008-1083}}} {5.2.52}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1084}} “Form is Buddha Vairocana, Sensation is Vajrasūrya, Perception is Padmanarteśvara, Predispositions are Vajrarāja, {5.2.53}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1085}} “Consciousness is Vajrasattva— The inherent nature of everything is Heruka. The eye is called Mohavajra; The ear has the name Dveṣavajra. {5.2.54} {{page:{number:66,folio:F.106.a}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1086}} “Īrṣyāvajra is the nose, Rāgavajra is the mouth, Mātsaryavajra is touch, And Heruka, the supreme lord, is all the sensory fields and elements. {5.2.55}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1087}} “Pātanī is the element of earth; The element of water is known as Māraṇī. Ākarṣaṇī is the element of fire; The element of wind is Narteśvarī. {5.2.56}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1088}} “The element of space is said to be Padmajvālinī, because of her imperturbability. In this way the bodies of embodied beings— Their aggregates, and so forth—have the nature of deities. {5.2.57}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1089}} “Pleasure and pain, and acting on them, Generate afflictive emotions, and the rest— Following one’s lot resulting from this generation, One will incur either cyclic existence or its cessation.” {5.2.58}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1090}} This concludes the second part of the fifth chapter on the purity of the aggregates, and so forth.
Part 3
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1091}} “Now, the right practice, which destroys The enemy, conceptual thinking, will be explained; Distilled from the totality of Buddha’s teachings, This practice of reality {{note:{index:262,id:UT22084-079-008-1092}}} is supreme. {5.3.1}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1093}} “For the sake of the Buddha’s sons, Who are established in perfect awakening, This practice, the ultimate Perfection of Wisdom, Will be truthfully explained by Anaṅgavajra. {{note:{index:263,id:UT22084-079-008-1094}}} {5.3.2}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1095}} “Like a boat safely sailing on, She delivers all beings From the terrifying ocean of births, Rough with the waves of old age, and so forth. {5.3.3}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1096}} “She, the divine one, quickly brings accomplishment, Being an essential {{note:{index:264,id:UT22084-079-008-1097}}} receptacle of all good qualities. Manifested from the jewel of the mind, She fulfills everyone’s desired aim. {5.3.4}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1098}} “Since without her, who is praised by Vajradhara And constitutes the body of qualities of all the perfectly awakened ones, Accomplishment is not possible, the wise ones who desire liberation Should perform this unequaled practice. {5.3.5}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1099}} “The lotuses of her feet are worshiped by Viṣṇu, Indra, Śiva Mahādeva, Kubera, Brahmā, and so forth. By doing this practice that removes sin, The tathāgatas swiftly attained the ultimate state. {5.3.6} {{page:{number:67,folio:F.106.b}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1100}} “This practice of the central channel {{note:{index:265,id:UT22084-079-008-1101}}} has been taught By the glorious Vajrasattva for the benefit of the world. {5.3.7}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1102}} “Accordingly, the practitioner should cultivate This sublime inconceivable state in great secrecy. He should engage in this samaya practice While free of all concepts. {5.3.8}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1103}} “In the initial stage, the practitioner should abide With the natural outflow of the existing condition. Then, should he tire from meditation, He should take a break, adopting the playfulness of a child. {5.3.9}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1104}} “For the sake of different types of people who require guidance, He should visualize himself in the gentle form of Mañjuśrī. {{note:{index:266,id:UT22084-079-008-1105}}} {5.3.10}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1106}} “Everything known as accomplishment comes about through Different practices accordingly taught; there is, however, an unexcelled practice That brings about the unparalleled accomplishment of Samantabhadra— It is this practice that the Blessed Vajrasattva has taught. {{note:{index:267,id:UT22084-079-008-1107}}} {5.3.11}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1108}} “Always paying homage to his protector, The glorious vajra master, He should rely on the secret practice, Doing what needs to be done and maintaining a noble heart. {5.3.12}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1109}} “Then, following his inclinations While turning away from all attachments, He should comport himself while in touch with reality, In every respect like a lion. {5.3.13}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1110}} “Through perfectly knowing things as they are, And thus forming the intention to deliver the world, He comes to embody full mastery of the correct view, With a steadfast mind free of reference points. {5.3.14}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1111}} “All attributes such as the aggregates, elements, And so forth are like a dream and an illusion. Knowing the entire triple universe To be, in short, like this, {5.3.15}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1112}} “He should associate with those Who live free from all obscurations, {{note:{index:268,id:UT22084-079-008-1113}}} Casting far away All the eight worldly concerns. {5.3.16}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1114}} “Always free of concepts, He should gain certainty about the nondual state, And apply the six perfections In order to attain the accomplishment of an awakened one. {5.3.17}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1115}} “Although eminently engaged {{note:{index:269,id:UT22084-079-008-1116}}} for the welfare of beings, He should not form concepts about them. He should set his mind on awakening And embark on the practice of conquering the directions. {5.3.18} {{page:{number:68,folio:F.107.a}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1117}} “Being the embodiment of wisdom and means conjoined, And turning away from all attachments, He will succeed even in this lifetime If he exerts himself in the cultivation of true reality. {5.3.19}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1118}} “Free of all concepts and, in particular, Of ideas about other beings, He should enjoy anything at all, applying the understanding That things are like an illusion, and so forth. {5.3.20}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1119}} “Having arisen from the undifferentiated sphere of phenomena, No beings can become his adversaries. He should enjoy things as he pleases With a mindset free of hesitation. {5.3.21}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1120}} “All this is for the sake of enjoyment— This entire triple universe, Conjured up by Vajrasattva For practitioners’ benefit. {5.3.22}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1121}} “If, by attaining infinite gnosis, He does not need to worship the tathāgatas, What need is there to mention initiations, and so forth, For him constantly engaged in meditation? {5.3.23}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1122}} “The nature of all objects Is the nature of awakened mind. That alone is the Blessed One, the vajra holder. Therefore, that alone is the identity of the deities. {5.3.24}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1123}} “Neither maṇḍalas nor fasts are to be performed, Nor the formation of gestures or caityas. Also other things Taught by the glorious vajra lord Out of his great dedication— Of what use would they be to he who knows reality? {5.3.25}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1124}} “Just as one who seeks ambrosia Should discard the buttermilk after taking the fresh butter, So should he discard all thoughts After obtaining the ambrosia {{note:{index:270,id:UT22084-079-008-1125}}} of Dharma. {5.3.26}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1126}} “When the wise practitioner is without concepts, Has given up doubt, and is free of reference points, Then, just as Vajra Mind {{note:{index:271,id:UT22084-079-008-1127}}} has said, There is no doubt he will succeed. {5.3.27}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1128}} “Because of concepts, he will go to hell And wander in the ocean of cyclic existence, with its six destinies. But free from concepts, he will be liberated, Reaching the state of stainless tranquility. {5.3.28}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1129}} “Therefore, in order to destroy the net of concepts {{note:{index:272,id:UT22084-079-008-1130}}} He should regularly practice the samaya observances, Which were performed by the awakened one, Abiding by them wherever he may be. {5.3.29}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1131}} “They should be performed by someone who knows mantra, {{page:{number:69,folio:F.107.b}}} Without excessive attachment, but not eschewing anything. They all without exception should be regarded By applying the understanding of the non-arising of forms. {{note:{index:273,id:UT22084-079-008-1132}}} {5.3.30}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1133}} “He should drink the blood of dogs, donkeys, camels, elephants, and so on, And eat their meat regularly. Human meat smeared with blood Should be regarded as the best of all. {5.3.31}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1134}} “He should eat all kinds of poor meats, And the excellent meats containing hundreds of thousands of living creatures. The practitioner should also eat terribly putrid feces Swarming with hundreds of worms, {5.3.32}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1135}} “And keenly relish meat Mixed with dog and human vomit, Dowsed with vajra water, {{note:{index:274,id:UT22084-079-008-1136}}} covered in flies, And blended with feces. {5.3.33}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1137}} “He should drink vajra water. When meat cannot be found anywhere, in order to partake of it he should imagine something else in the form of meat and eat that. {5.3.34}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-8110}} “Foodstuffs inedible to others {{note:{index:275,id:UT22084-079-008-1139}}} are edible for the master of the true state. Places improper to visit are fine for him to visit. Things improper to do are proper for him. The follower of the mantra path must not think in terms of ‘fit to visit’ and ‘unfit to visit’; ‘edible’ and ‘inedible’; ‘desirable’ and ‘undesirable’; or ‘drinkable’ and ‘undrinkable.’ {5.3.35}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1140}} “He should be content in body, speech, and mind. In order to be free of mental agitation, the practitioner should always drink wine. Like the victorious ones, he should regard all things, whether repulsive or greatly enjoyable, colorful or plain, delightful or depressing, as identical. {{note:{index:276,id:UT22084-079-008-1141}}} {5.3.36}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-8111}} “He should not recite texts, assemble maṇḍalas, or gather flowers. He should not recite mantras, nor should he pay homage to the deity, consecrated things, and so forth. He should speak false words and approach the charming wives of others. He should have no loving kindness for rogues, {{page:{number:70,folio:F.108.a}}} and should kill buddhas and other living beings. {5.3.37}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1143}} “The wise practitioner, however, should always worship his teacher, venerated by the victorious ones, who is the wisdom and the pledge being—the best of all beings, and who is the samaya that bestows various accomplishments. Since whatever merit is possessed by the fully awakened ones and the bodhisattvas dwelling throughout the ten directions can be seen in the openings of the master’s pores, the buddhas rejoice at seeing the bodhisattvas worship the master. {{note:{index:277,id:UT22084-079-008-1144}}} {5.3.38}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1145}} “Since the buddhas with whom he has the bond of samaya will grant the desired awakening, he should never criticize the teacher and never disrespect his siblings on the vajra path. Accepting whatever is offered, he should not pay homage to caityas. {{note:{index:278,id:UT22084-079-008-1146}}} Regarding his blood brothers, sons, and father, as well as the kingdom with its pleasures, treasuries, riches, and granaries to all be like grass, he should gain dominion over the three realms.” {5.3.39}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1147}} This concludes the third part of the fifth chapter describing the post-initiatory observances. {{note:{index:279,id:UT22084-079-008-1148}}}
Part 4
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1149}} “Now I will teach about the signs indicating a full adoption of post-initiatory practice. {5.4.1}
“By these signs the vajra practitioner Can be recognized from afar without any doubt. He should eat and drink whatever food is found, Comprising the oblation to a ḍākinī, and so forth. {5.4.2}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1151}} “Wearing clothes and a kaupīna from a corpse, And smeared with ashes from a cremated body, He should wander around at night, In secret, carrying a bowl made from a broken skull. {5.4.3}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1153}} “At a crossroads, on a mountain, Under a lone tree, or in a charnel ground— It is said that in these four places The meditation of the follower of Mantra will be effective. {5.4.4}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1154}} “Alternatively, in a mātṛkās’ temple at night, Or in an isolated place, or the wilderness, When some heat has been generated, {{note:{index:280,id:UT22084-079-008-1155}}} He can do the following practice if he wishes to. {5.4.5}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1156}} “If he wants accomplishment for himself, He should start behaving like a child again. A practitioner of keen intellect should roam about With the purpose of benefiting sentient beings. {5.4.6} {{page:{number:71,folio:F.108.b}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1157}} “With his mind free of attachment, And always wearing colorful clothes, The practitioner should imagine that from the pores of his skin Radiate deities throughout the ten directions. {5.4.7}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1158}} “With himself transformed into Mañjuvajra, He should visualize the circle of his retinue of deities. The practitioner should do this in a pleasant lotus garden At a confluence of rivers. {5.4.8}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1159}} “Should he stay there and meditate, He will swiftly attain accomplishment. Alternatively, he should sojourn in a cave Or on a mountain peak, with a focused mind. {5.4.9}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1160}} “He should eat whatever he finds; Whenever he eats, he should offer an oblation, And he should bedeck himself with various fruits, garlands, and so forth, And likewise with little bundles of flowers, and so forth. {5.4.10}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1161}} “He should dress in clothes from the skins of living creatures. Aspiring for bliss, he is conferred bliss. {{note:{index:281,id:UT22084-079-008-1162}}} He should recite sometimes in Sanskrit And, conversely, sometimes in Prakrit. {5.4.11}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1163}} “In the vein of a madman, he should eat whatever he finds, whether it is regarded as fit for eating or not, roaming throughout other countries, renowned mountain caves, groves, great ancient charnel grounds, and the shores of great oceans. {5.4.12}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1164}} “Staying in such places, the wise practitioner should meditate Completely free of all fear. But once having done so, he should embark On the conquest of the quarters. {5.4.13}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1165}} “Completely free of every obscuration, He should fulfill the wishes Of all the residents throughout the ten directions, Who are veiled by the obscurations concomitant with birth. {5.4.14}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1166}} “When he has completely abandoned through meditation All involvement with apprehended objects and apprehending subjects, And all his meditation becomes like this, He is called “the conqueror of the quarters.” {5.4.15}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1167}} “Having then attained some stability, The practitioner of the real state is unassailable. {{note:{index:282,id:UT22084-079-008-1168}}} He can summon vidyā goddesses And make the most beautiful one his lover. {5.4.16}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1169}} “It could be an apsaras, who is a charming gem And attends to the gratification of vidyādharas, Or it could be a celestial daughter, a yakṣiṇī, A nāginī, or an asurī. {5.4.17} {{page:{number:72,folio:F.109.a}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1170}} “The practitioner should summon, From among them, one vidyā, pleasing to his mind. He should subdue her By means of a goad and a noose, {5.4.18}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1171}} “Until this deity grants all objects that may be useful, Without his having to beg for them. {{note:{index:283,id:UT22084-079-008-1172}}} Free from disease and old age, not swayed by opposites, He {{note:{index:284,id:UT22084-079-008-1173}}} will remain in the three worlds free from sin. {5.4.19}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1174}} “Having offered his body as a gift, The practitioner should then start his samaya practice. Accordingly, the gift should not be given Based on consideration of whether the recipient is worthy or not. {5.4.20}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1175}} “He should partake of solid and liquid food and drink Just as they happen to come by. He must not grasp in that regard, Deliberating in terms of what is “desirable” and “undesirable.” {5.4.21}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1176}} “He should be free from training {{note:{index:285,id:UT22084-079-008-1177}}} and initiations And know that there is no need for him to feel ashamed of anything. The practitioner should analyze such things with great compassion, According to the empty nature of all things. {5.4.22}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1178}} “Having gone beyond oblatory rites and austerities, He should likewise remain free from mantra recitation and meditation. Freed from the rules of such conduct and firmly established In deity yoga, he should do his observances accordingly. {5.4.23}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1179}} “Even if a demon as powerful as Indra Should clearly appear before him, He must not be afraid, But wander about like a lion. {5.4.24}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1180}} “For the sake of benefiting all beings, He should always drink compassion as his drink. Delighting likewise in the drink of yoga, The practitioner should not immerse himself in other drinks. {5.4.25}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1181}} “Now another samaya practice is described— That of the glorious position of a crown prince, Through which the final accomplishment is reached For the sake of benefiting all beings. {5.4.26}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1182}} “The meditator should put on his ears A set of fine earrings; On his head, a crown; On his wrists, a pair of bracelets; {5.4.27}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1183}} “On his hips, a waist chain; On his ankles, a pair of anklets; At the root of his upper arm, an arm bracelet; And on his neck, a necklace of bone. {{note:{index:286,id:UT22084-079-008-1184}}} {5.4.28}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1185}} “He should cover himself in a tiger skin And eat the five ambrosias. If he is a man, he should remain in the absorption Of the Heruka yoga. {5.4.29}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1186}} “He should find a girl from the vajra family With a beautiful face and elongated eyes, {{page:{number:73,folio:F.109.b}}} Who has been consecrated by himself and is compassionately disposed. Having obtained such a girl, he should learn the observance of consort practice. {5.4.30}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1187}} “If a girl from the vajra family is not available, He should go for one from the family of his chosen deity. Alternatively, he should take a girl from another family, Consecrated with the seed of awakening. {{note:{index:287,id:UT22084-079-008-1188}}} {5.4.31}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1189}} “When a song is sung, it should be A supreme song related to vajra. {{note:{index:288,id:UT22084-079-008-1190}}} When joy has arisen, He should dance as a cause of liberation. Accordingly, the practitioner should always Do his dance with vajra steps. {5.4.32}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1191}} “Akṣobhya is recollected by the crown, Amitābha by the earrings, Ratnasambhava by the necklace, And Vairocana by the wrist bracelets. {5.4.33}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1192}} “Amoghasiddhi resides in the waist chain, And the consort (prajñā) takes on the form of the khaṭvāṅga. {{note:{index:289,id:UT22084-079-008-1193}}} The practitioner should always eat medicinal herbs And drink water. {5.4.34}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1194}} “Old age and death will not take hold of him, And he will always be protected. He should fashion a tiara with the hair of a thief {{note:{index:290,id:UT22084-079-008-1195}}} And place there that which comes from hūṁ. {{note:{index:291,id:UT22084-079-008-1196}}} {5.4.35}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1197}} “He should wear five skulls representing the five buddhas As part of his practice of deity yoga. Making the skull pieces five finger-widths in length, He should keep them fastened to the tiara. {5.4.36}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1198}} “A doubly-twined cord of hair {{note:{index:292,id:UT22084-079-008-1199}}} Represents wisdom and means. The practitioner should wear, as part of his practice, Charnel ground ashes and a sacred cord made of a corpse’s hair. {5.4.37}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1200}} “His recitation is the sound of his ḍamaru, Which invites all sentient beings to be his guests. This should be the nature of his recitation, {{note:{index:293,id:UT22084-079-008-1201}}} While he himself should become Vajrakapāla. {5.4.38}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1202}} “He should avoid greed, stupidity, fear, anger, And the idea that shame is necessary. Embodying the nature of Heruka, The practitioner should mix with members of all the five castes. {5.4.39}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1203}} “He should recognize only one caste As comprising the five castes, For the distinction between many And just one caste should not be made. {5.4.40}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1204}} “He should without doubt perform the practice While depriving himself of sleep.” {5.4.41} {{page:{number:74,folio:F.110.a}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1205}} This concludes the chapter on the practice, the fifth in the “ Emergence from Sampuṭa .”
Chapter 6
Part 1
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1206}} [The goddess {{note:{index:294,id:UT22084-079-008-1207}}} said:]
“I would be interested to hear, my lord, What are the stages of self-consecration? What is the purpose of secrecy?” {6.1.1}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1209}} The Blessed One said:
“Listen, O most compassionate Vajrasattva, {{note:{index:295,id:UT22084-079-008-1211}}} With undivided attention! I will now briefly explain the definitive meaning Common to all tantras. {6.1.2}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1212}} “What is referred to with the letter e (the dharmodaya), Is the place with imperceptible characteristics. Going and coming with the elements, Mind is always in motion.” {6.1.3}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1213}} [The goddess asked], “Why is the word elements being used?” {6.1.4} The lord replied, “Regarding the secret sixteen syllables, {{note:{index:296,id:UT22084-079-008-1215}}} the following has been said:
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1216}} “The syllable ra is the element of blood. The ha is the two types of wind. The sye is said to be phlegm, And the pa , bile. {{note:{index:297,id:UT22084-079-008-1217}}} {6.1.5}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1218}} “The following ra is for chyle, {{note:{index:298,id:UT22084-079-008-1219}}} The me , for the two types of fat. {{note:{index:299,id:UT22084-079-008-1220}}} The ra is said to be fire, {{note:{index:300,id:UT22084-079-008-1221}}} And the mye , flesh. {6.1.6}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1222}} “The sa is said to be feces, While the rvā is fatty tissue. {{note:{index:301,id:UT22084-079-008-1223}}} The tma is said to be skin, And the ni , bone. {6.1.7}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1224}} “The sa is said to be urine, And the dā is thought to be lungs. The sthi is said to be the lotus, Moist with wonderful fluid. {6.1.8}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1225}} “The ta represents semen, Which comes from bodhicitta. This has been explained, goddess, Based on the natures of the channels and sounds. {{note:{index:302,id:UT22084-079-008-1226}}} {6.1.9}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1227}} “From the nature of bodhicitta Comes the embodiment of semen. The letter ra is said to be body heat; Bile is produced from blood. {6.1.10}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1228}} “Phlegm, which is held to be a singular property, Produces sweat and tendons. Wind is said to be their master; As the syllable ha , it is known to be omnipresent. {6.1.11}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1229}} “In the spaces between the bones Are planted the five seeds. On the palate is the ra And everywhere the sublime four syllables. {{note:{index:303,id:UT22084-079-008-1230}}} {6.1.12}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1231}} “At the location of the first enclosure, {{note:{index:304,id:UT22084-079-008-1232}}} {{page:{number:75,folio:F.110.b}}} And adorned with the five syllables, Is the letter ha conjoined with the sixth vowel ( ū ), Which is proclaimed to be the syllable of consciousness ( hūṁ ). {6.1.13}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1233}} “By means of the letter ha, All buddhas everywhere assemble. From this source, whose nature is sound, Emerge the objects of the samaya practice. {{note:{index:305,id:UT22084-079-008-1234}}} {6.1.14}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1235}} “Difficult to come by in the three worlds, this source {{note:{index:306,id:UT22084-079-008-1236}}} Is present at the beginning, in the middle, and at the end. One can connect to it, just like a churning stick is connected to the act of churning, By means of mantra recitation, meditation, and so forth. {6.1.15}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1237}} “Listen to what has been taught in the tantras. There are two subtle channels inside the womb, The left and the right. {6.1.16}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1238}} “In the left one, the white sexual fluid is known to be present; In the right one, the blood. Where they come into contact is The complete sphere of phenomena. {{note:{index:307,id:UT22084-079-008-1239}}} {6.1.17}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1240}} “The sattvam principle is the body, rajas is speech, {{note:{index:308,id:UT22084-079-008-1241}}} And, according to its nature, tamas is mind. Sattvam is semen, rajas is blood, {{note:{index:309,id:UT22084-079-008-1242}}} And tamas , foetal development ( utpatti ). {6.1.18}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1243}} “Through the meeting of the vajra and the lotus, Existence and nonexistence become a single taste. The experience becomes of a single taste. {{note:{index:310,id:UT22084-079-008-1245}}} Feces, urine, phlegm, blood, and semen as the fifth {{note:{index:311,id:UT22084-079-008-1246}}} — {6.1.19}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1247}} “The embryo consists of these five ambrosias, Therefore it is here called vajrin. {{note:{index:312,id:UT22084-079-008-1248}}} Bone, marrow, and semen Are said to come from the father. {6.1.20}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1249}} “Skin, flesh, and blood Are said to come from the mother. These six are described as bodily elements And are joined together in the embryo. {6.1.21}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1250}} “A single cell becomes two; The two become many— Since it has the nature of both one and many, It is here called vajrin . {6.1.22}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1251}} “In what is described solely in terms of the movement Through the subtle channels, those channels have two openings. {{note:{index:313,id:UT22084-079-008-1252}}} At the time of their convergence, One can perceive the deity there. {6.1.23}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1253}} “There is the upper opening and the lower one. Through the lower one courses consciousness, And through the upper, the elements. {6.1.24}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1254}} “The practitioner, having brought together all the channels, Should visualize it {{note:{index:314,id:UT22084-079-008-1255}}} entering. The vajrin is continuously present At the upper opening of one’s body. {6.1.25} {{page:{number:76,folio:F.111.a}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1256}} “In the upper opening {{note:{index:315,id:UT22084-079-008-1257}}} there is a triple mechanism Surrounded by nine openings.” {6.1.26}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1258}} [The goddess asked], “O Blessed One, to what does triple mechanism refer? Why and how is mind always in motion?” {6.1.27}
The Blessed One said:
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1260}} “There are three mechanisms, hence a triple mechanism, Established as threefold in terms of its parts. Having the nature of body, speech, and mind, There are lesser, middling, and superior functions, respectively. {6.1.28}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1261}} “The body has one thick pillar, the ninefold door, And five presiding deities. {{note:{index:316,id:UT22084-079-008-1262}}} This door is the nine orifices, Therefore it is proclaimed to be ninefold. {6.1.29}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1263}} “The lower opening is that of the body— It is thick and fashioned by deities. Because of his mental faculty, a man is exceptional, Meaning that he is a practitioner. {{note:{index:317,id:UT22084-079-008-1264}}} {6.1.30}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1265}} “The movement is distinguished by motion, {{note:{index:318,id:UT22084-079-008-1266}}} Regularly, at every moment. Thus, in the case of monopeds, Bipeds, and quadrupeds, {6.1.31}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1267}} “Movement is always typified By the types of wind belonging to them. The wind is fourfold; The mind’s mode of resting is twofold. {{note:{index:319,id:UT22084-079-008-1268}}} {6.1.32}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1269}} “Through the process of dissolving and circulating the winds, the resting of dissolving and the motion of circulating will always extend to all beings. He who does not know that is mindless, unexceptional, and unintelligent, meaning that he is not a practitioner. {{note:{index:320,id:UT22084-079-008-1270}}} {6.1.33}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1271}} “In the southeast, the northeast, The east, and the west Are cakras, where mind’s movement Courses upward, toward the sides, straight, and downward. {{note:{index:321,id:UT22084-079-008-1272}}} {6.1.34}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1273}} “Following the division between the moon and the sun, The third opening is that of the mind. As it involves both entering and exiting, {{note:{index:322,id:UT22084-079-008-1274}}} This is the most exalted opening. {6.1.35}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1275}} “It is the main one, the supreme opening, Said to be directed both upward and downward. Consciousness moves through the lower opening, And the elements move through the upper. {6.1.36}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1276}} “The five buddhas—Vairocana, and so forth— Move toward and settle in the upper opening. They are situated below, But are requested to depart upward. {6.1.37}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1277}} “The mind always moves them By way of invitation and request to depart. {{page:{number:77,folio:F.111.b}}} All the buddhas of the three times And the ḍākinīs, the mothers of yogins, {6.1.38}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1278}} “Activate good and bad qualities When brought in and expelled, Their natures thus being pleasure and pain respectively. As an accomplished being, one will abide in the innate state.” {{note:{index:323,id:UT22084-079-008-1279}}} {6.1.39}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1280}} So spoke the blessed vajra holder, Vajrasattva, the great bliss. {{note:{index:324,id:UT22084-079-008-1281}}} {6.1.40}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1282}} Now, the goddess, having inserted The lord’s bola into her kakkola, Gratified the great being And spoke these words: {6.1.41}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1283}} “Why is your name Vasanta (Spring)? What is the characteristic of Tilakā (Ornament)? {{note:{index:325,id:UT22084-079-008-1284}}} How can there be a place for them For someone abiding in nonduality, and so forth? {{note:{index:326,id:UT22084-079-008-1285}}} {6.1.42}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1286}} “Explain to me how Pullīramalaya and the rest Are said to relate to the distribution of cakras and other entities. From what do the subtle energy channels emerge? Tell me what categories these entities fall into.” {{note:{index:327,id:UT22084-079-008-1287}}} {6.1.43}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1288}} The Blessed One said, “Listen, O goddess. I will now explain the ultimate secret of secrets. {6.1.44}
“The division of pīṭhas and other pilgrimage places, which correspond in their nature to the subtle channels, is said to be twenty-four-fold. They are found within the cakras of the body, speech, and mind of living beings. They are further linked to the ten bodhisattva levels and the ten perfections. {6.1.45}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1290}} “The head is the land of Malaya; The topknot is Jālandhara.’ Uḍḍiyāna, for its part, Is said to be in the right ear. {6.1.46}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1291}} “Arbuda is the backbone— These four are called pīṭha. Godāvarī is to be known As having the same nature as the left ear. {6.1.47}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1292}} “Rāmeśvara is said to be In the eye between the eyebrows. {{note:{index:328,id:UT22084-079-008-1293}}} Devīkoṭṭa is in the eyes, And Mālava at the base of the arms. {6.1.48}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1294}} “Those just mentioned are auxiliary pīṭhas — They are established in the cakra of the mind. Based on the specific nature of these places, They are said to belong to khecarīs. {6.1.49}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1295}} “Kāmarūpa is in the armpit; Oḍra is proclaimed to be on the breasts. These two are described as kṣetra. {{note:{index:329,id:UT22084-079-008-1296}}} The navel is thought to be Triśakuni. {6.1.50}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1297}} “Kośala is the tip of the nose. These last two are called auxiliary kṣetras. {{page:{number:78,folio:F.112.a}}} Kaliṅga is said to be the mouth, And Lampāka, the throat. {6.1.51}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1298}} “These two are called chandoha. Kāñci is said to be in the heart; The phallus is Himālaya. Thse two are called auxiliary chandohas . {6.1.52}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1299}} “All these places just mentioned Are situated in the cakra of speech. Owing to the specifications of such places, They are said to belong to bhūcarīs. {6.1.53}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1300}} “Pretādhivāsinī is in the sexual organ, While Gṛhadevatā is in the anus— These two are melāpakas. Saurāṣṭra is said to be in the thighs, {6.1.54}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1301}} “While the two shanks are said To have the nature of Suvarṇadvīpa. The last two are auxiliary melāpakas. Nagara is known to be in the fingers; {6.1.55}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1302}} “Sindhu, on the back of the feet— These two are called charnel ground. The thumb is said to be Maru, And the knees, Kulatā. {6.1.56}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1303}} “The last two are called Auxiliary charnel ground by the ḍākinīs. {{note:{index:330,id:UT22084-079-008-1304}}} All these are places and they are born with one’s own body— They are thus inside and outside oneself. {6.1.57}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1305}} “These are the places, within the cakras of the body, speech, and mind, That have a twenty-four-fold division. These places are always described As associated with all manner of ḍākinīs. {6.1.58}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1306}} “In these places dwell ḍākinīs In the form of subtle channels.” {6.1.59}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1307}} This concludes the first part of the sixth chapter.
Part 2
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1308}} “Now I will explain the cakras of subtle channels according to their location in the body of a tathāgata, one that is present in every being. {{note:{index:331,id:UT22084-079-008-1309}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1310}} “The lotus cakra in the center of the chest Has eight petals and a pericarp. The channel located in its center Has the appearance of the flame of an oil lamp. {6.2.1}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1311}} “It extends and faces down, Like a plantain flower. At its center dwells the virile one (Heruka), The size of a mustard seed. {6.2.2}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1312}} “He has the form of the indestructible seed syllable hūṁ, Which flows and has the color of snow. He is called Vasanta because, like spring, He brings joy to the hearts of embodied beings. {6.2.3}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1313}} “Nairātmyā, who has the appearance of vaḍabāgni fire, Is known as Tilakā. Fanned by the wind of karma, {{page:{number:79,folio:F.112.b}}} She blazes in the navel cakra. {6.2.4}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1314}} “Having reached Vasanta, she is gratified, And becomes established in meditative absorption. He is the glorious Heruka, the virile one; He is known as Vasantatilakā. {6.2.5}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1315}} “Taking the form of a yoginī, He is present in the animate and the inanimate. While the winds emerge through the three types of openings, According to their division into body, speech, and mind, {6.2.6}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1316}} “He enacts the goings and comings. He dwells in everyone’s body. In the navel he takes the form of the letter a, Which is said to be short. {6.2.7}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1317}} “In the heart, he abides as the syllable hūṁ, Which is two measures long. In the throat he has the form of the syllable oṁ, Which is said to be three measures long. {6.2.8}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1318}} “In the forehead he has the form of the syllable haṁ; He is a sound and an indestructible drop. According to his distribution between the cakras, He is the earth and the remaining great elements. {6.2.9}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1319}} “Presiding over the four temporal junctures, He emerges in each of the four lotuses. Being the essence of the four joys, He is wholly immersed in the practice of the four yogas. {{note:{index:332,id:UT22084-079-008-1320}}} {6.2.10}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1321}} “One in nature with the supreme joy, He assumes the modes of both the action and its agent. {{note:{index:333,id:UT22084-079-008-1322}}} In the form of Vajrasattva He plays as he pleases in this {{note:{index:334,id:UT22084-079-008-1323}}} body. {6.2.11}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1324}} “On the four petals in the four directions Are situated The subtle channels of the four elements, Resembling oil lamp flames. {6.2.12}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1325}} “In the intermediate quarters There are four subtle channels that extend to the other four. They convey the five {{note:{index:335,id:UT22084-079-008-1326}}} ambrosias And assume forms particular to their respective types of worship. {6.2.13}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1327}} “As they take on their respective forms They are described as the four types of worship. Accordingly, the heart center of the body Has five {{note:{index:336,id:UT22084-079-008-1328}}} subtle channels situated in it. {6.2.14}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1329}} “With the division into body, speech, and mind, There are said to be twenty-four subtle channels. They are each situated in their particular places, Following the divisions of pīṭhas, and so forth. {6.2.15}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1330}} “The channels that originate in the head Are known as head-born. The main ones among them are those With the natures of rajas, sattvam , and tamas , respectively. {{note:{index:337,id:UT22084-079-008-1331}}} {6.2.16}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1332}} “The one in Pullīra, {{note:{index:338,id:UT22084-079-008-1333}}} called Abhedyā, Is known to nourish the nails and teeth. The one in Jālandhara, called Sūkṣmarūpā, Nourishes the hair of the scalp and the body. {6.2.17} {{page:{number:80,folio:F.113.a}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1334}} “The one called Divyā {{note:{index:339,id:UT22084-079-008-1335}}} is situated In the great pīṭha of Uḍḍiyāna; Located in the right ear, She {{note:{index:340,id:UT22084-079-008-1336}}} nourishes the skin and its hair. {6.2.18}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1337}} “In Arbuda, the ḍākinī {{note:{index:341,id:UT22084-079-008-1338}}} Vāmā {{note:{index:342,id:UT22084-079-008-1339}}} Nourishes the flesh. The one that courses through the sinews and tendons Is situated in Godāvarī; {6.2.19}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1340}} “It is called Vāmanī And abides in a hard form. The one in Rāmeśvara Is commonly known as Kūrmajā; {6.2.20}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1341}} “Because of her hard form, She abides as a bone necklace. {{note:{index:343,id:UT22084-079-008-1342}}} The one in Devīkoṭṭa Has a soft form, and is called Bhāvikī; {6.2.21}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1343}} “She nourishes the heart {{note:{index:344,id:UT22084-079-008-1344}}} And is always present in every living body. {{note:{index:345,id:UT22084-079-008-1345}}} Sekā is in Mālava; Located in the heart, she is the queen of the victorious ones. {6.2.22}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1346}} “The one that nourishes the eyes Is situated in Kāmarūpa; It is called Dveṣāvatī {{note:{index:346,id:UT22084-079-008-1347}}} And is claimed to have a visible form. {6.2.23}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1348}} “The one in Oḍra carries bile; She is known as Mahāviṣṭā. Mātarā, born in Triśakuni, Is connected with the lungs. {6.2.24}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1349}} “The divine Śavarī, who wears a garland of intestines, Flows through Kośala. Śītadā is in Kaliṅga; She flows through the sides. {{note:{index:347,id:UT22084-079-008-1350}}} {6.2.25}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1351}} “Uṣmā, who resides in the abdomen, Is the one known [as present] in Lampāka. Pramāṇā, {{note:{index:348,id:UT22084-079-008-1352}}} who resides in Kāñcī, Always carries the feces. {6.2.26}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1353}} “Hṛṣṭavadanā, in Himālaya, Extends from the center of the body to the extremities. {{note:{index:349,id:UT22084-079-008-1354}}} Svarūpiṇī, located in Pretādhivāsinī, {{note:{index:350,id:UT22084-079-008-1355}}} Carries phlegm. {6.2.27}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1356}} “The one that always carries pus Is located in Gṛhadevatā— She is called Sāmānyā, The supreme goddess ḍākinī. {{note:{index:351,id:UT22084-079-008-1357}}} {6.2.28}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1358}} “The one that flows through Sauraṣṭra Is called Hetudāyikā and contains blood. The one that carries sweat Is located in Suvarṇadvīpa; {6.2.29}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1359}} “Turbulent {{note:{index:352,id:UT22084-079-008-1360}}} and with a flaming body, {{page:{number:81,folio:F.113.b}}} She is known as Viyogā. Premaṇī is in Nagara; She is thick with fat and also carries semen. {{note:{index:353,id:UT22084-079-008-1361}}} {6.2.30}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1362}} “In Sindhu there is Siddhā; She is thought to carry tears of grief. The one in Maru carries phlegm; She should go by the name Pāvakī. {6.2.31}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1363}} “Sumanā is in Kulatā; She carries saliva and snot.” {{note:{index:354,id:UT22084-079-008-1364}}} {6.2.32}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1365}} This concludes the second part of the sixth chapter on the placement of the sites.
Part 3
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1366}} [The goddess said,] “I would like to hear, O lord, how to perform the worship, and so forth, of the inner maṇḍala. I do not know the procedure for the burnt offering rite. Please explain it, O Great Bliss.” {6.3.1}
The Blessed One said:
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1368}} “Deities such as the herukas, and so forth, Exquisitely manifest in the form of the subtle channels. The body is a delightful maṇḍala, Which has four gates, as has been described. {6.3.2}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1369}} “Its eight pillars being the eight limbs of one’s body, The maṇḍala is always encircled by them. Because of the equality among all things, It is known to be symmetrical, with four sides. {6.3.3}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1370}} “Being in essence body, speech, and mind, respectively, The three cakras are said to be a single one. On the stamens of the lotus on top of one’s head, which is Mount Meru, There is Vairambhaka and the other three winds, in their right order. {6.3.4}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1371}} “This maṇḍala is present, having manifested Through the two stages, as handed down by the succession of gurus. On the soles of the feet there is the Vairambha wind In the shape of a bow. {6.3.5}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1372}} “Located in the triangular area of the abdomen Is the blazing triangle. The element of water, in the form of a circle, Is located in the abdomen. {6.3.6}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1373}} “In the heart area there is the earth element, Symmetrically quadrangular in form. The spinal column, with the form of a staff, Is just like Sumeru, the king of mountains. {6.3.7}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1374}} “On a lotus with thirty-two petals, Located in the area of the head, The vowels and consonants are exquisitely present— They are claimed to be the thirty-two-fold bodhicitta. {6.3.8}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1375}} “That which is in the center of the lotus Is, for its part, described as a moon disk. The brain inside the head Is what is said to be present there. {6.3.9}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1376}} “In its center is the syllable hūṁ, {{page:{number:82,folio:F.114.a}}} Indestructible, in the form of a drop of ambrosia. All beings have their foundation in this, As it is the mainstay of animate and inanimate entities. {6.3.10}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1377}} “Their existence is in the form of this seed syllable, Whether it takes manifest or unmanifest forms. The forms of all embodied beings Are therefore complete from the beginning. {6.3.11}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1378}} “It is present day and night, Dripping in the form of ambrosia. By this ambrosia alone is the ‘sound’ unleashed And the flame satisfied. {{note:{index:355,id:UT22084-079-008-1379}}} {6.3.12}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1380}} “The maṇḍala will become filled with it, There is no doubt about it. Only this can be called maṇḍala, Which is the ultimate essence of all things. {6.3.13}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1381}} “Since it gathers this essence, {{note:{index:356,id:UT22084-079-008-1382}}} The maṇḍala is thought to be the body. The maṇḍala is thus thought to be The network of thirty-two primary subtle channels. {6.3.14}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1383}} “This very maṇḍala is the essence— The great jewel of bodhicitta. In its outer and inner aspects, It is present pervading everything. {6.3.15}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1384}} “The outer aspect constitutes the range of engagement Of all the sense faculties in forms, sounds, and the rest, While the inner one is present as The ‘fulfilled’ substances, {{note:{index:357,id:UT22084-079-008-1385}}} such as semen, and so forth. {6.3.16}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1386}} “By means of these outer and inner aspects In their coarse and subtle forms, {{note:{index:358,id:UT22084-079-008-1387}}} respectively— Their essence being the bodhicitta of the followers Of the vajra path in their roles of the world’s kinsmen, {{note:{index:359,id:UT22084-079-008-1388}}} {6.3.17}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1389}} “The bodhicitta taught in support of the pledge To become a buddha or a bodhisattva— Awakening can be attained in this very life, Thanks to this very maṇḍala. {{note:{index:360,id:UT22084-079-008-1390}}} {6.3.18}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1391}} “Through this maṇḍala will also come The final {{note:{index:361,id:UT22084-079-008-1392}}} attainments of the hearers, Solitary buddhas, and gods, Such as Brahmā, and so forth. {6.3.19}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1393}} “One should perform a burnt offering with appropriate substances— The inner ones, such as semen, and so forth, And the outer ones, like the aggregate of form and the rest— Offering them in a blazing fire of insight. {6.3.20}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1394}} “Based on the specificities of the six sense-fields, The elements, the aggregates, and so forth, They have the nature of deities, And likewise, ḍākinīs. {6.3.21} {{page:{number:83,folio:F.114.b}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1395}} “The inner worship ( yogapūjā ) is said to consist of these, For they are offered by the practitioner in worship. The skull of one’s own head Is said to be the vessel for burnt offerings. {6.3.22}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1396}} “Rasanā (the right channel) is said to be the sacrificial sruva ladle; Lalanā (the left channel), at the heart cakra, has the nature of the sruk ladle; {{note:{index:362,id:UT22084-079-008-1397}}} The mouth is averred to be the sacrificial plate, {{note:{index:363,id:UT22084-079-008-1398}}} While the sacrificial fire pit is located in the hollow of the navel. {6.3.23}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1399}} “The brahmanical fire, fanned by activating winds, Is located at the triangle of the abdomen. The sound of the winds is said to be the mantra, While their cycling is the repetition. {6.3.24}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1400}} “The appearances in such meditation Reflect the practice of the nondual maṇḍala. Mounted upon the innate nature, this is, accordingly, The maṇḍala, and so forth, of the victorious ones. {6.3.25}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1401}} “The teacher is the sovereign mind, According to his nature of being the lord of the maṇḍala. He should therefore understand everything in this tantra Just as explained, starting from ‘Thus.’ ” {6.3.26}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1402}} [The goddess said:]
“I am still unclear how the lord sports in the forms Of dharmakāya, sambhogakāya, nirmāṇakāya, and great bliss. I do not know the categories. Please tell me, O Great Bliss.” {6.3.27}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1404}} The Blessed One said:
“The two cakras located at the head and at the navel Each contain the shape of the letter e. {{note:{index:364,id:UT22084-079-008-1406}}} Those, on the other hand, that are in the heart and the throat Bear a semblance to the syllable vaṁ. {{note:{index:365,id:UT22084-079-008-1407}}} {6.3.28}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1408}} “The cakra located at the navel Is a lotus with sixty-four petals. The one inside the head Is a lotus with thirty-two petals. {6.3.29}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1409}} “The one inside the neck Is a lotus with sixteen petals, And the one in the heart Is known to be a lotus with eight petals. {6.3.30}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1410}} “The nirmāṇakāya is said to be In the one with sixty-four petals, Whereas the dharmakāya abides {{note:{index:366,id:UT22084-079-008-1411}}} In the lotus with eight great petals. {6.3.31}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1412}} “The sambhogakāya abides in the lotus with sixteen petals, Whereas in the one with thirty-two petals, Great bliss, as great gnosis, Is situated throughout. {6.3.32}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1413}} “In the center of the nirmāṇa cakra there is, Surrounded by the eight classes of letters, That supreme syllable—the letter a — Which occupies the foremost position among all letters. {{note:{index:367,id:UT22084-079-008-1414}}} {6.3.33} {{page:{number:84,folio:F.115.a}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1415}} “In the cakra of the dharmakāya There is the celebrated syllable hūṁ , thought to be indestructible. It appears in combination with five vowels, And is adorned with ya, ra, la , and va . {6.3.34}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1416}} “In the center of the sambhoga cakra There is the syllable oṁ , which illuminates all letters. It is surrounded on all sides By sixteen letters in sets of four. {{note:{index:368,id:UT22084-079-008-1417}}} {6.3.35}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1418}} “In the exalted cakra of great bliss Is the syllable haṁ in the form of a drop. The sun and the moon are said to be On its left and right sides respectively. {6.3.36}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1419}} “In its section starting from the throat And ending at the center of the navel, The left channel (lalanā), associated with the sambhogakāya, Flows downward and carries semen. {6.3.37}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1420}} “The subtle channel that flows upward (rasanā), In its section starting from the navel And ending at the center of the neck, Is said to carry blood. {6.3.38}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1421}} “Semen is called moon; Blood is known as sun. Mounted upon the two openings, They are situated below and above respectively. {6.3.39}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1422}} “For these two, the moon and the sun, Are known as the duo of subtle channels That cause the going and the coming Of the virile ones and the ḍākinīs. {6.3.40}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1423}} “Their meaning is that of setting and rising, Similar to falling asleep and waking again. On the left and the right sides There are a dozen vowels. {{note:{index:369,id:UT22084-079-008-1424}}} {6.3.41}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1425}} “They are said to be facing upward And are surrounded by the syllables ka, kā, {{note:{index:370,id:UT22084-079-008-1426}}} and so forth. The vowels are joined with these downward-facing consonants, Which have been moved from the sides to the center. {{note:{index:371,id:UT22084-079-008-1427}}} {6.3.42}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1428}} “The syllable kṣa , which is called rākṣasa, Is situated in the lower region of the body. {{note:{index:372,id:UT22084-079-008-1429}}} When the moon (bodhicitta) is present in the throat cakra In its mode of intense passion, {{note:{index:373,id:UT22084-079-008-1430}}} {6.3.43}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1431}} “It is then called sambhogakāya, The supreme body of buddhas. It is so called also when it is at the tip of the [lotus] protuberance, Having reached the tip of the vajra. {{note:{index:374,id:UT22084-079-008-1432}}} {6.3.44}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1433}} “When the sambhogakāya Has reached the end of its path And fallen into the bhaga, It is known as mustard seed. {{note:{index:375,id:UT22084-079-008-1434}}} {6.3.45}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1435}} “It is then said to have the nature of the sun And is called nirmāṇakāya. {{page:{number:85,folio:F.115.b}}} It is by way of this nirmāṇakāya That the manifestation of buddhas and bodhisattvas are born. {6.3.46}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1436}} “In that setting sun, In the form of nirmāṇakāya, Resides the king Padmanarteśvara, In union with the lotus which was caused to open its petals. {6.3.47}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1437}} “When that, which is then called perfect bodhicitta, Becomes the pure embryonic lump, It is cut off from the paths of cyclic existence And is the auspicious state of the cessation of conceptual thinking. {6.3.48}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1438}} “Nondual and ultimately pure, It is the nature of glorious Vajrasattva Called glorious Heruka, Present in the tantras as a worm. {{note:{index:376,id:UT22084-079-008-1439}}} {6.3.49}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1440}} “He is established in the three tantras As a burst of laughter, a glance, or a handshake, respectively.
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1441}} He abides as a worm, Consuming both passion and dispassion.” {6.3.50}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1442}} This concludes the third part of the sixth chapter on the subtle channel conjunctions which constitute the concealed essence of the ḍākinīs’ net.
Part 4
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1443}} Then the great bodhisattvas, headed by Vajragarbha, with the yoginī Nairātmyā, and so forth, among them, spoke thus:
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1444}} “Please teach us the way to meditate On the circle of deities according to the order of their arising And, in particular, the special circle of ḍākinīs And their secret code-language, {6.4.1}
“As well as the concealed essence, which you mentioned before.” {{note:{index:377,id:UT22084-079-008-1446}}} {6.4.2}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1445}} The Blessed One said:
“The concealed essence is located in the center Of the yoginī’s body in the form of the letter a. That secret essence is said to be the same In both its external and internal forms. {6.4.3}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1449}} “The pleasure derived from the bola is the mahāmudrā; The abode of the vajra {{note:{index:378,id:UT22084-079-008-1450}}} is the means. {{note:{index:379,id:UT22084-079-008-1451}}} The external coupling is explained As this secret combination. {{note:{index:380,id:UT22084-079-008-1452}}} {6.4.4}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1453}} “The three bodies are said to reside within the body In the form of the three cakras. The cakra of great bliss is understood In terms of fully cognizing the three bodies. {6.4.5}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1454}} “There is dharmakāya, sambhogakāya, and nirmāṇakāya, As well as the body of great bliss. The three bodies are situated Within the womb , the heart, and the throat. {6.4.6}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1455}} “Wherever any beings Are said to come into existence, {{page:{number:86,folio:F.116.a}}} There is the creation of the nirmāṇakāya, For this creation is constant and broad. {{note:{index:381,id:UT22084-079-008-1456}}} {6.4.7}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1457}} “Phenomena are the nature of mind {{note:{index:382,id:UT22084-079-008-1458}}} And the body of phenomena (dharmakāya) is in the heart. The sambhogakāya is said to be The enjoyment of the six types of flavors. {6.4.8}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1459}} “As it {{note:{index:383,id:UT22084-079-008-1460}}} is firmly rooted in all phenomena, Everything has its nature. The sambhogakāya cakra is in the neck, While the cakra of great bliss is in the head. {6.4.9}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1461}} “The result corresponding to its cause is in the syllables e-vaṁ; {{note:{index:384,id:UT22084-079-008-1462}}} The fully matured result is in the cakra of the dharmakāya; The result consisting of valiant effort is in the cakra of the sambhogakāya; And the stainless result is in the cakra of great bliss. {6.4.10}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1463}} “The result is said to be fourfold, Following the division of the result corresponding with its cause, and the rest. The partaker in karmic results is the lady Wisdom herself, When she is stirred by the karmic winds. {6.4.11}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1464}} “The Sthāvarī division (nikāya) of the canon is in the cakra of nirmāṇakāya, Since the nirmāṇa creation is constant and enduring ( sthāvara ). {{note:{index:385,id:UT22084-079-008-1465}}} The Sarvāstivāda school is in the cakra of dharmakāya, For the doctrine ( dharma ) is born from speech ( vāda ). {{note:{index:386,id:UT22084-079-008-1466}}} {6.4.12}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1467}} “The Saṃvidī {{note:{index:387,id:UT22084-079-008-1468}}} school is in the cakra of the sambhogakāya, For experiencing ( saṃvid ) is based in the throat. The Mahāsāṃghika school is in the cakra of great bliss, For the great bliss is located in the head. {6.4.13}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1469}} “The mother’s body is said to be the congregation of monks; The mother’s belly is the monastery. Inside the womb, the embryo is the renunciant; The embryo’s membrane is the flame-colored robe. {6.4.14}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1470}} “One’s mother is one’s teacher; Folding one’s hands at the head {{note:{index:388,id:UT22084-079-008-1471}}} is the salutation. Worldly activity is the abiding by rules of conduct; The sound of breathing ( a-ham ) {{note:{index:389,id:UT22084-079-008-1472}}} is the mantra recitation. {6.4.15}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1473}} “In this way a monk is born—muttering this mantra, Naked, and with bald head and face. With such attributes, there is no doubt That all beings are buddhas. {6.4.16}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1474}} “The ten months of pregnancy are the ten stages, And the beings in the womb are the lords of the ten stages. Referred to by the name semen , a buddha is implanted In the bhaga of a queen , which is the realm of Sukhāvatī. {6.4.17}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1475}} “Without him—the semen—there would be no bliss, And without bliss, he—the semen—would not arise. So, since these two are ineffective without each other, In the case of impotence, the bliss can be generated through deity yoga. {6.4.18}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1476}} “Consequently, buddhas are neither entities, Nor are they non-entities. They possess a form with arms and face, {{page:{number:87,folio:F.116.b}}} But in terms of the ultimate bliss, they are formless. {6.4.19}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1477}} “Therefore, all beings are the innate condition; The innate condition is said to be their very nature. With the mind in a purified form, This nature is nirvāṇa. {6.4.20}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1478}} “Union with the form of the deity Is established as soon as one is born Based on having a face, hands, color, and shape, But including also base predispositions from the past. {6.4.21}
“In this way, O goddess, is explained {{note:{index:390,id:UT22084-079-008-1480}}} the usurpassable among all unions.” {{note:{index:391,id:UT22084-079-008-1481}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1482}} Then all the goddesses, headed by Nairātmyā, including Locanā, Māmakī, Pāṇḍaravāsinī, Tārā, Bhṛkuṭī, Cundā, Parṇaśavarī, Ahomukhā and Śaṃvarī—yoginīs as numerous as the dust particles on Mount Sumeru—became utterly bewildered, fainting and trembling. {6.4.22}
At that moment, all the tathāgatas, headed by Akṣobhya, said this: “May the Blessed One please resuscitate all the hosts of yoginīs.” {6.4.23}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1484}} Then, having entered the meditative absorption called the “vajra conquering all ignorance,” {{note:{index:392,id:UT22084-079-008-1485}}} the lord revived all the yoginīs and said: {{note:{index:393,id:UT22084-079-008-1486}}} {6.4.24}
“Sentient beings are buddhas, But they are sullied by adventitious defilements. When these defilements are removed, they become buddhas. This is so, O Blessed One and other sons of noble family. {{note:{index:394,id:UT22084-079-008-1488}}} {6.4.25}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1489}} “If an ordinary man were to eat poison in ignorance He would fall unconscious. But if he were free from delusion, Then knowing the truth would neutralize his affliction. {6.4.26}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1490}} “One who knows the true nature of poison Can overcome poison with poison, Using a potion that would kill All other creatures. {6.4.27}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1491}} “Similarly, someone afflicted by flatulence Is given a dish of beans, For flatulence is killed by flatulence After administering a medicine that seems counterproductive. {6.4.28}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1492}} “Conditioned existence is purified by conditioned existence, {{page:{number:88,folio:F.117.a}}} And concepts are removed by concepts. Just as water that has gotten inside the ear Is extracted with more water, {6.4.29}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1493}} “So too are concepts about entities Purified with entity-forms of the deity. {{note:{index:395,id:UT22084-079-008-1494}}} Just as those who have been burned by fire Apply fire once more as a sudorific, {6.4.30}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1495}} “So too those burned by the fire of passions Apply the sudorific of the fire of passion. Any savage act that binds Its perpetrator by karma {6.4.31}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1496}} “Can, in and of itself, when conjoined with skillful means, Release him from the fetters of conditioned existence. People are bound by passion, And only by passion are they released. {6.4.32}
