{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1497}} “This inverted meditation Is unknown to orthodox Buddhists or tīrthikas. In sexual play there are five types of enjoyment Corresponding to the five elements. {6.4.33}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1498}} “What is a single great delight Becomes fivefold when the categories are applied. The solidity (earth element) is experienced Through the touch felt when bola and kakkola unite. {6.4.34}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1499}} “Because the solidity has the quality of delusion, Delusion is regarded as Vairocana. Since bodhicitta is liquid, This liquid is regarded as the water element. {6.4.35}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1500}} “Since water has the nature of Akṣobhya, Hatred is the guide Akṣobhya. When the two organs are united in mutual rubbing Heat is always born. {6.4.36}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1501}} “This heat of passion is the vajra state of Amitābha, For passion is born within heat. The semen-consciousness deposited in the kakkola Has the nature of wind. {6.4.37}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1502}} “This movement of envy is Amoghasiddhi, For Amogha is born from wind. Pleasure is the impassioned mind— The jewel with the characteristics of space. {{note:{index:396,id:UT22084-079-008-1503}}} {6.4.38}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1504}} “Space is the vajra quality of backbiting, {{note:{index:397,id:UT22084-079-008-1505}}} For backbiting {{note:{index:398,id:UT22084-079-008-1506}}} is born from space. The one great semen-consciousness Is thus characterized by these five aspects. {6.4.39}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1507}} “Arisen within the five families, They are multiplied therein by the thousand. Still, their nature is but single— The unending, ultimate bliss. {{note:{index:399,id:UT22084-079-008-1508}}} {6.4.40}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1509}} “This bliss, however, becomes fivefold according to the division Into the five mental states of passion, and so forth. {6.4.41} {{page:{number:89,folio:F.117.b}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1510}} “Within each of the five families there are multitudes of tathāgatas, Equal in number to the grains of sand in ten Ganges Rivers. Within each of these great families there are many families, And within each of these families there are many hundreds more families. {6.4.42}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1511}} “These too are big, containing hundreds of thousands of families, Which have tens of millions, which in turn become innumerable. Within each of these families there are further innumerable families— All of them arise from the family of the supreme joy.”
So spoke [Vajrasattva]. {6.4.43}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1513}} [The goddess asked,] “How can all this be contained in the form of a globule the size of a particle?” {{note:{index:400,id:UT22084-079-008-1514}}} {6.4.44}
The Blessed One said:
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1516}} “It is so because many buddhas can fit in the space of a hair’s width, Without crowding or causing inconvenience to one another. {{note:{index:401,id:UT22084-079-008-1517}}} {6.4.45}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1518}} “Rise, rise, O deities, replete with the ten powers, Who wish to feast in my house, And you, sons of the buddha families, who appear through your miraculous powers. {{note:{index:402,id:UT22084-079-008-1519}}} {6.4.46}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1520}} “Listen, O goddess, as I will now teach The characteristics of the emergence from sampuṭa. {6.4.47}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1521}} “The word rahasye abides in the element earth; {{note:{index:403,id:UT22084-079-008-1522}}} Parame , in the element water; Ramye , in the element called fire; And sarvātmani abides in wind. {6.4.48}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1523}} “The phrase sadā sthitaḥ expresses The saṃvara identity {{note:{index:404,id:UT22084-079-008-1524}}} of all buddhas, Always present in the form of mirror-like wisdom, The wisdom of equality, {6.4.49}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1525}} “The wisdom of clear discrimination, Or the wisdom accomplishing all actions. The phrase sadā sthitaḥ thus conveys The nature of impeccable purity. {6.4.50}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1526}} “It is thus always present as Vairocana. {{note:{index:405,id:UT22084-079-008-1527}}} When it is always present as Amoghasiddhi, It could be in the form of Ratnasaṃbhava, Or perhaps Amitābha. {{note:{index:406,id:UT22084-079-008-1528}}} {6.4.51}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1529}} “It is a drop made of the five ambrosias, Consisting in its nature purely of mind. It is also pristine great gnosis, The nature of all female deities. {6.4.52}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1530}} “It is called Vajrasattva And is declared to be the ultimate bliss. Its self-existing nature, however, Is known as the dharmakāya. {6.4.53}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1531}} “This Vajrasattva possesses innate wisdom, Prajñā, {{page:{number:90,folio:F.118.a}}} Established by her nature as part of him. She is fanned by the activating winds And blazes in the area of the navel. {{note:{index:407,id:UT22084-079-008-1532}}} {6.4.54}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1533}} “She is called Nairātmyā, Also known as Vasantatilakā. Her body consists of hundreds of thousands of points of light As dazzling as a massive flash of lightning. {6.4.55}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1534}} “During deity yoga practice, however, These points of light come out Through the pores of one’s skin into the ten directions, Threatening all the gods and demigods. {6.4.56}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1535}} “Having blazed in the dharmakāya cakra at the chest, The rays of light reach the cakra of the sambhogakāya. They then exit through the right nostril, Radiating all around. {6.4.57}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1536}} “Coming out also through the opening located at one’s crown, The light rays radiate throughout the ten directions, Entering the buddhas and bodhisattvas Through their left nostrils. {6.4.58}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1537}} “The light rays then enter the cakra at the top of their heads; Having set their cakra ablaze with light, [Nairātmyā] should withdraw and re-enter the practitioner Through the previously mentioned opening at the crown. {6.4.59}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1538}} “While all the buddhas are being burned up, She will cause bliss to arise. Finally, having returned to the area of the navel, She will abide there as before.” {6.4.60}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1539}} This concludes the sovereign chapter called Vasantatilakā, the sixth in the great tantra, the “ Emergence from Sampuṭa .”
Chapter 7
Part 1
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1540}} [Vajragarbha said:]
“I want to hear, O Blessed One, The description of secret code words. What can be said about this twilight language? Please speak conclusively, O Blessed One, {7.1.1}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1542}} “About this great pledge {{note:{index:408,id:UT22084-079-008-1543}}} of the yoginīs That cannot be deciphered by the hearers and others. With the smiling, glancing, Embracing, coupling, and so forth, {7.1.2}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1544}} “This twilight language has not been taught Even in the four divisions of tantra.”
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1545}} [The Blessed One said:]
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1546}} “I will teach it, Vajragarbha; Please listen with undivided attention. {7.1.3}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1547}} “The great language called twilight language Is an extensive list of pledge signs. {{note:{index:409,id:UT22084-079-008-1548}}} Amorous intoxication stands for ‘wine,’ strength for ‘meat,’ And sandalwood for ‘meeting.’ {7.1.4}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1549}} “ Phlegm {{note:{index:410,id:UT22084-079-008-1550}}} stands for ‘going,’ shelter for ‘corpse,’ And nudity for ‘bone ornament.’ Swing {{note:{index:411,id:UT22084-079-008-1551}}} is said to mean ‘arriving,’ And fuel {{note:{index:412,id:UT22084-079-008-1552}}} is known to stand for ‘hand drum.’ {7.1.5}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1553}} “ Dundura drum {{note:{index:413,id:UT22084-079-008-1554}}} is said to mean ‘unworthy,’ {{page:{number:91,folio:F.118.b}}} And Kāliñjara mountain {{note:{index:414,id:UT22084-079-008-1555}}} stands for ‘worthy.’ Diṇḍima drum stands for ‘untouchable,’ And lotus vessel for ‘skull.’ {7.1.6}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1556}} “ Satisfying should be known to stand for ‘food,’ And jasmine wood for ‘herbs.’ Four ingredients {{note:{index:415,id:UT22084-079-008-1557}}} is said to mean ‘feces,’ And musk , ‘urine.’ {7.1.7}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1558}} “ Frankincense is known to mean ‘blood,’ And camphor is known to mean ‘semen.’ Rice product is said to mean ‘human meat,’ And olibanum {{note:{index:416,id:UT22084-079-008-1559}}} means ‘union of the two sexual organs.’ {7.1.8}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1560}} “ Vajra is said to mean ‘male sexual organ,’ And lotus , ‘female sexual organ.’ {7.1.9}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1561}} “Placing the finger on the mouth Is the sign of Ḍākinī. The code word is muku. {{note:{index:417,id:UT22084-079-008-1562}}} Placing folded hands at the forehead Is the sign of Dīpinī. The code word is ghoghu. {{note:{index:418,id:UT22084-079-008-1563}}} {7.1.10}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1564}} “Pressing the thumb Is the sign of Cūṣiṇī. The code word is gughu. Tapping on the ears with the hands Is the sign of Kambojī. The code word is mughu . {7.1.11}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1565}} “Tapping on the tip of one’s nose with the palm of the hand, {{note:{index:419,id:UT22084-079-008-1566}}} One will inquire about a person’s well-being. The code word is lughu. The practitioner of Yogatantra should also display the ‘head of a deer,’ Giving to this hand gesture his full attention. {{note:{index:420,id:UT22084-079-008-1567}}} The code word for this is draṣṭa . {7.1.12}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1568}} “Further, the word ḍā {{note:{index:421,id:UT22084-079-008-1569}}} denotes a man; ḍī , a woman; pu, {{note:{index:422,id:UT22084-079-008-1570}}} the magic of paralyzing; su , eating; mā , mother; yo , wife; bhi , younger sister; dhī, {{note:{index:423,id:UT22084-079-008-1571}}} female friend; lu , daughter; strī, {{note:{index:424,id:UT22084-079-008-1572}}} menstrual blood; sa , drinking soma; pe , (alcoholic?) drink; phī, {{note:{index:425,id:UT22084-079-008-1573}}} meat; bha , eating; bhū , meeting; pī, {{note:{index:426,id:UT22084-079-008-1574}}} charnel ground; bhu , a corpse; dī, {{note:{index:427,id:UT22084-079-008-1575}}} a yoginī; ga , the goddess Lāmā; tri, {{note:{index:428,id:UT22084-079-008-1576}}} the goddess Rūpiṇī; ku , the goddess Ḍākinī; kha , the goddess Khaṇḍarohā; ja , the pair of knees; ke , the pair of arms; bha , reverential salutation; and sva, {{note:{index:429,id:UT22084-079-008-1577}}} an act of welcome. {7.1.13}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1578}} “These, which are code words with a single syllable each, will be understood by the virile ones and their sisters. {{note:{index:430,id:UT22084-079-008-1579}}} This is the art of the pledge seals consisting of syllables.” {7.1.14}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1581}} Vajragarbha said:
“I do not know the meanings of some coded expressions. Please explain them, O Great Bliss.” {7.1.15} {{page:{number:92,folio:F.119.a}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1583}} The Blessed One said:
“I will now teach it briefly, So please listen to my words. Potāṅgī {{note:{index:431,id:UT22084-079-008-1584}}} is a greeting; Potāṅgī given {{note:{index:432,id:UT22084-079-008-1585}}} in response is a greeting returned. {7.1.16}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1586}} “The word gamu expresses the notion ‘I go’; the word lumba , ‘I come’; the word swallowing , the notion ‘please give’; wooden vessel , ‘please take’; heart , ‘hero’; descendant of Kuru , ‘killing’; earring , ‘bell’; alikaraṇa , ‘head’; boar , ‘hair’; hearing , ‘ear’; churning , ‘ambrosia’; man , ‘coming together’; palm of the hand , ‘ḍākinī’; hell , ‘maṇḍala’; such and such , ‘charnel ground’; kākhilā, {{note:{index:433,id:UT22084-079-008-1587}}} ‘door’; breathing , ‘brahmin’; enclosure , ‘kṣatriya’; cessation , ‘vaiśya’; cruel , ‘śūdra’; end, {{note:{index:434,id:UT22084-079-008-1588}}} ‘house of an untouchable’; {{note:{index:435,id:UT22084-079-008-1589}}} scorpio , ‘cattle’; younger sister , ‘ḍākinī’; mudaka , ‘fat’; gṛhāṇa , ‘gesture’; when one touches one’s teeth with the tongue , ‘hunger’; {{note:{index:436,id:UT22084-079-008-1590}}} fragrant with perfume , ‘thirst’; arrival , ‘where’; place , ‘such and such a person’; light ray , ‘flower’; hanging , ‘abdomen’; {{note:{index:437,id:UT22084-079-008-1591}}} teeth , ‘mirth’; cessation , ‘rain’; report , ‘satisfaction’; smoky , ‘clouds’; fond of smoking and summit , ‘mountains’; {{note:{index:438,id:UT22084-079-008-1592}}} streams , ‘rivers’; fingers , ‘part / portion’; mouth , ‘face’; washerwoman, {{note:{index:439,id:UT22084-079-008-1593}}} ‘tongue’; eating , ‘teeth’; row / series , ‘banner’; desire / intention , ‘garland’; movement , ‘wind’; lord of animals , ‘cattle’; circle , ‘evenness / equanimity’; breathing , ‘crossroads’; {{page:{number:93,folio:F.119.b}}} phālguṣa , ‘person’; and the great syllable ( oṁ ?), ‘great sacrificial victim.’ {{note:{index:440,id:UT22084-079-008-1594}}} {7.1.17}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1595}} “Further, the syllable chā {{note:{index:441,id:UT22084-079-008-1596}}} signifies a goat; nā, {{note:{index:442,id:UT22084-079-008-1597}}} a human being; go , an ox; ma , a buffalo; bhā , eating anywhere; {{note:{index:443,id:UT22084-079-008-1598}}} and hā, {{note:{index:444,id:UT22084-079-008-1599}}} a recurrence. The word apyakā {{note:{index:445,id:UT22084-079-008-1600}}} means ‘king’s men,’ and to remain , ‘the act of remaining.’ When one touches the mouth, {{note:{index:446,id:UT22084-079-008-1601}}} it means ‘I have eaten’; When one touches the teeth, it means ‘I am sated.’ The syllable ho means ‘recurrence.’ The word shame means ‘bashfulness.’ When one touches an empty space, this means, ‘Please have sex with me’; When one touches the thighs, this means, ‘Let’s do so quickly.’ {7.1.18}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1602}} “This concludes the section about the art of secret signs. {{note:{index:447,id:UT22084-079-008-1603}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1604}} “The gaze that brings downfall is said To always be even, with eyebrows furrowed in anger. {{note:{index:448,id:UT22084-079-008-1605}}} The enthralling gaze should be directed to the left, With both eyes looking at the effigy on the left side. {{note:{index:449,id:UT22084-079-008-1606}}} {7.1.19}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1607}} “In the summoning gaze, the effigy is on the right And the two eyes turned upward. {{note:{index:450,id:UT22084-079-008-1608}}} The paralyzing gaze is directed toward the center, With the two eyes directed at the bridge of the nose. {{note:{index:451,id:UT22084-079-008-1609}}} {7.1.20}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1610}} “For killing, the gaze should be level, {{note:{index:452,id:UT22084-079-008-1611}}} With the two eyes fixed at the tip of the nose. Causing downfall should be done while exhaling, And enthralling while holding the breath in. {{note:{index:453,id:UT22084-079-008-1612}}} {7.1.21}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1613}} “Summoning is done while inhaling, And paralyzing while holding the breath in. {{note:{index:454,id:UT22084-079-008-1614}}} While training, the gaze causing downfall should be directed at a pine tree, {{note:{index:455,id:UT22084-079-008-1615}}} And the enthralling gaze, at a flower. {7.1.22}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1616}} “The summoning gaze should be directed at a euphorbia, And the paralyzing gaze, at grass that is swaying. {{note:{index:456,id:UT22084-079-008-1617}}} One will succeed after six months of practice, There is no doubt about this. {7.1.23}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1618}} “One should not err in this practice. The powers of the Buddha are inconceivable. {7.1.24}
“The homage is paid and returned with the two ‘teachers’ present. {{note:{index:457,id:UT22084-079-008-1620}}} {7.1.25}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1621}} “If one employs the deity yoga of the glorious Vajrasattva or others and frowns with the right eyebrow, one will be successful, upon contemplating sky-travel, in rising into the air. If one frowns with the left eyebrow, victory over a hostile army will follow. With the same practice one will crush the forces of Māra. {{note:{index:458,id:UT22084-079-008-1622}}} {7.1.26}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1623}} “If one contemplates the form of Gaurī or other female deities and bats one’s left eye, one will be able to manifest their forms. {{page:{number:94,folio:F.120.a}}} If one contemplates the form of Vajrasattva or other male deities and bats one’s right eye, one will manifest their respective forms. {{note:{index:459,id:UT22084-079-008-1624}}} {7.1.27}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1625}} “Without an agreed convention of language, not even the well-established worldly usages would have any effect. {{note:{index:460,id:UT22084-079-008-1626}}} The same is the case with the yogic accomplishments in poetry and song, both mundane and supramundane. {{note:{index:461,id:UT22084-079-008-1627}}} {7.1.28}
“This concludes the section about the art of gaze-mudrās.
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1629}} “Assuming the form and shape of glorious Vajrasattva Consistent with being fully in union with him, One should place, as directed, Some mustard seeds in a human skull cup. {7.1.29}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1630}} “Additionally, he should eat a dish cooked in oil, And smear the head with the fruits. {{note:{index:462,id:UT22084-079-008-1631}}} This affords the best of all protections By binding earth and sky up to their farthest limits in the ten directions. {{note:{index:463,id:UT22084-079-008-1632}}} {7.1.30}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1633}} “Visualizing oneself as one with glorious Vajrasattva, Biting his lower lip and in union with his consort — The illustrious one proudly holding implements in his left hands And, with his right hands, displaying the circuit of the compass— {7.1.31}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1634}} “One should consecrate the space below and above And stamp one’s ‘seal’ on the earth and the atmosphere. Sealed, it becomes composed of all the buddhas And will confer accomplishments. {{note:{index:464,id:UT22084-079-008-1635}}} {7.1.32}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1636}} “One should place the following {{note:{index:465,id:UT22084-079-008-1637}}} in a bowl made of a brahmin’s skull or, as one’s second choice, any human skull. Aside from [a skull] of a woman, a man, a hermaphrodite, and so forth, [a skull] of a crow, an owl, a vulture, or a sparrow will produce various excellent {{note:{index:466,id:UT22084-079-008-1638}}} accomplishments. The procedure prescribes wild licorice root. Through this, one will be able to assume at will the fine form of an elephant or a horse, or, according to one’s wish, the form of an ox or a buffalo, or, should one wish it so, a dog, a cat, or a jackal. Depending on one’s wish, one can be a male or a female. {7.1.33}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1639}} “One can enter any being by censing oneself with black bdellium resin burned inside the mouth cavity of a corpse, with the fire from a cremation pyre, on the day of spirits, {{note:{index:467,id:UT22084-079-008-1640}}} during the waning period of the lunar month. By censing oneself as before with a mixture of equal parts thorn apple fruit, yellow arsenic, citrons, leadwort, sweet flag, and chicken eggs, {{note:{index:468,id:UT22084-079-008-1641}}} one can enter anywhere in the animate or inanimate worlds. {7.1.34} {{page:{number:95,folio:F.120.b}}}
“The root of white oleander, margosa, and grasshoppers, combined with a hundredth part of the venom from a scorpion’s stinger, {{note:{index:469,id:UT22084-079-008-1643}}} will, when applied to the hand, transform it into a gonāsa snake. {7.1.35}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1644}} “For seven days one should douse velvet bean pods and soak chalk with the milk from giant milkweed. When a drawing made with this chalk and velvet bean mixture is touched, one will become like the king of serpents, with poisonous hands. An antidote to the touch of these hands is explained as follows: {7.1.36}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1645}} “Sandal, mesua flower, costus root, and emetic nut, combined with Indian valerian, neutralize a variety of poisons. So does costus mixed with rice water. {{note:{index:470,id:UT22084-079-008-1646}}} Should one consume a pill consisting of the pith of Indian valerian, together with the feces {{note:{index:471,id:UT22084-079-008-1647}}} of a child born on that day, one will be able to drink poison as much as one likes, like Vajrapāṇi himself. {7.1.37}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1648}} “A touch from a hand smeared with a broth made with the fat of a frog and an earth boa snake, and with the fruit of sebesten tree, will remove poison. {7.1.38}
“An ointment made from ghee, sandal, peacock blood, and the bones and flesh of an earth boa snake, when applied to the body, {{note:{index:472,id:UT22084-079-008-1650}}} can detoxify even the entire triple universe upon contact. {7.1.39}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1651}} “The fever that recurs every four days will be cured if, while concentrating by means of the ritual procedure of getting naked, and the rest, one fastens to the hand on the day of spirits a root of fragrant swamp mellow broken into seven pieces. {7.1.40}
“By merely applying an incense composed of equal parts of newly shed skin from a large snake and peacock feathers, one will create enmity throughout the triple universe. {7.1.41}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1653}} “Alternatively, by merely burning an incense, according to procedure, composed of equal parts crow and owl feathers, one will actually cause enmity even among the supporters of Hara. {{note:{index:473,id:UT22084-079-008-1654}}} {7.1.42}
“When the head of a snake placed inside the hole of a horse’s hoof is buried together with the tongue of a mad dog underneath the door of the enemy’s house, he will be driven away after seven days. {7.1.43} {{page:{number:96,folio:F.121.a}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1656}} “Flame lily, pig feces, hair from the head of a corpse, and bones of a camel—this excellent method will send into exile, after seven days, even the entire triple universe. {{note:{index:474,id:UT22084-079-008-1657}}} {7.1.44}
“By smearing on a mirror flowers of red oleander, cashew nut, and mangosteen oil, the shapes of a horse, a donkey, a camel, and so forth, will be seen in it. {7.1.45}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1659}} “Through burning in a sealed duplex vessel the hooves and claws of a horse, a cow, a boar, a monkey, an ass, and a camel, mixed with frog fat, the forms of those creatures will be seen, as stipulated earlier. After anointing the eyes, during the asterism of Puṣya, {{note:{index:475,id:UT22084-079-008-1660}}} with alangium seed oil and cow’s milk, one will perceive in the mirror any forms present within the universe. {7.1.46}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1663}} “A person whose eyes are anointed with a paste of Indian valerian fruit and alangium oil will see ordinary people as divine forms. Through anointing his eyes with oil his vision will go back to normal. {{note:{index:476,id:UT22084-079-008-1662}}} {7.1.47}
“After anointing the feet with camphor, {{note:{index:477,id:UT22084-079-008-1664}}} powdered leech, frog fat, and root of the trumpet flower tree, one will be able to walk upon a heap of smoldering embers. {7.1.48}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1666}} “After smearing the hands and the feet with spikenard, frog fat, powdered leech, and cardamom, one will be able to make fire feel as cold as snow. {7.1.49}
“After taking blood of a water snake {{note:{index:478,id:UT22084-079-008-1667}}} into one’s mouth, the wise person will be able to enter water and remain there as long as he likes, as if inside a floating house. {{note:{index:479,id:UT22084-079-008-1668}}} {7.1.50}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1671}} “Should he put on a pair of shoes, having filled them with seeds of the broken bones plant, a person thus purified will be able to walk on water as if on a road. {{note:{index:480,id:UT22084-079-008-1670}}} {7.1.51}
“A wise person, after smearing all the orifices of his body with a paste made of freshly churned butter, gold dust, onion, {{note:{index:481,id:UT22084-079-008-1672}}} and fish oil, will be able to move in water like an alligator. {7.1.52}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1676}} “Seeds from a branch of thorn apple mixed with wood dust produced by woodworms, {{note:{index:482,id:UT22084-079-008-1674}}} together with female cuckoo birds, {{note:{index:483,id:UT22084-079-008-1675}}} will make a person like a ghost. {{page:{number:97,folio:F.121.b}}} This can be reversed by means of a molasses and rice gruel mixture. {7.1.53}

{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1679}} “The tail of a jackal, rightly conjoined with the right wing of a crow, when placed under the enemy’s bed will soon unleash upon him a terrifying apasmāra. {7.1.55}
“With thorn apple fruit, citron, and the [droppings of] pigeon, peacock, and chicken, one can instantly cause madness. The insanity will go away with the cutting of the victim’s hair. {7.1.56}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1681}} “One should take a thorn apple fruit and mix into it powdered woodworms with human flesh. {{note:{index:486,id:UT22084-079-008-1682}}} After adding this to the victim’s food and drink, he will immediately lose his mind and die after seven days. {7.1.57}
“One should take a crow’s nest from a neem tree with a hand on which white mustard oil has been rubbed. Using the same hand, {{note:{index:487,id:UT22084-079-008-1684}}} one should burn it together with a piece of wood obtained from a charnel ground and afterward retrieve the ashes. Whoever’s head is sprinkled with these ashes will be driven away. {7.1.58}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1685}} “One should combine the feather {{note:{index:488,id:UT22084-079-008-1686}}} of a crow and an owl, together with the hair of a brahmin and a naked mendicant, and light a fire using thorn apple wood. After burning these feathers and hair in a smokeless fire, one should retrieve some of the ashes and secretly throw them under the bed of two persons, men or women. Right at that moment the two will become enemies. {7.1.59}

When struck with it, even a woman loyal to her husband will be enthralled, if one mixes this powder with one’s own semen during the asterism of Puṣya. {{note:{index:491,id:UT22084-079-008-1691}}} {7.1.60}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1692}} “Placing in the hand of a virgin girl equal amounts of elephant rut and a paste from buds plucked by women from male trees will result in marriage and conjugal felicity. {{note:{index:492,id:UT22084-079-008-1693}}} {7.1.61}

{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1725}} “One will enthrall the people of the world with a tilaka well concocted from ‘glory sandalwood,’ {{note:{index:511,id:UT22084-079-008-1726}}} red sandalwood, and camphor, infused with equal parts of the blood of a wagtail and a female mule. {{note:{index:512,id:UT22084-079-008-1727}}} {7.1.74}

{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1731}} “Otherwise, if one wishes to make a magical pill, one should grind the impurities and the eyes {{note:{index:514,id:UT22084-079-008-1732}}} of a black cat and the eyes of a black crow together with the blood from the left ear of a black boar. The pill, which should also include an authentic relic of the tathāgatas, should then be wrapped in the aforementioned concoction, and then enclosed in ‘sun,’ ‘moon,’ and ‘fire.’ {{note:{index:515,id:UT22084-079-008-1733}}} In the asterism of Puṣya, the pill should be activated. {{note:{index:516,id:UT22084-079-008-1734}}} One will be successful by reciting the mantra of one’s chosen deity. When the pill is placed in the mouth, one can roam the earth assuming, like a yakṣa, any desired form. {7.1.76}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1735}} “Alternatively, one should make a pill with the eyes of a black pecikā owl, black crow, black ullūka owl, and black cuckoo, combined with an authentic relic of the tathāgatas. One should cover the pill in the milky sap of Indian spurge tree and wrap it in ‘sun,’ ‘moon,’ and ‘fire.’ {{note:{index:517,id:UT22084-079-008-1736}}} When this pill is placed in the mouth, one becomes invisible. {{note:{index:518,id:UT22084-079-008-1737}}} {7.1.77} {{page:{number:100,folio:F.123.a}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1738}} “Alternatively, in order to produce a pill consisting of a relic of the tathāgatas, one should grind together the ashes from the funeral pyre of a woman cremated with her deceased husband, powdered fruit of wood apple, and resin of white dammar, along with perspiration. An authentic relic of the tathāgatas should be wrapped in this concoction and enclosed in ‘sun,’ ‘moon,’ and ‘fire.’ {{note:{index:519,id:UT22084-079-008-1739}}} The pill should be activated during the asterism of Puṣya. When it is placed in the mouth, one will be able to roam the earth like a yakṣa, assuming any desired form. {{note:{index:520,id:UT22084-079-008-1740}}} {7.1.78}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1741}} “Alternatively, one should make a pill with an eye ointment called srotaḥ , camphor, spiky leaves of saffron crocus, honey, and the first blossom of the mahua tree, with added stamens of a young flame lily. {{note:{index:521,id:UT22084-079-008-1742}}} This pill, encased within the three metals of gold, silver, and copper, will make one invisible. {7.1.79}
“Alternatively, in a capsule made of the three metals of gold, silver, and copper should be placed sprouts of a blue aśoka tree {{note:{index:522,id:UT22084-079-008-1744}}} inuncted seven times with the blood of a beautiful woman. {{note:{index:523,id:UT22084-079-008-1745}}} Placing it in the mouth will conceal any being. {7.1.80}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1746}} “Alternatively, a pill made of the northern root of Indian valerian, dug out during a lunar eclipse while naked, should be encased in the metals of ‘sun,’ ‘moon,’ and ‘fire.’ If placed in the mouth, this pill will make one invisible. {7.1.81}
“A pill made from bovine orpiment and blossoms from the Indian almond tree, combined with the eyes and hair left behind by a crow who fed on the corpse of a girl who hung herself, is called ‘the lady who fulfills wishes.’ {{note:{index:524,id:UT22084-079-008-1748}}} {7.1.82}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1749}} “Alternatively, one should mix realgar with the discharge from rubbing a girl maddened by menstruation in an ancestor grove. {{note:{index:525,id:UT22084-079-008-1750}}} By applying a tilaka of this to the declivity in the center of one’s forehead, one will be able to hide from even the entire triple universe. {7.1.83}
“Alternatively, applying to the forehead a tilaka prepared with the twigs from a crow’s nest located on a northern branch of a blue aśoka tree will hide a man from all animate and inanimate beings. If srotaḥ eye ointment is placed in the abdomen of a pigeon, put in the fire of a funeral pyre, and cooked, the magical ointment will make one invisible. Re-appearance can be achieved by means of the blood of a black cat. {{note:{index:526,id:UT22084-079-008-1752}}} {7.1.84} {{page:{number:101,folio:F.123.b}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1753}} “Alternatively, earth pushed up by a tuft of young grass and mixed with a bee, along with its stinger, can make one invisible even to the adepts if it is prepared on the asterism of Puṣya, and a tilaka of it is applied to the forehead. {7.1.85}
“Alternatively, there is a pill superior even to that. Made with red arsenic and bovine orpiment, its effects surpass the uses explained before. {7.1.86}
“This concludes the section on the art of becoming invisible.
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1756}} “Now I will describe the rites involving magical ointment.
“One should make a lamp-wick out of cloth recovered from a charnel ground and saturate it with oil obtained from human {{note:{index:527,id:UT22084-079-008-1758}}} flesh. On the night of spirits, in the charnel ground, one should place the lighted lamp on a lotus petal [inside a woman’s skull] atop three other human skulls, and collect the lampblack that collects above, in the delightful lady’s skull. Then, after burning up an owl’s head and mixing it with red sandalwood many times, one should, that very night, prepare from this a fine powder by grinding it on a stone slab. One should then blend this powder with the earlier collected lampblack until the mixture is homogeneous, wrap that in the skin from a vulture’s foot, and with it fill the hollow of a bone from this foot using a splinter from a human bone. {{note:{index:528,id:UT22084-079-008-1759}}} Explaining how to activate this ointment, the lord said, ‘It can be activated inside a woman’s bhaga, by a follower of the Mantrayāna, according to prescribed procedure.’ {7.1.87}
“This is the art of concocting magical ointment.
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1761}} “Now I will teach the rites Known as the ritual procedure of quicksilver, Whereby practitioners attain success If they always delight in meditation and recitation. {7.1.88}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1762}} “If the procedure is not complete, Happiness cannot be brought to wretched beings. {{note:{index:529,id:UT22084-079-008-1763}}} {7.1.89}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1764}} “One should combine substances that come from mountains and oceans {{note:{index:530,id:UT22084-079-008-1765}}} with well-matured vinegar and quicksilver, and grind them together repeatedly in a sealed and heated stone crucible. One should always boil this concoction in a copper dish along with common milk hedge, butterfly pea, jasmine, and Indian caper, combined with fermented rice. Taking a metal [magnet], one should mix in its powder, and along with parts of safflower and large blue lotus, grind it with the vinegar concoction until it becomes the same consistency as freshly churned butter. Immediately thereafter, one should mix it with the sap of Indian spurge tree, and liquify it with sindhu and white borax. Then, it should be mixed together with half a karṣa each of copper and silver in a covered crucible, adding half the amount of sulphur crystals. From this, one will obtain gold measuring half the amount of the substrate. {7.1.90} {{page:{number:102,folio:F.124.a}}}
“This is about the art of quicksilver.
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1767}} “Now I will teach the rites of the art of longevity, giving an essential summary of everything. {7.1.91}
“Following the ritual restrictions with respect to seasons, one should practice yoga and mudrā. {{note:{index:531,id:UT22084-079-008-1769}}} One should employ the ‘four ingredients,’ {{note:{index:532,id:UT22084-079-008-1770}}} musk, red sandalwood, camphor, and śālija , and also olibanum, tailed pepper, and lotus seeds. {{note:{index:533,id:UT22084-079-008-1771}}} These great drugs are especially powerful during six different time periods. {{note:{index:534,id:UT22084-079-008-1772}}} {7.1.92}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1773}} “There is spring, hot season, And rainy season. There is also autumn, early winter, And the snowy late winter too. {7.1.93}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1774}} “In springtime, the wise one should perform the rite in the morning; During the hot season, at midday; During the rainy season, in the afternoon; In the autumn, after dark; {7.1.94}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1775}} “In early winter, at midnight; And in late snowy winter, before dawn. This practice, as done by those observing the right time, Is now being taught to you, O beautiful-faced one. {7.1.95}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1776}} “Midnight is right for ingesting the flower infusion (menstrual blood); The season recommended for this is early winter. In the spring, though, the “four ingredients” (feces) {{note:{index:535,id:UT22084-079-008-1777}}} Will bring accomplishment if ingested in the morning. {7.1.96}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1778}} “During the rainy season, in the afternoon, Musk (urine) is pleasing to the mind. During the hot season, at midday, Lotus seeds {{note:{index:536,id:UT22084-079-008-1779}}} will bring the fulfillment of all one’s aims. {7.1.97}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1780}} “In the autumn, after dark, Lotus sap (vaginal secretion?) brings the desired accomplishment. In late winter, before dawn, Camphor (semen) is particularly recommended. {7.1.98}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1781}} “This supreme practice is the best. One who does it with a collected mind Will become free from old age and death, There is no doubt about this. {7.1.99}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1782}} “Quicksilver and sulphur, In combination with śekhara, {{note:{index:537,id:UT22084-079-008-1783}}} Blended homogenously with ghee, Should be employed in every rite. {{note:{index:538,id:UT22084-079-008-1784}}} {7.1.100}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1785}} “One should procure the fourteen substances And zealously ingest them in nine different ways. {{note:{index:539,id:UT22084-079-008-1786}}} One should perform this rite according to one’s wishes, Following the divisions of lunar and solar cycles. {{note:{index:540,id:UT22084-079-008-1787}}} {7.1.101}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1788}} “One will attain full results within twenty-one days. Lost teeth, fingernails, and hair will grow back. When one is accomplished, one will be able to change all elements {{note:{index:541,id:UT22084-079-008-1789}}} into gold. {7.1.102} {{page:{number:103,folio:F.124.b}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1790}} “Now I will teach a rite involving oil.
“Oil of lotus, oil of vālā, {{note:{index:542,id:UT22084-079-008-1792}}} and oil from the “four ingredients” {{note:{index:543,id:UT22084-079-008-1793}}} should all be combined with an equal amount of ground black turmeric, {{note:{index:544,id:UT22084-079-008-1794}}} and mixed with the juice of country mallow. One should also prepare an extract from moonseed and mix it with cow’s milk.
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1795}} “Now I will give you the measurements. One should prepare thirty-two palas of the black turmeric and moonseed powder and boil it with twice that amount of water until it is reduced to four cups of liquid. One should mix this three times, according to the proper sequence, with three parts of the juice of country mallow. One should blend this with four parts of milk to one part of oil, half that amount of moonseed, half that amount of sediment, and the previously mentioned ingredients, cooking it all together gently. {{note:{index:545,id:UT22084-079-008-1796}}} When the mixture is going to be drunk, which requires a medium amount, the moonseed should be left out. For anointing the head, which is said to require a thicker consistency, cooking it three more times is said to be best. For an errhine one should use ten palas. For drinking, one hundred palas is recommended. When anointing, one should use one hundred and eight palas. The practitioner should perform all this with a focused mind. By applying an errhine of this, he can live for a thousand years. When drinking it, he can live five hundred years. When anointing the head, he can live three hundred years. My words are not to be doubted. He will obtain a divine form and a pleasant voice, will always be adored, and will definitely reach proficiency in all sciences and disciplines. His body will have great splendor and luminosity. He will be able to remove all obstacles. {7.1.103}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1797}} “He should procure the ‘four ingredients,’ {{note:{index:546,id:UT22084-079-008-1798}}} dry them well, and blend them thoroughly with milk. He should heat this mixture up in a cow dung fire until the ingredients dissolve, then obtain from it the oil. The practitioner should blend this oil with twice as much black sesame oil and again twice as much milk, and cook it as prescribed. A decoction made of four parts thorn apple, the three fruits, {{note:{index:547,id:UT22084-079-008-1799}}} false daisy, common jasmine, and grass is regarded as helpful for promoting growth. {{note:{index:548,id:UT22084-079-008-1800}}} {7.1.104} {{page:{number:104,folio:F.125.a}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1801}} “Black turmeric, black babchi, blue lotus bulb, iron filings, sulphur, bdellium, white dammar, camphor, and musk—he should cook these substances in oil. They will promote health and longevity. If they are rubbed on the head, they will remove grey hair and wrinkles. All diseases will depart, without a doubt. {{note:{index:549,id:UT22084-079-008-1802}}} {7.1.105}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1803}} “Now I will teach the rite of preparing oils for rubbing on the body.
“One should use the same oil, but add myrrh, thorn apple tree, Indian caper, and fragrant swamp mallow. {{note:{index:550,id:UT22084-079-008-1805}}} Mixing in chaste tree berries, the practitioner of mantra should prepare this into a solution through the previously described method. This should then be mixed with black creeper, beautyberry, ironwood, bulletwood tree, golden champa, red poon, fetid cassia, turmeric, thorn apple, cockscomb, agarwood tree, asafoetida, {{note:{index:551,id:UT22084-079-008-1806}}} parahṛd, vallabhī, {{note:{index:552,id:UT22084-079-008-1807}}} mukta, {{note:{index:553,id:UT22084-079-008-1808}}} pongam oil tree, mañjari, {{note:{index:554,id:UT22084-079-008-1809}}} thorn apple tree, sweet flag, babchi, nut grass, black turmeric, Indian madder, costus, and veronicalolia—these will remove all illnesses. {{note:{index:555,id:UT22084-079-008-1810}}} {7.1.106}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1811}} “An incense of both white and red sandalwood, deer musk, camphor, Indian olibanum, and fingernails, mixed with molasses, can fulfill all one’s wishes. One will be able to cure itching, rash, and cutaneous eruptions, and remove all toxins produced in the body. My words are true, O goddess, {{note:{index:556,id:UT22084-079-008-1812}}} there can be no doubt. {7.1.107}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1813}} “Turmeric powder, {{note:{index:557,id:UT22084-079-008-1814}}} chaste tree berries, powder from a temple brick, extract of thorn apple leaves, musk, and the “four ingredients,” when combined with caura {{note:{index:558,id:UT22084-079-008-1815}}} and keṁśu, {{note:{index:559,id:UT22084-079-008-1816}}} can destroy many different diseases, such as intestinal worms, leprosy, and the toxins in the body. It is especially effective when applied together with babchi. {7.1.108} {{page:{number:105,folio:F.125.b}}}
“These are the ritual procedures for anointing the body with medicinal unguents.
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1818}} “One should pulverize the three astringent substances {{note:{index:560,id:UT22084-079-008-1819}}} together with the ‘four ingredients’ {{note:{index:561,id:UT22084-079-008-1820}}} and drink this with cold musk {{note:{index:562,id:UT22084-079-008-1821}}} for one year while observing vows. In this way one will be able to cure a variety of illnesses related to the internal organs, such as diseases of phlegm, and so forth. When this elixir is digested, it will without fail remove grey hair, and so forth, from the practitioner of mantra. {7.1.109}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1822}} “Alternatively, he should procure the four ingredients and grind them into a fine powder together with the three fruits. {{note:{index:563,id:UT22084-079-008-1823}}} Then he should blend them with ghee and honey and eat one karṣa {{note:{index:564,id:UT22084-079-008-1824}}} of this preparation. Consequently, he will become divinely beautiful and live three hundred years. {7.1.110}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1825}} “Now comes the same recipe, still in liquid form, but without ghee or honey. Alternatively, he should procure the three astringent substances and grind them into a fine powder, gradually adding one cat’s paw {{note:{index:565,id:UT22084-079-008-1826}}} of musk from the midriff. {{note:{index:566,id:UT22084-079-008-1827}}} If the practitioner drinks it well cooled, imagining that power is his, it will cure flatulence and indigestion and, in time, remove wrinkles and grey hair. If it is warm, however, it will cause the greying of hair. {7.1.111}
“Alternatively, he should procure the three fruits, {{note:{index:567,id:UT22084-079-008-1829}}} cook them with milk and water, and apply the concoction to the head. {{note:{index:568,id:UT22084-079-008-1830}}} {7.1.112}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1831}} “He should grind root of long pepper with red rice. He should then make pills out of this, cook them with ghee, and eat them with honey. Then, after three months, all diseases will depart, and especially grey hair. After a six-month treatment, the practitioner will obtain a pleasant voice and become well nourished. After nine months, he will obtain a divine body, become quick-witted, and be able to retain what he hears. After one year, he will obtain the strength of an elephant and be able to live three hundred years. {7.1.113}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1832}} “Alternatively, he should procure three parts each of nāga {{note:{index:569,id:UT22084-079-008-1833}}} root, palāśa {{note:{index:570,id:UT22084-079-008-1834}}} root, and costus root. He should grind them into powder with one part long pepper as the tenth part of the concoction. {{note:{index:571,id:UT22084-079-008-1835}}} After blending the powder with cow milk, a wise yogin should consume one karṣa {{note:{index:572,id:UT22084-079-008-1836}}} of this mixture every day. {7.1.114} {{page:{number:106,folio:F.126.a}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1837}} “Should a yogin dwell in desolate mountains, and such, For hundreds of years, He will surely be totally satiated And free of hunger and thirst. {7.1.115}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1838}} “Thus, he should dwell in desolate mountains, and such, With this remedy. Any other method is unnecessary, As far as the attainment of buddhahood is concerned. {{note:{index:573,id:UT22084-079-008-1839}}} {7.1.116}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1840}} “He should meditate without company in a mountain cave—the hermitage of the relative truth of practitioners. {7.1.117}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1841}} “One who wants to be a practitioner But does not know the ritual restrictions with respect to seasons {{note:{index:574,id:UT22084-079-008-1842}}} Is like someone hitting his fist against empty space Or drinking mirage water, Or like a hungry person threshing chaff. {7.1.118}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1843}} “Futile will be their toil; It will bear no fruit. The practitioner should thus stay focused According to the ritual procedure revealed by me. {7.1.119}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1844}} “This is the section on the science of longevity called ‘the source of all knowledge.’ ”
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1845}} This concludes the first part of the seventh chapter.
Part 2
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1846}} [Vajragarbha said:]
“I want to hear, O Blessed One, how to perform The ritual of homa with its recitation, and so forth. How should one do the rites of pacifying, enriching, enthralling, and assaulting, Along with their respective oblation offerings, and so forth?” {7.2.1}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1848}} [The Blessed One replied:]
“Hear, Vajragarbha, the description of the rites Of homa, and so forth, as they actually are. First, the practitioner of mantra should do one hundred thousand recitations of the mantra, And after, start the performance of the rite. {7.2.2}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1850}} “A deity yoga practitioner, Having assumed the āliḍha posture, the pratyāliḍha posture, Or one with the feet parallel, or forked, Should invite his consort (vidyā) to join him. {7.2.3}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1851}} “She could be a brahmin, a kṣatriya, A vaiśya, or a śūdra— So require the rules of the rite. Afterward, he should commence the homa rite. {7.2.4}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1852}} “If it is the rite of pacifying, he should delimit a round fire-pit area one cubit in diameter. Having done the measurements, he should dig a hole half a cubit deep in the ground. He should daub the insides of this half-cubit-deep pit with white sandalwood. He should demarcate a four-finger-width {{note:{index:575,id:UT22084-079-008-1853}}} wide rim of earth in a circle surrounding the fire pit. {7.2.5} {{page:{number:107,folio:F.126.b}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1854}} “The pit for enriching should be a square of two cubits on each side. The basin should be one cubit deep. The rim should be eight finger-widths wide. The pit should be bedecked with heaps of yellow flowers and anointed with yellow sandalwood. {7.2.6}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1855}} “The pit for the rites of assaulting should be triangular and measure twenty finger-widths across. The basin should be ten finger-widths deep. He should draw the rim three finger-widths wide and smear the pit with charnel ground ash. {7.2.7}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1856}} “Since the activities of enthralling and summoning are similar, their pit is described as having identical characteristics. One should prepare a pit shaped like a half-moon and with the same measurements as the pit for enriching. {{note:{index:576,id:UT22084-079-008-1857}}} The depth of the basin should be half its diameter. One should demarcate the rim to fit the other measurements and daub the pit with red sandalwood. {7.2.8}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1858}} “The powder used for demarcating the pit Should be white in rites of pacifying, Yellow in rites of enriching, black in rites of killing, And red in rites of enthralling. {7.2.9}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1859}} “The specifications for summoning are the same as those for enthralling, And those for sowing hatred, the same as those for killing. {7.2.10}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1860}} “Now I will explain the connection between the types of rites and the directions.
“The fire pit for pacifying should be to the east of the temple or maṇḍala, {{note:{index:577,id:UT22084-079-008-1862}}} That for the rites of assaulting to the south, The one for enthralling and summoning to the west, And the one for enriching to the north. {7.2.11}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1861}} “The marking powder is said to correspond in color to the rites just described. This concludes how one should dig the fire pits. {7.2.12}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1864}} “Now I will explain the procedure involving different types of grain.
“He should mix rice, corn, white sesame, barley, nutmeg, dūrvā grass, milk, ghee, and honey with the five ambrosias and offer this in a homa along with moist wood branches originating from the five sap-bearing trees, still with leaves on them, smeared at both ends in honey, milk, and ghee. He should start the fire with the kindling of Indian cluster fig and palash tree. {{note:{index:578,id:UT22084-079-008-1866}}} If he wants to perform the rite of pacifying, he should cast the offerings into the fire one hundred and eight times, three times a day, while sitting facing east. He can then pacify even the entire district. {7.2.13}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1867}} “Now, if he wants to perform the rite of enriching, he should procure black sesame and mung beans along with red rice. As an alternative, he can use barley or something else. The kindling sticks are said to be the same as before, but this time they should be smeared with one handful of milk and butter. {{note:{index:579,id:UT22084-079-008-1868}}} {{page:{number:108,folio:F.127.a}}} All the ingredients should be sprinkled with saffron perfume and combined with the three sweet things, rice pudding, curds, honey, ghee, dill, {{note:{index:580,id:UT22084-079-008-1869}}} bel fruit, lotus, stamens of ironwood blossoms, and rice. Having then lit the fire using wood of Indian cluster fig, he should generate himself as the deity appropriate for the ritual. Facing north, he should cast the ingredients into the fire a thousand times, three times a day, with a focused mind. When seven days have passed, he will become a great owner of wealth. {7.2.14}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1870}} “Now, if he wants to perform the rite of enthralling, he should procure red sesame or black sesame, {{note:{index:581,id:UT22084-079-008-1871}}} beautyberry, stamens of ironwood blossoms, champak, sorrow-less tree, vajra, {{note:{index:582,id:UT22084-079-008-1872}}} bulletwood tree, bāṇa, {{note:{index:583,id:UT22084-079-008-1873}}} and dill, mixed with sandalwood, ghee, and honey. He should also procure pieces of wood eight finger-widths long from deodar, banyan, pipal, Indian cluster fig, and other trees. Also, the milky sap from the Indian olibanum and guggul trees, as well as sugandha {{note:{index:584,id:UT22084-079-008-1874}}} and other substances, should be used. {{note:{index:585,id:UT22084-079-008-1875}}} Then, he should assume a red form using menstrual blood mixed with vajra water {{note:{index:586,id:UT22084-079-008-1876}}} and sit facing the west. Whoever’s name he employs while making offerings to the fire will become enthralled after seven days. He will be able to keep her or him for as long as he lives. {7.2.15}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1877}} “Now, if he wishes to perform the rite of assaulting, he should blend black sesame, mung beans or something similar, the fruit of the marking nut, and kālaka, {{note:{index:587,id:UT22084-079-008-1878}}} with black mustard oil and an admixture of blood. {{note:{index:588,id:UT22084-079-008-1879}}} He should then procure thorns from a crooked black tree, and pieces of wood ten finger-widths long from all trees that are pungent, bitter, and so forth. Adding human bone, human feces, donkey droppings, and hair, as well as dog feces, hair, and paws, he should blend all this with oil, and facing south with a focused mind, offer it into a charnel ground fire one hundred and eight times. Whoever’s name one employs will die within three days. {{page:{number:109,folio:F.127.b}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1880}} “If not, he should stand to one side and prepare a triangular fire pit. There, he should offer the previously mentioned substances into a fire obtained from a household of untouchables. By this means alone the enemy will be led to the abode of the lord of death, of this there is no doubt. {7.2.16}
“If he wants to drive someone away, he should mix mustard seeds, {{note:{index:589,id:UT22084-079-008-1882}}} mung beans, and dust from a footpath, and blend them with blood and black mustard oil. He should add to this a crow’s nest from a thorn apple tree. The person whose name he employs while offering this preparation into the fire will be driven away instantly. {7.2.17}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1883}} “Alternatively, he should use crow meat {{note:{index:590,id:UT22084-079-008-1884}}} and camel droppings mixed with wine. Naked and with loose hair, he should offer this into a fire from a charnel ground. Whoever’s name he employs will be driven away. {7.2.18}
“If he wants to perform paralyzing, he should grind fish, meat, and the remaining three substances, {{note:{index:591,id:UT22084-079-008-1886}}} together with rice grains, blood, and honey, and add to this a crow’s feather. He should offer this into a fire made with sticks from a crow’s nest and discarded sticks for cleaning teeth, in a square fire pit. Whoever’s name he employs will be stopped from carrying out any task. {7.2.19}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1887}} “Alternatively, he should use turmeric, (arsenic) orpiment, realgar, and bovine orpiment. He should offer this into the fire while facing north. Whoever’s name he employs will become paralyzed. {7.2.20}
“If he employs dog and chicken meat, he should grind them together with camel droppings and cat blood. Then, lighting the sacrificial fire using neem tree sticks, he should offer this into the fire. Whichever village’s name he employs will be destroyed. {7.2.21}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1889}} “He should blend spirituous liquor with human flesh and offer it into the fire, at the three junctions of the day, until he has done this one hundred and eight times. After six months he will become the governor of the district. {7.2.22}
“He should offer one hundred burnt offerings of jackal meat. {{note:{index:592,id:UT22084-079-008-1891}}} After three months he will be able to remove dire poverty in an instant. {7.2.23}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1892}} “He should soak cow flesh in cow blood and offer it one thousand times into a fire. Enthrallment will take place, lasting as long as he lives, there is no doubt. {7.2.24} {{page:{number:110,folio:F.128.a}}}
“He should blend the same meat with spirituous liquor and offer it into a fire {{note:{index:593,id:UT22084-079-008-1894}}} with his left hand. He will be able to enthrall even a buddha, let alone ordinary people. If not, he can also use a stick for cleaning the teeth, covered in saliva, smeared with bodily impurities, and doused with wine. By offering this stick as a burnt offering he will enthrall the target, there is no doubt. {7.2.25}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1895}} “By offering ingested and vomited menstrual blood with an addition of human hair as a burnt offering, he will be able to summon the target immediately. This method of summoning is the best. {7.2.26}
“He should smear crow’s feathers with white mustard oil and offer them in a thorn apple fire. Whoever’s name he employs will immediately be driven away and die. {7.2.27}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1897}} “He should offer in a fire an oblation of atimuktikā, {{note:{index:594,id:UT22084-079-008-1898}}} white gourd melon, mung beans, {{note:{index:595,id:UT22084-079-008-1899}}} sann hemp, vomit, and black mustard, together with tamāla leaves, {{note:{index:596,id:UT22084-079-008-1900}}} at home. {{note:{index:597,id:UT22084-079-008-1901}}} He will be able to seal the target’s mouth, there is no doubt. {7.2.28}
“He should offer in a fire an oblation of dog meat combined with vajra water. {{note:{index:598,id:UT22084-079-008-1903}}} Whoever’s name he employs will become enthralled within seven days. {7.2.29}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1904}} “He should offer in a fire horse meat together with human feces at night. {{note:{index:599,id:UT22084-079-008-1905}}} He will be able to enthrall the king within seven days. {7.2.30}
“He should offer in a fire elephant meat mixed with semen. He will be able to enthrall an entire city. {7.2.31}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1907}} “He should offer in a fire fish and meat combined with spirituous liquor. When he has offered this one hundred and eight times, he will be able to enthrall any woman. {7.2.32}
“He should offer in a fire only crow meat one thousand times. {{note:{index:600,id:UT22084-079-008-1909}}} Whoever’s name he employs will flee within three days. If even Vajrasattva will flee, how much more so will ordinary people? {7.2.33}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1910}} “He should offer crow and hawk meat into a fire made with thorn apple sticks. Whoever’s name he employs will be driven away. {7.2.34}
“He should offer human flesh and bird meat. Whoever’s name he employs will go insane. Should he offer the same {{note:{index:601,id:UT22084-079-008-1912}}} into a chaff fire, the target will become well again. {7.2.35}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1913}} “All these rites can only be performed by someone Who has done preliminary practices. Otherwise he will become without a doubt An object of ridicule of all the people. {7.2.36}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1914}} “He must not disclose the secret of his practice to anyone. If the secret is revealed, he will never gain accomplishment or find happiness. {{page:{number:111,folio:F.128.b}}} Therefore a mantra practitioner must never perform these rites in front of anyone. If he wants to perform them, he should do so alone. Then the mantra practitioner can succeed in every rite.” {{note:{index:602,id:UT22084-079-008-1915}}} {7.2.37}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1916}} This concludes the section on homa rites, which forms the second part of the seventh chapter.
Part 3
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1917}} [The goddess said:]
“It would be interesting to hear, my lord, About the methods of deriving mantras. I do not know their categorization. Please explain this, O Great Bliss.” {7.3.1}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1919}} The Blessed One said:
“Listen Great Wisdom, my lady! I will tell you the mantras of the deities. In the pleasant maṇḍala with three corners Is the secret lotus, Māmakī. {7.3.2}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1921}} “One should form an eight-petaled lotus With its pericarp located in the secret area. {{note:{index:603,id:UT22084-079-008-1922}}} There, one should reproduce the valiant one in syllables That fulfill all one’s aims and wishes. {7.3.3}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1923}} “Based on the divisions of the letters of the alphabet, Beginning with the letter a , mantra is the supreme lord of letter classes. {7.3.4}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1924}} “Take the second letter of the first group, {{note:{index:604,id:UT22084-079-008-1925}}} surmounted by a dot; {{note:{index:605,id:UT22084-079-008-1926}}} the third letter of the seventh group, adorned with a half moon; {{note:{index:606,id:UT22084-079-008-1927}}} and the seed syllable of awakening, ‘worshiped’ on its crown by the full moon. This is the heart mantra. {{note:{index:607,id:UT22084-079-008-1928}}} {7.3.5}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1929}} “Now I will give you the auxiliary heart mantra. One should take the second letter of the seventh group ( ra ), join it with Vajraḍākinī ( u ), and double it. Then, one should take the third letter of the hot sounds ( sa ) and support it underneath with the second letter of the sixth group ( pha ), joined with the fifth vowel ( u ). The second of the semivowels ( ra ) should be supported underneath by the fifth vowel ( u ). The third letter of the third group ( ja ) should be supported underneath by the twenty-ninth letter ( va ). The third letter of the seventh group ( la ) and the first letter of the fifth group ( ta ) should be joined with the third vowel ( i ). The second letter of the eighth group ( ṣa ) should be supported underneath by the twelfth letter ( ṭha ). One should take the thirty-second letter ( sa ) and join it with Gaurī ( i ). Then, one should add the third letter of the fifth group ( da ) with the fourth letter from that same group ( dha ) below it. One should add the third semivowel ( la ), supremely adorned by Ghasmarī ( o ). One should join to the first letter of the third group ( ca ) and the fifth letter of the fifth group ( na ), Caurī ( e ), who is the highest boon. {7.3.6} {{page:{number:112,folio:F.129.a}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1930}} “Locanā {{note:{index:608,id:UT22084-079-008-1931}}} is the creator of peace for the buddhas. She makes all rites successful, She is said to revive the dead, And she is the requester of the vajra pledge.” {7.3.7}
And the Blessed One added, {{note:{index:609,id:UT22084-079-008-1933}}} “ Oṁ, svāhā to Vajravairocanī. {{note:{index:610,id:UT22084-079-008-1934}}} {7.3.8}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1935}} “The fourth letter of the second group ( gha ) adorned with Vāri is the heart mantra of Māmakī. Her auxiliary heart mantra is explained as follows:
“The first letter of the hot sounds ( śa ) is adorned above by Khecarī ( aṁ ). The first letter of the second group ( ka ) and the second letter of the seventh group ( ra ) are joined with Caurī ( e ) in like fashion. The first letter of the eighth group ( śa ) should be joined by the supreme Vajrā ( a ), who is the highest boon. One should take the twentieth letter ( na ) and support it underneath with the sixteenth {{note:{index:611,id:UT22084-079-008-1937}}} letter ( ta ). Gaurī ( i ) is held to be their adornment. One should take the first letter of the second group ( ka ) and the twenty-seventh letter ( ra ), and one should join them with Caurī ( e ). The fourth letter of the second group ( gha ), with Vajraḍākinī ( u ) as its seat, should be combined with the first letter of the third group ( ṭa ), then doubled. The fourth letter of the second group ( gha ) should be joined with Vajraḍākinī ( u ). Take the eleventh letter ( ṭa ), distinguished by the third vowel ( i ), add the fifth letter of the fifth group ( na ), and join it with Gaurī ( i ). One should take the fourth letter of the second group ( gha ), along with the supreme essence of Vajrā ( a ), then add the sixteenth letter ( ta ) and the twenty-sixth letter ( ya ), and double the whole thing. The fourth letter of the second group ( gha ) should be adorned with the fifth vowel ( u ).
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1938}} “The first letter of the fourth group ( ṭa ) Should be joined with Gaurī ( i ). The fifth letter of the fifth group ( na ) One should join with Gaurī ( i ). {7.3.9}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1939}} “In the protective vajra rites, She (Māmakī) invariably accomplishes all actions. She is declared to be the strength-giver To those afflicted by the great vajra fear.” {{note:{index:612,id:UT22084-079-008-1940}}} {7.3.10}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1941}} Now the Blessed One said the mantra of Māmakī’s consort Ratnasambhava:
“ Oṁ , burn, burn, hūṁ, phaṭ! Svāhā to [the deities who shout] phaṭ !” {{note:{index:613,id:UT22084-079-008-1943}}} {7.3.11}
[And he continued further:]
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1945}} “Now, for the mantra of Paṇḍaravāsinī, one should take the first letter of the second group ( ka ) and the first letter of the fourth group ( ṭa ); Caurī ( e ) is thought to be their adornment. One should take the fourth letter of the seventh group ( va ), adorned on top with Gaurī ( i ). One should then take the first letter of the second group ( ka ) and the eleventh letter ( ṭa ), adorned on top with Caurī ( e ). {{page:{number:113,folio:F.129.b}}} One should take the fifth letter of the fifth group ( na ) and join it with the third vowel ( i ). One should take the first letter of the second group ( ka ) and the first letter of the fourth group ( ṭa ), and connect to them Caurī ( e ), who is the supreme boon. One should then add the first letter of the second group ( ka ) and the first letter of the fourth group ( ṭa ), adorned on top with Khecarī ( aṁ ). One should add the first letter of the second group ( ka ) and the eleventh letter ( ṭa ), joined with Caurī ( e ). {7.3.12}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1946}} “Mahākoṣavatī always generates energy, Which fosters the Dharma Merely by reciting the mantra, Similar to the words of Vāgvajra. {7.3.13}
“ Oṁ , Vajradharma hrīḥ! Svāhā! {{note:{index:614,id:UT22084-079-008-1948}}} {7.3.14}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1949}} “Now, for the mantra of Tārā, one should take the sixteenth letter ( ta ), With Vajrī ( ā ) as the supreme adornment, And the second semivowel ( ra ), With Caurī ( e ) joined to it. {7.3.15}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1950}} “One should take the first letter of the fifth group ( ta ), With Ḍākinī ( u ) thought to be its seat. {{note:{index:615,id:UT22084-079-008-1951}}} One should then take the sixteenth letter ( ta ), With the first letter of the fifth group ( ta ) as its seat, and Vajrā ( ā ) joined with it. {7.3.16}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1952}} “One should take the twenty-seventh letter ( ra ) In combination with Caurī ( e ). To this should be added the first letter of the fifth group ( ta ) Joined with Ḍākinī ( ā ) below. {7.3.17}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1953}} “The second letter of the seventh group ( ra ) Should be augmented by the essence of Caurī ( e ). The great army of Buddhavajra, And the realm of beings all around, {7.3.18}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1954}} “Will carry out any orders like servants; They will surely be enthralled right at that time.” {{note:{index:616,id:UT22084-079-008-1955}}} {7.3.19}
So spoke the great Blessed Vajradhara. {{note:{index:617,id:UT22084-079-008-1957}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1958}} “One should derive a mantra beginning with The syllable oṁ that illuminates everything, and ending with svāhā. {{note:{index:618,id:UT22084-079-008-1959}}} Such a mantra will grant all desired accomplishments, Just like the words of the Tathāgata. {7.3.20}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1960}} “ Oṁ , act, act! Accomplish, accomplish! Bind, bind! Frighten, frighten! Shake, shake! Hraḥ hraḥ! Pheṃ pheṃ! Phaṭ phaṭ ! Burn, burn! Cook, cook! Devour, devour! You who wear a garland of entrails covered in fat and blood, seize seize! Threaten the serpents in the seven subterranean paradises. Summon them, summon! Hrīṁ hrīṁ! Jñaiṁ jñaiṁ! Kṣmāṁ kṣmāṁ! Hāṁ hāṁ! Hīṁ hīṁ! {{note:{index:619,id:UT22084-079-008-1961}}} Hūṁ hūṁ! Kili kili! {{page:{number:114,folio:F.130.a}}} Sili sili! Cili cili! {{note:{index:620,id:UT22084-079-008-1962}}} Dhili dhili! Hūṁ hūṁ! Phaṭ phaṭ! Svāhā! {{note:{index:621,id:UT22084-079-008-1963}}}
This mantra of the lord of spells accomplishes all activities. {7.3.21}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1965}} “The heart mantra of Akṣobhya:
“To start, one should take the syllable of Vairocana ( oṁ ), And then take the fourth letter of the ‘hot sounds’ ( ha ), Adorned with Pukkasī ( ū ) and topped with ‘empty space’ ( ṁ ). One should append svāhā at the end. {7.3.22}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1967}} “By reciting this mantra 100,000 times One will be able to paralyze the world at any time. {7.3.23}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1968}} “The heart mantra of Ratnasambhava:
“At the beginning one should take the king of letters ( oṁ ), And after that, Khecarī ( laṁ ). One should add svāhā at the end— With this one will be able to enthrall even the buddhas. {7.3.24}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1970}} “The heart mantra of Amoghasiddhi:
“One should take the first letter of the Vedas ( oṁ ) and the second letter of the second group ( kha ) topped with ‘empty space’ ( ṁ ), and add svāhā at the end. The wise practitioner will be able to drive away even the buddhas. {7.3.25}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1972}} “The heart mantra of Amitābha:
“At the beginning one should place the syllable of Vairocana ( oṁ ) and combine it with the third letter of the third group ( ja ), adorned with the neuter syllable ( ra ) and Vāri ( ī ), together with ‘empty space’ ( ṁ ). The mantra should end with svāhā . When pronounced, it sows enmity. {7.3.26}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1974}} “The heart mantra of Vairocana:
“At the beginning one should place the king of letters ( oṁ ). Then, one should take the fourth letter of the seventh group ( va ), {{note:{index:622,id:UT22084-079-008-1976}}} joined with the syllable of Vajraḍākinī ( u ) and ‘empty space’ ( ṁ ). One should add svāhā at the end. This mantra is employed in acts of assaulting. {7.3.27}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1977}} “The heart mantra of Locanā:
“One should again use the king of letters ( oṁ ), then add the red syllable hūṁ , and finish with svāhā . With this mantra one will be able to summon the entire world, and among the apsarases, Rambhā, and so forth, and even Tilottamā. {7.3.28}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1979}} “The heart mantra of Māmakī:
“At the beginning one should place the syllable of the ‘delusion family’ ( oṁ ), And join it with the syllable ghuḥ. At the end, one should again add svāhā — With this one will be able to cause the death of gods and men. {7.3.29}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1984}} “The heart mantra of Paṇḍaravāsinī:
“One should take the second letter in the eighth group ( ra ), {{note:{index:623,id:UT22084-079-008-1986}}} adorned with the eighth letter of the eighth group ( ha ). One should place the syllable of the ‘delusion family’ ( oṁ ) at the beginning and complete it with svāhā at the end. {7.3.30}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1987}} “The mantra of Tārā:
“One should take the syllable of action ( ī ) and join it with the syllable of Vairocana ( oṁ ) at the beginning, and with svāhā at the end. {7.3.31}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1989}} “The heart mantras for the surrounding gate keepers Are the four neuter vowel syllables ( ṛ, ṝ, ḷ, ḹ ); The remaining vowels constitute the mantras for the eight offering goddesses. Starting with the first syllable of the Vedas ( oṁ ), One should pronounce the mantra with svāhā at the end. {7.3.32}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1990}} “The offering goddesses Puṣpā, Dhūpā, Gandhā, And also Dīpā, Vaṃśā, Vīṇā, Mukundā and Murajā, {7.3.33}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-8112}} “As prescribed by the rule, should thus be arranged As in the maṇḍala for the gaṇacakra feast. {7.3.34}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1992}} “Now I will teach on Tārā’s many boons, Variously manifesting through each ritual action. {{page:{number:115,folio:F.130.b}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1993}} “The first method;
“One should draw a lotus with four petals Extending throughout the cardinal and intermediate directions. {7.3.35}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1995}} “Its pericarp should be decorated, as prescribed, With three taṁ {{note:{index:624,id:UT22084-079-008-1996}}} syllables. Around, following the shape of a circle, The mantrin should write as follows: {7.3.36}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1997}} “ Oṁ , Prasannatārā! One with the face and eyes of an immortal! Fulfiller of all aims! Pacifier of all beings! Please bring about enthrallment, no matter whether it is of a woman, a man, or a king! Svāhā! {{note:{index:625,id:UT22084-079-008-1998}}} {7.3.37}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-1999}} “In the center of the lotus he should draw a wheel with eight spokes, furnished with eight syllables. On its hub should be drawn the first letter of the fifth group ( ta ) adorned with the crescent moon and the bindu ( tam̐ ). Then, he should surround it with the mantra in the shape of a garland, ending with svāhā , and with syllables hrīḥ placed on the anthers {{note:{index:626,id:UT22084-079-008-2000}}} in the spaces in between. The mantrin who thus forms two wheels joined as prescribed will be able within seven days to enthrall even a king. {7.3.38}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2001}} “The second method;
“Alternatively, he should draw a wheel with ten spokes, which houses a lotus Furnished at its center with the ten syllables of the mantric formula. {{note:{index:627,id:UT22084-079-008-2003}}} The target’s name should be written on the pericarp within the mantra. He will enthrall the target for as long as she or he lives, there is no doubt. {7.3.39}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2004}} “The third method;
“He should draw another yantra-wheel with six spokes, Containing the six syllables of the mantric formula, And write in the center ‘ hrīḥ , please enthrall, hrīḥ ,’ {{note:{index:628,id:UT22084-079-008-2006}}} Adding the word svāhā at the end. {7.3.40}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2007}} “Whoever writes this mantra on birchbark With bovine orpiment mixed with lac, Red sandalwood, and one’s own blood, And wears it on his body, {7.3.41}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2008}} “Will enthrall even gods and other such beings, Let alone ordinary people. {7.3.42}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2009}} “The fourth method;
“He should draw in the center of a water disk A three-pronged, crossed vajra scepter. He should place the name Of the target in its hub. {7.3.43}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2011}} “Should he draw this in chalk, according to procedure, In a pair of earthenware vessels, he will paralyze the target. {7.3.44}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2012}} “The fifth method;
“There can also be a yantra-wheel with eight spokes, depicted entirely as a lotus with its petals. He should place upon it the syllables interspersed with the syllable gaḥ following the right procedure. The pericarp of the lotus should be adorned with eight gaḥ syllables. In the center he should write gaḥ svāhā gaḥ , combining this with the name of the target. He should write this on a stone slab with the juice of turmeric and position it face down. The target will become thoroughly paralyzed—it cannot be otherwise. {7.3.45} {{page:{number:116,folio:F.131.a}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2014}} “The sixth method;
“He can also draw the same yantra-wheel, but write in it hūṁ hūṁ interspersed with the syllable phaṭ . He should write this on a human skull, with a human bone as the writing utensil, using poison, blood, and black mustard seed for ink. If he does this in a charnel ground, he will kill the target. {7.3.46}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2016}} “The seventh method;
“Another yantra-wheel should be identical, but he should intersperse hūṁ hūṁ with the syllable oṁ and write it on birchbark, using saffron for ink. He should offer yellow flowers or, alternatively, the five types of service. Through so doing the target will become enriched after seven days. {7.3.47}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2018}} “The eighth method;
“If he intersperses the same syllables with the word svāhā , he will ensure protection. {7.3.48}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2020}} “The ninth method;
“Using the same wheel, he can take the ten syllables of the mantric formula, this time interspersed with the syllable āḥ , and write the target’s name on an earthenware plate using white sandal as ink. He should then offer fragrant white flowers and make offerings according to his ability, reciting the mantra one hundred and eight times at the three junctions of the day, as prescribed. Through so doing the target will be pacified of negative influences after seven days. {7.3.49}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2022}} “The tenth method;
“Using the same wheel again, he should write ‘ āḥ , of such and such’ in the center of the letter e. {{note:{index:629,id:UT22084-079-008-2024}}} He should then write hūṁ above it, below it, and to its sides; vaṁ in the intermediate directions around it; and three lines surrounding everything on the outside. If he writes this on birchbark using bovine orpiment as ink, and then places the birchbark in ghee and honey, he will certainly enthrall the target after seven days. {7.3.50}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2025}} “The eleventh method;
“Using the same wheel, he should draw a lotus with four petals, each furnished with the syllable hrīṁ . In the center, he should write ‘ hrīḥ , such and such’ surrounded by four hūṁ syllables. If he writes this with red sandalwood paste on unbaked earthenware he will be able to placate an angry person, there is no doubt about it. {7.3.51}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2027}} “The twelfth method;
“Alternatively, he should draw two wheels on birchbark using saffron and bovine orpiment, or lac, as ink. He should wear one wheel and place the other wheel in ghee and honey and leave it there. Through so doing, whomever he has in mind will become a dear friend. {7.3.52}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2029}} “The mantra specific to some of these rituals is:
Oṁ , Tārā, you who bewilder everyone! Eager to save! Strong and powerful one! Bewilder all evildoers, bewilder! Blessed one! Bind all evildoers, bind! Hūṁ hūṁ hūṁ! Phaṭ phaṭ phaṭ! Svāhā! {{note:{index:630,id:UT22084-079-008-2030}}} {7.3.53}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2031}} “The thirteenth method;
“If he ties a knot at the edge of his garment and sets out on a journey, he will not be robbed by robbers. {{note:{index:631,id:UT22084-079-008-2033}}} {7.3.54}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2034}} “The fourteenth method;
“To whomever he gives a blue lotus marked with a wheel after incanting it with the appropriate mantra {{note:{index:632,id:UT22084-079-008-2036}}} seven times, that person will be enthralled. This is the rite of the wheel marked with a blue lotus. {{note:{index:633,id:UT22084-079-008-2037}}} {7.3.55} {{page:{number:117,folio:F.131.b}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2038}} “The fifteenth method;
“For the next yantra-wheel, the lotus to be drawn should have eight petals and be provided with the syllables hrīḥ and śrīḥ . On its anthers {{note:{index:634,id:UT22084-079-008-2040}}} he should write ‘ hrīḥ , such and such, śrīḥ. ’ If he writes this on birchbark with bovine orpiment as ink and wears it, he will be fortunate in every respect. {7.3.56}
