{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2041}} “The sixteenth method;
“He should draw a lotus with eight petals and write at its center the mantra of the ‘delusion family’ ( oṁ ). He should draw a circular line surrounding it and eight three-pronged vajra scepters surrounding that. If he draws this with saffron following the prescribed procedure and wears it, tied to his arm, he will always be protected. {7.3.57}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2043}} “The seventeenth method;
“The next yantra-wheel should be the same but without the vajra scepters. He should write on the pericarp, or on the outside the following:
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2045}} “ Oṁ, hūṁ hūṁ ! Wake, wake! Devour, devour! Chop, chop! Shake, shake! Churn, churn! Bind, bind! Sow enmity between such-and-such and such-and-such! Hūṁ hūṁ! Phaṭ phaṭ! Svāhā! {{note:{index:635,id:UT22084-079-008-2046}}} {7.3.58}
“This is the mantra of Hayagrīva for sowing enmity. He should write this mantra with a substance suitable for the rites of assaulting in the center of a buffalo’s or horse’s hoof. He will cause enmity at that moment even between Śiva and Durgā, let alone ordinary humans. {7.3.59}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2048}} “The eighteenth method;
“He should draw two maṇḍalas of fire {{note:{index:636,id:UT22084-079-008-2050}}} with a pair of corners below and above, following the prescribed rule. Above he should write hūṁ gaḥ hūṁ hūṁ gaḥ hūṁ , and in the area below, hūṁ hūṁ phaṭ . Further, on the outer points of the triangles, he should write hūṁ gaḥ hūṁ hūṁ gaḥ hūṁ , and in the center, hūṁ gaḥ hūṁ. {{note:{index:637,id:UT22084-079-008-2051}}} He should draw all this with ink made from poison, blood, black mustard, charnel ground ash, juice from the leaves of the neem tree, and urine on a rag from a charnel ground or the rag of a madman. If he then encircles the entire diagram with the mantra of Mahābala and places the rag above a burning fire, he will paralyze the enemy. {7.3.60}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2052}} “The nineteenth method;
“He should depict a lotus, adorned with eight āḥ syllables on its petals, at the center of a square Indra maṇḍala with eight oṁ syllables positioned at its eight cardinal and intermediary points. On its pericarp should be positioned the target’s name adorned with four hūṁ syllables. If he encloses this in a two-piece earthenware dish and wraps it all around with a vajra cord while reciting the mantra words of invocation and meditating that Vajradhara stands astride the target’s head, this mantra wheel will paralyze all men, gods, and bodhisattvas. {7.3.61} {{page:{number:118,folio:F.132.a}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2054}} “The twentieth method;
“As for the next yantra-wheel, the maṇḍala of Indra should be marked with eight three-pronged vajra scepters. In the center of this maṇḍala should be a four-cornered maṇḍala, inscribed with the following mantras:
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2056}} “In the east, ‘ Oṁ , bring downfall! Pātanī, svāhā to you!’ {{note:{index:638,id:UT22084-079-008-2057}}} In the south, ‘ Oṁ , crush! Jambhanī, svāhā to you!’ {{note:{index:639,id:UT22084-079-008-2059}}} In the west, ‘ Oṁ , delude! Mohanī, svāhā to you!’ {{note:{index:640,id:UT22084-079-008-2061}}} In the north, ‘ Oṁ , paralyze! Stambhanī, svāhā to you!’ {{note:{index:641,id:UT22084-079-008-2063}}} {7.3.62}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2064}} “He should then draw another maṇḍala of Indra inside that square maṇḍala and write at its center, ‘ Please paralyze such and such.’ {{note:{index:642,id:UT22084-079-008-2065}}} He should draw this yantra on birchbark with turmeric juice and then stuff it into a frog’s {{note:{index:643,id:UT22084-079-008-2066}}} mouth. Piercing the mouth with a thorn of downy datura from above, he should fix the upper palate to the lower. {{note:{index:644,id:UT22084-079-008-2067}}} Through so doing one will paralyze a hostile army at that very instant. {7.3.63}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2068}} “The twenty-first method;
“The next yantra-wheel should have a round shape with a five-pronged, crossed vajra scepter aligned with the intermediate directions. At the tip of its central prongs there should be four hūṁ syllables. {{note:{index:645,id:UT22084-079-008-2070}}} On its hub he should write the following garland of mantra syllables:
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2071}} “ Oṁ , you move your feet, you march forward. You are good fortune, you are the essence, you are the intellect, you are the vital breath, you are the sea-waves, you are the tree-forests, you are the undergrowth, you are the monk’s robes, you are the great robes, you are the invisibility. Svāhā! {{note:{index:646,id:UT22084-079-008-2072}}} {7.3.64}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2073}} “The syllable oṁ should be written everywhere. At the center of the circle should be drawn a three-pronged, crossed vajra scepter, aligned with the cardinal directions. On its central, left, and right prongs should be written, respectively, the mantras ‘ Oṁ Vattalī! ’ ‘ Oṁ Varalī! ’ and ‘ Oṁ Varāmukhī! ’ He should write thus on all the prongs, repeating the same pattern for each of the four tips of the crossed vajra scepter. In the northeast and other intermediate quarters he should write ‘ Oṁ to Mārīcī.’ {{note:{index:647,id:UT22084-079-008-2074}}} In the center he should write ‘ Oṁ , Varālī! Vattālī! Varāhamukhī! Crush the body, speech, and mind of all the most wicked evildoers! Paralyze their mouths!’ {{note:{index:648,id:UT22084-079-008-2075}}} In the center of that he should place the syllable māṁ and, in its center, the words ‘ Protect such and such, protect! ’ {{note:{index:649,id:UT22084-079-008-2076}}} On the outside of the syllable māṁ he should write ‘ Oṁ to the deity {{note:{index:650,id:UT22084-079-008-2077}}} Mārīcī!’ {{note:{index:651,id:UT22084-079-008-2078}}} If he draws this yantra-wheel on birchbark with saffron and wears it, he will always be protected. {7.3.65}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2079}} “The twenty-second method;
“He should make an effigy of a naked man with flowing hair and earrings in his ears. {{page:{number:119,folio:F.132.b}}} Atop its head there should be a three-pronged vajra scepter marked with the syllable haṁ . Above its forehead one should write lāṁ lāṁ . On its cheeks and throat, {{note:{index:652,id:UT22084-079-008-2081}}} starting from the right side of its chin, he should write, ‘ May the counter-spells ruin those who injure my mind. ’ {{note:{index:653,id:UT22084-079-008-2082}}} In the area from its navel to its mouth, he should draw the shape of a caitya. Above it, he should draw a five-pronged vajra scepter. He should then write the mantra of interdependent origination, ‘Those dharmas that arise from causes, etc.,’ forming the shape of a garland of words that extends from the right side of the hollow inside the caitya up to the chest, {{note:{index:654,id:UT22084-079-008-2083}}} left, and then down. On its neck he should draw the syllable hūṁ upside down, and on its mid-torso, a five-pronged vajra scepter pointing upward. On both sides of its torso should be written twelve hūṁ syllables. Then, below, on the broad plinth of the caitya, {{note:{index:655,id:UT22084-079-008-2084}}} he should write the vowels, but without the four neuter letters ( ṛ, ṝ, ḷ, ḹ ). On the flat surface of the effigy’s chest he should write, as before, ‘May the counter-spells ruin those who injure my mind,’ {{note:{index:656,id:UT22084-079-008-2085}}} but this time in a straight line. He should also write the same in straight lines on its shanks and on its phallus. {{note:{index:657,id:UT22084-079-008-2086}}} On each of its eight limbs, he should write puṁ puṁ {{note:{index:658,id:UT22084-079-008-2087}}} raṁ . On the back of its hands, {{note:{index:659,id:UT22084-079-008-2088}}} he should write tāṁ tāṁ , and on its feet, puṁ {{note:{index:660,id:UT22084-079-008-2089}}} raṁ . He should have this effigy drawn using as ink poison, salt, black mustard, and neem leaf, mixed together with datura extract and charnel ground ash, while the moon is in the asterism of Puṣya. He should write ‘of such and such’ between the words of the mantra on the hub of the vajra scepter, using white sandalwood paste. For drawing the holy caitya he should likewise use white sandalwood paste, and for the vajra scepter with its hub he should use saffron. If he wears this with the spell inscribed on it, he will always have great protection. {7.3.66}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2090}} “The twenty-third method;
“He should draw Mount Sumeru with its eight spurs, adorned on top with a crossed, three-pronged, crossed vajra scepter. The spurs {{note:{index:661,id:UT22084-079-008-2092}}} should be marked, in the corner areas of the yantra, with the syllable naṁ, {{note:{index:662,id:UT22084-079-008-2093}}} and each enclosed by a pair of hūṁ syllables. He should write the four words alakta, kata, vāya , and māṃsaṃ {{note:{index:663,id:UT22084-079-008-2094}}} between each two cardinal directions, starting from the northeast. He should surround all this with a circular line, and at its center draw Gaṇapati. He should be depicted in the form of the lord of dance, with a dish of sweetmeats and a rosary in his right hands, a three-pronged vajra scepter and a leaf-crowned radish in his left hands, seated on a lotus, and riding a shrew. {7.3.67} {{page:{number:120,folio:F.133.a}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2095}} “The mantra to recite is:
“ Hūṁ gaḥ hūṁ hūṁ gaḥ gaḥ hūṁ ! Please send rain! Hūṁ gaḥ gaḥ hūṁ! {{note:{index:664,id:UT22084-079-008-2096}}} {7.3.68}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2097}} “He should write the short version of this mantra on the elephant god’s forehead, chest, hips, {{note:{index:665,id:UT22084-079-008-2098}}} and above the navel. If he draws this on unbaked earthenware using blood from his ring finger mixed with the three pungent substances, and heats it in a fire of cutch-tree wood, it will definitely bring rain—it cannot be otherwise. If he draws the same, but with orpiment instead on the inner surface of the earthenware, {{note:{index:666,id:UT22084-079-008-2099}}} and then heats it over fire, he will stop the rain. {7.3.69}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2100}} “The twenty-fourth method;
“He should draw a wheel with eight spokes and adorn it with eight gaḥ syllables. In its center, he should write the target’s name enclosed within the mantra, following the prescribed procedure. He should write this using orpiment and turmeric essence on a rag from a charnel ground or a rag that has been struck with a weapon. He should make an effigy of Gaṇapati from rice flour, placing this wheel in his chest. He should then put this effigy inside well-baked earthenware, wrap it on the outside with a yellow thread, and offer to it yellow flowers as prescribed. The rite described here, O goddess, is the supreme king of the rites of paralyzing. {7.3.70}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2102}} “The twenty-fifth method;
“He should write the following mantra in the center of the syllable māṁ:
“ Oṁ , Vattālī! Varālī! Varāhamukhī! Paralyze the mouths of all the most wicked evildoers! {{note:{index:667,id:UT22084-079-008-2105}}} {7.3.71}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2106}} “He should write this mantra using turmeric extract on two bricks. Having then joined them with a hollow in between, he should bury this device in the ground; it will paralyze all evildoers—it cannot be otherwise. {7.3.72}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2107}} “The twenty-sixth method;
“He should draw the yantra diagram on the ground in the form of a bhaga together with a liṅga, and write there the name of the target. Alone, he should urinate on this yantra for seven days until, following the procedure of surrounding her name with a noose formed from hrīḥ syllables, he causes the woman whom he desires to arrive. {7.3.73}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2109}} “The twenty-seventh method;
“He should draw a wheel with eight spokes in the center of a moon disk. In the divisions he should draw, in short, a vajra scepter, a banner, an axe, a trident, a noose, a double vajra scepter, {{page:{number:121,folio:F.133.b}}} a khaṭvāṅga, and a goad. In the center of the circle he should draw a full moon disk and, in the center of this moon, he should write, “May such and such a man and such and such a woman obtain a son.” {{note:{index:668,id:UT22084-079-008-2111}}} In the hub of the wheel he should write the following mantra:
“ Oṁ , Maṇidharī! Vajriṇī! Mahāpratisarā! Hūṁ hūṁ! Phaṭ phaṭ! Svāhā! {{note:{index:669,id:UT22084-079-008-2113}}} {7.3.74}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2114}} “Then, in the center of a moon disk, he should write this mantra:
“ Oṁ , Amṛtavilokinī! Protectress of the womb! Summoner of the being to be born! Hūṁ hūṁ! Phaṭ phaṭ! Svāhā! {{note:{index:670,id:UT22084-079-008-2116}}} {7.3.75}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2117}} “If he writes this mantra on birchbark using saffron and bovine orpiment while the moon is in the asterism of Puṣya, and wears it, he will obtain a son. {7.3.76}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2118}} “The twenty-eighth method;
“A wheel should be drawn in the shape of a pitcher with a neck, and the neck should be long. Following the prescibed procedure, he should write ‘ yaḥ plea yaḥ se yaḥ ex yaḥ pel yaḥ such yaḥ and yaḥ such yaḥ !’ {{note:{index:671,id:UT22084-079-008-2120}}} using crow’s blood as ink on a piece of cloth that was used as a banner in a temple of the supreme deity. He should write on it the name of the target and tie this to the neck of a live crow. He should then release the crow in the northwestern direction. Whoever’s name it was, this person will be exiled. {7.3.77}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2121}} “The twenty-ninth method;
“He should draw a wheel with eight spokes in the center of a sun disk. The syllable hūṁ —the elemental seed—should be nestled within it. He should visualize the vajra sun, {{note:{index:672,id:UT22084-079-008-2123}}} and then write the target’s name enclosed within the mantra. If the practitioner draws and writes this, as prescribed, on birchbark using saffron and bovine orpiment, and wears it, he will always be protected. {7.3.78}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2124}} “The thirtieth method;
“A lotus should be drawn with twenty-four petals, surrounded by a triple line. By writing oṁ hrīṁ klīṁ on it, as prescribed, while the moon is in the asterism of Puṣya, and holding it in his hand, he will be able to turn anyone into his servant with a mere touch of the hand. {7.3.79}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2126}} “The thirty-first method;
“A wheel should be drawn in the shape of a tambourine and adorned with a vajra scepter and a lotus. On the outside it should be surrounded with a triple line representing, in short, the vajra body, and so forth. By meditating intently on the vajra of action all his enemies will be crushed. And all activities will be accomplished with the mantras sanctioned by the ritual procedure. {{note:{index:673,id:UT22084-079-008-2128}}} The mantras are these:
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2129}} “ Oṁ , smother, smother! Hūṁ hūṁ, phaṭ! {{page:{number:122,folio:F.134.a}}} Oṁ , seize seize! Hūṁ hūṁ, phaṭ! Oṁ , hand them over, do! Hūṁ hūṁ, phaṭ ! Bring them over, O Lord Vidyārāja! Hūṁ hūṁ, phaṭ! Svāhā! {{note:{index:674,id:UT22084-079-008-2130}}} {7.3.80}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2131}} “The thirty-second method;
“The eighth syllable within the ya group ( ha ), Joined with the twelve vowels, {{note:{index:675,id:UT22084-079-008-2133}}} And with the six intermediary syllables ( hā, hī, hū, hai, hau, haḥ ) removed, Constitutes the six limbs of Heruka ( ha, hi, hu, he, ho, haṁ ). {{note:{index:676,id:UT22084-079-008-2134}}} {7.3.81}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2135}} “These six syllables are in union with the six-section mantra of the six heroes, And each syllable is assigned a place. The first one is the heart. The second is declared to be the head. {7.3.82}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2136}} “The third one should be assigned the topknot. The fourth will be the armor. The fifth will be the eyes, And the sixth is said to be the weapon. {7.3.83}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2137}} “He is together with Vajravārāhī, Adorned with four arms, Crowned by a divine yellow halo, And his hair is bedecked with a crescent moon. {7.3.84}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2138}} “He wears a necklace of human bone And has a khaṭvāṅga in his hand. Having thus generated himself as Heruka, He should stay mindful of being him. {7.3.85}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2139}} “In his heart he should visualize the wisdom being And place a perimeter wall in the four quarters. He should visualize him surrounded by flames of anger, Ferocious and adorned with frightening ornaments, {7.3.86}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2140}} “Driving away and nailing down the hordes of obstacle makers, and threatening the gods, demigods, and humans who dwell throughout all directions. Wearing his armor, {{note:{index:677,id:UT22084-079-008-2141}}} he cannot be destroyed even by the thirty-three gods. {{note:{index:678,id:UT22084-079-008-2142}}} {7.3.87}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2143}} “Next, he should draw a maṇḍala With four sides and four gates. In its center he should place A six-petaled lotus, complete with filaments. {7.3.88}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2144}} “Making it double, {{note:{index:679,id:UT22084-079-008-2145}}} the mantrin Should also draw the circle of ḍākinīs. On the pericarp, he should place the hero (Heruka) And, in addition, the ḍākinī. {7.3.89}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2146}} “The gates should be yellow all around And marked wih three-pronged vajra scepters. He should place the messenger goddesses at the inner sanctum, And likewise at the doors, according to the right order. {{note:{index:680,id:UT22084-079-008-2147}}} {7.3.90}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2148}} “If a lay vow holder wears this yantra-wheel, having first offered worship with many offerings when the planets were auspicious, he will be protected from untimely death, armed conflicts, and so forth. About my words, O goddess, there can be no doubt. {{page:{number:123,folio:F.134.b}}} This yantra-wheel is called ‘one which brings victory over enemies.’ {7.3.91}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2149}} “The thirty-third method;
“Alternatively, he should etch on a copper plate, during the asterism of Puṣya, the same wheel and mantra, but without the gates. The mantra should be interspersed with the target’s name. If he places it in water and makes offerings to it three times a day, then all enemies will become completely immobilized. When a well-focused practitioner of mantra puts this, as prescribed, in a covered pool that does not dry up, he can bring an appeasement. {7.3.92}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2151}} “The thirty-fourth method;
“There is also another yantra-wheel with four corners, four gates, and archways {{note:{index:681,id:UT22084-079-008-2153}}} adorned with vajra scepters. At the gates there should be respectively a vajra hammer, a bejeweled staff, a lotus, and a vajra sword. In the corners, inside white skull cups, there should be blue lotuses and goads. In the center among them there should be a lotus with ten petals, on which the wise practitioner should place the syllables. At its pericarp, he should write the following excellent mantra:
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2154}} “ Oṁ , Prasannatārā! One with the face and eyes of an immortal! Fulfiller of all aims! Svāhā! {{note:{index:682,id:UT22084-079-008-2155}}}
“He should write this mantra during rites of enthralling. {7.3.93}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2157}} “The thirty-fifth method;
“Now, for the rite of averting all mischief-makers, the following mantra has been prescribed:
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2159}} “ Oṁ , Tārā, you who bewilder everyone! Eager to save! Bewilder all evildoers, bewilder! Blessed one! Bind all evildoers, bind! Hūṁ hūṁ! Phaṭ! Svāhā! {{note:{index:683,id:UT22084-079-008-2160}}} {7.3.94}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2161}} “The thirty-sixth method;
“In the center of the aforementioned ten-petaled lotus he should depict a moon disk, and in the center of the moon disk he should draw the first letter of the fourth group ( ta ) in the form of lotus filament, which is circular in design. In the six divisions around its center he should place six syllables {{note:{index:684,id:UT22084-079-008-2163}}} of the mantric formula, interspersed with the syllable hrīḥ , following the prescribed procedure. This yantra-wheel is called ‘the beneficial influence of Tārā that vanquishes an entire army.’ {{note:{index:685,id:UT22084-079-008-2164}}} By reciting it 100,000 times, he can make the earth shake, dry up oceans and other water reservoirs, and turn poison into nectar, or nectar into poison. Having incanted a bowl of candied sugar, he should throw the sugar in the cardinal and intermediate directions, above and below. As a result, the gods, demigods, yakṣas, rākṣasas, gandharvas, kiṃnaras, and mahoragas will all become bound. {{page:{number:124,folio:F.135.a}}} He will steal magical potions from all the ḍākinīs and poisons from all the nāgas. If he incants candied sugar and throws it into a river, the river will flow upstream. With the same candied sugar he will be able to arrest the waves. If he recites the mantra 1,000 times while facing upward, he can prevent a heavy rain from falling. If he recites the mantra 1,000 times in the direction of an enemy army, and then enters battle, he will meet with no harm even when struck with hundreds of weapons. He cannot be chopped up. His body becomes a diamond body. He will perform many miracles, and will play with deities invoked by this king of mantras.” {7.3.95}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2165}} This concludes the third part of the seventh chapter, called “The Benefits of Yantra-Wheels Used for the Complete Range of Activity.”
Part 4
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2166}} [The goddess said:]
“May the lord explain the fine details Of consecration rites, how they should be performed— I do not know about the mantra recitation and meditation. And what is the right procedure for the rite of homa? {7.4.1}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2168}} “Blessed One, in your being you are the essence of vajra, The fusion of all sublime qualities. Please teach out of your kindness, You who possess great bliss, and are so difficult to find.” {7.4.2}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2169}} The Blessed One said:
“Listen O goddess! I will explain the act Of meditation according to its prescribed routine. Through methods involving merely meditation One will be able to accomplish all actions.” {7.4.3}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2171}} Then, to first explain the purification of the ground, the Blessed One said:
“One should assume the divine pride of Vajrasattva And establish oneself in the nonduality that accompanies such pride. Having become the conqueror of the three worlds, One should uproot all obstacle makers. {7.4.4}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2173}} “One should position one’s feet as instructed And so also the feet of the goddesses. {{note:{index:686,id:UT22084-079-008-2174}}} The homa rite should be as has been taught And so should be the characteristics of the fire pit. {7.4.5}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2175}} “Then one should apply the hand gestures, And later draw the maṇḍala. {7.4.6}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2176}} “Becoming the deity Krodhavijaya, one should visualize oneself as having three faces and six arms. {{page:{number:125,folio:F.135.b}}} One should radiate cloud masses of Krodhavijayas, which invoke all the tathāgatas and their retinues throughout the ten directions, supplicating them, ‘May you please attend to the places of consecration and provide protection for the teacher and his disciples.’ One should then absorb the Krodhavijayas, along with the supplicated tathāgatas, and internalize them, placing them in a hūṁ syllable at the hub of a vajra scepter on a moon disk in one’s heart. Having fused the form of Vajradhara, in union with his consort (vidyā), {{note:{index:687,id:UT22084-079-008-2177}}} with all the blessed tathāgatas, {{note:{index:688,id:UT22084-079-008-2178}}} one should form the mudrā called ‘the turning of the lotus,’ preceded by the blessing with the three-letter consecration, and then perform the required set of motions {{note:{index:689,id:UT22084-079-008-2179}}} with the vajra scepter in one’s right hand. With one’s left hand, one should sound the bell harmoniously. On the soles of one’s feet one should visualize a syllable hūṁ which transforms into a blazing vajra scepter. Then, with the pride of being Krodhavijaya who makes the sound hūṁ , a wise practitioner should expel all obstructors, first by exclaiming hūṁ , and then by addressing the following words, while visualizing {{note:{index:690,id:UT22084-079-008-2180}}} himself in Krodha’s form, to the gods, demigods, and guhyakas: {7.4.7}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2181}} “ ‘May all gods, demigods, yakṣas, rākṣasas, pretas, piśācas, apasmaras, bhūtas, ḍākinīs, ostārakas, male and female elders—all with their retinues of followers {{note:{index:691,id:UT22084-079-008-2182}}} —garuḍas, kiṃnaras, and semi-divine adepts of spells, depart! A regal maṇḍala of such and such a deity needs to be drawn at this place in order that such and such a student attains a perfect awakening under the guidance of such and such a master, and in order that all beings obtain unsurpassable wisdom. You must therefore swiftly depart upon hearing this command by Vajradhara. If anyone does not run away, then Vajrapāṇi, the blazing Hūṁkāra with an angry face, will split his head into a hundred pieces with the brightly shining vajra scepter of great wisdom!’ {7.4.8} {{page:{number:126,folio:F.136.a}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2183}} “When this command has been pronounced three times, he should radiate wrathful forms of himself as Krodhavijaya while doing the ritual movements with his great vajra scepter. {{note:{index:692,id:UT22084-079-008-2184}}} Walking around the maṇḍala ground, tempestuously, with a vajra step, he should drive away all mischief-makers. Thus should he claim the ground. {7.4.9}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2185}} “Then, having summoned the earth goddess, he should perform by means of the mantra the consecration and the tutelage rites. {{note:{index:693,id:UT22084-079-008-2186}}} He should pay homage to his master—his mantra instructor—and afterward summon, cause to enter, and bind the gold-colored earth goddess who is holding a pitcher in her hand. He should worship her with the five types of service involving fragrant perfume, and so forth. After he has made her occupy the maṇḍala ground, he should remain near her.” {7.4.10}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2187}} Now the Blessed One gave the mantra of summoning:
“ Oṁ , come, come! O great goddess, mother of the earthly realm, adorned with all the richly bejeweled ornaments, resounding with the tinkling of necklaces and anklets, you who are so bountifully worshiped by Vajrasattva! Take this welcome offering and bring success to the homa rites! Hrī hī hī hī haṁ! Svāhā !” {{note:{index:694,id:UT22084-079-008-2189}}} {7.4.11}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2190}} [And he continued further:]
“Having performed with this mantra the rite of the goddess’s tutelage over the maṇḍala, he should perform the anointing of the ground. He should thus sprinkle and smear the ground with feces, urine, and so forth. He should then cense it with an incense of human flesh. After censing the ground, he should make offerings, and then place the ‘seal’ in the center, meaning he should usher in the consort (vidyā).” {7.4.12}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2192}} Vajragarbha asked:
“Should he, O Blessed One, usher in a consort (vidyā)-goddess who has been cast or otherwise artificially made, drawn in whatever way, or fashioned from wood or other such materials?” {7.4.13}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2194}} The Blessed One replied:
“He should usher in a human girl of the cāṇḍāla or similar caste. If such cannot be procured, he should take one from a caste different from his own. {{note:{index:695,id:UT22084-079-008-2196}}} He should place the mantra syllables on her body. The syllable hrīḥ should be placed on all her limbs. The syllable hrīṁ should be placed on her chest, between her eyebrows, on her throat and head. The syllable bhruṁ should be placed in the center of her vulva.” {7.4.14}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2197}} “And where, {{note:{index:696,id:UT22084-079-008-2198}}} O Blessed One, should the syllable bhrūṁ be placed, [if it is placed] in the middle of her body?” {7.4.15} {{page:{number:127,folio:F.136.b}}}
The Blessed One replied:
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2200}} “By the word middle , O sons of the buddha family, navel is meant. There he should place the syllable bhrūṁ. {{note:{index:697,id:UT22084-079-008-2201}}} Having thus {{note:{index:698,id:UT22084-079-008-2202}}} placed the syllables, he should visualize the forms of Locanā and other tathāgata consorts . At this point, he should visualize a brahmin or a śūdra consort in the form of Locanā—if it is the rite of pacifying, it should be the form of Locanā. He should visualize her as white and adorned with all manner of jewelry. If it is the rite of enthralling, he should visualize a woman from the cāṇḍāla caste in the form of red Tārā. If it is the rite of enriching, he should visualize a dancer woman or a woman of royal lineage as the yellow Pāṇḍaravāsinī. Thus, following the divisions of the types of activity, he should worship the consort with the five types of service, and offer a handful of flowers. He should place on her vulva blood or {{note:{index:699,id:UT22084-079-008-2203}}} semen. {{note:{index:700,id:UT22084-079-008-2204}}} In this way, the ground where the homa rite is to take place will be purified. {7.4.16}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2205}} “A girl, one from a caste different than his own, {{note:{index:701,id:UT22084-079-008-2206}}} should be instructed in the maṇḍala procedure. As this pertains to the maṇḍala, she should also be instructed in the rites of homa, including the secret maṇḍala of phenomena. Following this rule, he should measure out a twofold maṇḍala—the external one of colored powders, and the secret maṇḍala of phenomena that concerns his own samaya. Accordingly, he should prepare a sacrificial fire pit in an area that is a place of pilgrimage for yogins.”
So spoke the Blessed One. {7.4.17}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2208}} And he said further:
“I will now teach the rite of homa That makes different rites effective. {{note:{index:702,id:UT22084-079-008-2210}}} Those gods among whom Agni is the foremost {{note:{index:703,id:UT22084-079-008-2211}}} Are dependent upon the principle of homa. {{note:{index:704,id:UT22084-079-008-2212}}} {7.4.18}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2213}} “Through oblation the gods are satiated; When satiated, they grant success. Mantras that are recited inadequately or excessively, All become complete through homa. {7.4.19}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2214}} “Therefore homa is praised By the vajrins who possess the three bodies. {{note:{index:705,id:UT22084-079-008-2215}}} The fire obtained by whirling a stick {{note:{index:706,id:UT22084-079-008-2216}}} Will make the rite beneficial. {7.4.20}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2217}} “The fire obtained from an untouchable or from a charnel ground Will be effective in rites that bring harm. {{note:{index:707,id:UT22084-079-008-2218}}} The pit should be round, or square, Or shaped like a crescent moon, or triangular. {7.4.21} {{page:{number:128,folio:F.137.a}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2219}} “With its boundary marked with vajra scepters, The pit should fit within the outer circle. {{note:{index:708,id:UT22084-079-008-2220}}} He who knows the nature of homa {{note:{index:709,id:UT22084-079-008-2221}}} should place In the center of the pit, on top of a lotus, {7.4.22}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2222}} “A diadem, a lotus, a vajra scepter, or a jewel, [Depending on which of the rites is being performed]. {{note:{index:710,id:UT22084-079-008-2223}}} He should sit [facing the direction] as specified [for each rite], With his elbows between the knees. {7.4.23}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2224}} “The ladle for liquids should overflow with ghee So that the [solids] to be offered {{note:{index:711,id:UT22084-079-008-2225}}} become saturated. {{note:{index:712,id:UT22084-079-008-2226}}} On the right side should be the materials to be burned, {{note:{index:713,id:UT22084-079-008-2227}}} And on the left, a dish with water. {7.4.24}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2228}} “In front, there should be a dish with the welcome offering. While chanting the ‘all-purpose’ mantra, he should perform the rites of sprinkling and sipping of water. He should encircle the pit all around with the straight tips of kuśa grass blades. {7.4.25}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2229}} “Observing that the fire has started, He should summon the fire deity With the following mantra, following the rule, Moving his right thumb in a gesture of fearlessness: {{note:{index:714,id:UT22084-079-008-2230}}} {7.4.26}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2231}} “Come, come, O great god of beings, Best among the sages and twice born! Take the oblatory food And approach me!
“ Oṁ , fire, blaze, blaze! Penetrate, O splendorous one, to carry away this burnt offering, svāhā! {{note:{index:715,id:UT22084-079-008-2233}}} {7.4.27}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2234}} “He should consecrate the five articles of offering, Besprinkling them with the vajra scepter held in his left hand. He should visualize, arriving from the southeast, The god of fire with protruding belly, three eyes, {7.4.28}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2235}} “Four faces, four arms, red in color, And matted hair tied in a topknot. He is in the midst of a circle of fire And is adorned with the light rays {{note:{index:716,id:UT22084-079-008-2236}}} of the four activities. {7.4.29}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2237}} “His first right hand is in the boon-granting gesture; In the second, he holds a rosary of rudrākṣa beads. In the first left hand he holds a water pitcher, And in the second, a staff. {7.4.30}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2238}} “He is bedecked with red adornments And surrounded by a retinue of sages. Visualizing him in this form, He should cause him to enter the fire pit. {7.4.31}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2239}} “The burnt offerings should be offered three times, Using up all the articles to be burned. Next, he should perform the ritual sipping of water, And thereby transform the offerings into the form of flames. {7.4.32}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2240}} “By applying this method stage by stage The wise practitioner will satiate the deity. Having satiated and propitiated him, He should tell him what accomplishments he desires. {7.4.33} {{page:{number:129,folio:F.137.b}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2241}} “Playfully he may assume the shapes of a parasol, A banner, a vajra scepter, a pitcher, a lotus, and a goad. His flames will have one, two, or three tongues, Shooting high, or burning low, or medium height. The wise practitioner will interpret these signs: In particular, if the flames swirl clockwise {7.4.34}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2242}} “And have a bright white color, He will interpret this as boding well. The flames may have the pure colors of a rainbow, Be smooth, and have the radiance of a firefly. {7.4.35}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2243}} “They may have the same hue as saffron or beryl, And be fragrant and pleasing to the mind, Shining like gold or silver, without smoke, Burning with the pure radiance of the sun. {7.4.36}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2244}} “White-colored flames are suitable for the rites of pacifying; For the rites of enriching they should be yellow. They should be red for acts of impassioning, {{note:{index:717,id:UT22084-079-008-2245}}} And an exquisite deep blue or black for rites of assaulting. {7.4.37}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2246}} “Likewise, he should observe whether the fire has many flames and belches smoke and sparks, or whether it gradually rises or very slowly wanes. The fire may look unpleasant, or be dark green in color; it may resemble a spear or a sun, or the head of a cow. It may smell of a corpse or a cow, or possibly a donkey. He should thus divine by the signs of the fire whether there will be obstacles, and if so, he should neutralize them. {{note:{index:718,id:UT22084-079-008-2247}}} {7.4.38}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2248}} “If he relies on mantra recitation and meditation, Every accomplishment will soon follow. {7.4.39}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2249}} “The mantra should begin with oṁ and end with svāhā. For the rites of pacifying, enriching, and enthralling, He should chant it as a song Without any breaks between individual sounds. {7.4.40}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2250}} “For the rite of pacifying, the practitioner should have a peaceful mind. For enriching, increase will come through adopting a satiated frame of mind. During the rite of enthralling, his mind should be enthralled, Intoxicated with love, and full of amorous wantonness. {7.4.41}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2251}} “If he follows the procedure for the rites of assaulting, He should engender thoughts of devouring the three realms. He should employ the syllables hūṁ and phaṭ While visualizing his body ablaze with flames. {7.4.42}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2252}} “He should intersperse the words of supplication, Combining them with the syllables of the mantra. {{page:{number:130,folio:F.138.a}}} Whatever gods are employed for whomever’s sake, {{note:{index:719,id:UT22084-079-008-2253}}} He should worship them with various rites. {7.4.43}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2254}} “The mantra adept who is familiar with the rules Involved in all the procedures of the homa rite Should first offer the complete burnt offering And then commence with the activity. {{note:{index:720,id:UT22084-079-008-2255}}} {7.4.44}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2256}} “He should supplicate the deity employing the essence {{note:{index:721,id:UT22084-079-008-2257}}} of homa— This is the procedure to follow when offering homa. In the rites of pacifying, enriching, or enthralling, The homa should consist of semen. {{note:{index:722,id:UT22084-079-008-2258}}} {7.4.45}
“Through the homa consisting of feces, urine, blood, bone marrow, bones, and human flesh, all the recipients become filled with joy.” {{note:{index:723,id:UT22084-079-008-2260}}} {7.4.46}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2261}} Then the Blessed One, having entered the samādhi called “The Vajra That Accomplishes the Wisdom Circle of the Vajra-Tathāgata Great Vairocana,” {{note:{index:724,id:UT22084-079-008-2262}}} taught the elaborate outer and inner ritual methods for accomplishing the complete wisdom circle: {7.4.47}
“Whatever deity is brought inside the center of the circle, that circle is praised by the buddhas as the vajra maṇḍala that is to be indicated with the name of that deity. {7.4.48}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2264}} “He should perform the rites of pacifying, enriching, Enthralling, and assaulting with authority, Applying thereto the powers of wisdom Of the maṇḍala’s main deity. {7.4.49}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2265}} “He should visualize inside the bhaga {{note:{index:725,id:UT22084-079-008-2266}}} The disk of a full moon, and on it, Arising out of the imagined syllable tāṁ, The goddess Tārā, she who has great magical powers. {7.4.50}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2267}} “She is imbued with the sentiment of erotic love; she has sixteen arms and seven faces, {{note:{index:726,id:UT22084-079-008-2268}}} each one with three eyes, and is smiling. She is emerald in color {{note:{index:727,id:UT22084-079-008-2269}}} and replete with the freshness of youth. She wears brightly colored clothes, a pearl necklace, anklets, a choker, a diadem, arm bracelets, {{note:{index:728,id:UT22084-079-008-2270}}} earrings, a waist chain, and so forth. She is adorned with different kinds of jewelry; her hair is adorned with a blue lotus flower and her body hue resembles barley flowers. {{note:{index:729,id:UT22084-079-008-2271}}} She stands with her left leg outstretched and her right slightly bent, inspiring fear even in the masters of the realms of the thirty-three (Indra) who fold their hands in a gesture of reverence. She is ablaze with red flames and surrounded by buddhas radiating light all around. If the practitioner visualizes her, the dear mother of all sentient beings, as such, he will swiftly attain the state of awakening. {7.4.51} {{page:{number:131,folio:F.138.b}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2272}} “In her first right hand she holds a sword; in the second, a blue lotus; in the third, an arrow; in the fourth, a vajra scepter; in the fifth, a goad; in the sixth, a staff; in the seventh, a flaying knife; and with the eighth she displays the mudrā of fearlessness. In her first left hand she holds a human skull cup; with the second she displays the threatening mudrā; in the third she holds a bow; in the fourth, a khaṭvāṅga; in the fifth, a noose; in the sixth, a trident; {{note:{index:730,id:UT22084-079-008-2273}}} in the seventh, a jewel; and in the eighth, a pitcher. {7.4.52}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2274}} “Her first face on the right side is blue, and the second one blazes with the color yellow. The first face on the left side is white, and the second has the greenish color of beryl. Her upper face bares its fangs, and is smoky in color, frighteningly contorted, hideous, and terrifying. So should he visualize the goddess who bounteously bestows all accomplishments. {7.4.53}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2275}} “Further above, he should visualize another face with the form of a donkey’s, or some other desired form. {{note:{index:731,id:UT22084-079-008-2276}}} With her four feet, a trident, and snakes wrapped around, she is referred to as “Herukī,” {{note:{index:732,id:UT22084-079-008-2277}}} and should be visualized as the ultimate cause of accomplishments. {{note:{index:733,id:UT22084-079-008-2278}}} Inside the bhaga {{note:{index:734,id:UT22084-079-008-2279}}} he should visualize, arising from the syllable yaṁ , the maṇḍala of wind, which has the appearance of smoke. Above it, in the center of a moon disk, he should visualize himself in the form of Mañjuśrī transformed from the syllable dhīḥ . In his heart he should visualize a sun disk transformed from the syllable āḥ . From this sun disk, he should radiate rays of light and make offerings with them as prescribed. Above the sun disk, he should visualize the syllable hūṁ made of five-colored light. This syllable is transformed into Vajrabhairava with nine faces and the form of a buffalo. He has sixteen feet and thirty-four arms. He is naked and black in color with great brilliance. The crown of his head is adorned with five skulls and he inspires great fear. He stands with his left leg outstretched and his right slightly bent, with his liṅga erect. He has a protruding belly, a huge body, and upward flowing hair resembling a blazing sun. He is adorned with a garland of skulls and other ornaments. {{page:{number:132,folio:F.139.a}}} He makes a roaring sound like at the time of the final dissolution of the world. He should visualize him consuming human blood, fat, serum, flesh, lymph, and bone marrow, {{note:{index:735,id:UT22084-079-008-2280}}} while devouring the triple universe along with Brahmā, Indra, {{note:{index:736,id:UT22084-079-008-2281}}} Upendra, Rudra, and so forth. {7.4.54}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2282}} “With his loud laughter and lolling tongue he frightens even fear itself. His first face is that of a buffalo. On his right horn there are three faces—blue, red, and yellow—each contorted with anger. On the left horn, the three faces are white, smoky, and black. Between the two horns there is an intensely red face with blood streaming from its mouth. Above it there is the princely youth Mañjuśrī, intensely yellow, semi-wrathful, wearing the ornaments of youth and a crown of five strips of cloth. Having stabilized this visualization, the mantra adept should cultivate himself as the deity with a well-focused mind. {7.4.55}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2283}} “Furthermore, in his first hand on the right, Vajrabhairava holds a flaying knife; in the second, a javelin; in the third, a mace; in the fourth, a small knife; in the fifth, a half-spear; {{note:{index:737,id:UT22084-079-008-2284}}} in the sixth, an axe; in the seventh, a spear; in the eighth, an arrow; in the ninth, a goad; in the tenth, a club; in the eleventh, a khaṭvāṅga; in the twelfth, a discus; in the thirteenth, a vajra scepter; in the fourteenth, a vajra hammer; in the fifteenth, a sword; and in the sixteenth, a ḍamaru. {7.4.56}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2285}} “On the left side, in his first hand, he holds a skull cup; in the second, a human head; in the third, a shield; in the fourth, a foot; in the fifth, a noose; in the sixth, a bow; in the seventh, entrails; in the eighth, a bell; in the ninth, a hand; in the tenth, a rag from a charnel ground; in the eleventh, a man impaled on a stake; in the twelfth, a fire pit; and in the thirteenth, a goblet. {{note:{index:738,id:UT22084-079-008-2286}}} With the fourteenth he displays the threatening mudrā; {{page:{number:133,folio:F.139.b}}} with the fifteenth, a hand gesture with three fingers stretched out; and in the sixteenth, he holds a ‘wind-cloth.’ With the remaining pair of hands he holds an elephant hide. {7.4.57}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2287}} “Under his right foot there are men, buffaloes, bulls, donkeys, camels, dogs, rams, and jackals. Under his left foot there are vultures, owls, crows, parrots, hawks, cocks, {{note:{index:739,id:UT22084-079-008-2288}}} eagles, and cranes. {{note:{index:740,id:UT22084-079-008-2289}}} He should visualize Vajrabhairava as such. Optionally, he should commission a painting of him. {7.4.58}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2290}} “Below Vajrabhairava he should visualize a great cemetery overrun with rākṣasas, kṣetrapālas, and vetālas; filled with humans impaled on stakes, humans hanged from banyan trees, {{note:{index:741,id:UT22084-079-008-2291}}} burning humans, humans pierced with spears, lots of crows and other birds, and dogs; and resounding with disquieting laughter, hā hā . So should the practitioner visualize the Great Bhairava who makes all cruel rites successful.” {7.4.59}
So spoke the Blessed One. {{note:{index:742,id:UT22084-079-008-2293}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2294}} “Next, he should visualize arising from the syllable māṁ The goddess Mārīcī, as bright as the sun, Riding on a chariot drawn by seven horses And radiant {{note:{index:743,id:UT22084-079-008-2295}}} with a halo of flames around her. {7.4.60}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2296}} “Each of her three faces has three eyes. She is yellow and has six arms. The face on the right is blue; The one on the left is the color of jasmine flowers or the moon. {7.4.61}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2297}} “She is resplendent with the light of manifold rays. She is engaged in guarding the ten directions. Being in the throes of youth she is smiling, with all her faces Expressing the sentiment of erotic love. {7.4.62}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2298}} “Her body is adorned with various garments And bedecked with all types of jewelry. Her crown is set with the five buddhas And her matted hair adorned with flowers. {7.4.63}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2299}} “In her first right hand she carries a vajra scepter; In the second, a threaded needle; And in the third, she holds up an arrow. With her first left hand she displays a threatening gesture and carries a noose; {7.4.64}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2300}} “In the second, she carries an aśoka sprout; And in the third, a bow. She is surrounded by multicolored light That radiates cloud-like masses of buddhas. {7.4.65} {{page:{number:134,folio:F.140.a}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2301}} “While this is being visualized, {{note:{index:744,id:UT22084-079-008-2302}}} living beings Are brought to the state of enthrallment.”
So spoke the Blessed Vajra holder, The tathāgata Vajrasattva. {7.4.66}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2304}} “In the center of the expanse of the sky He should visualize a sun disk. On it, transformed from the syllable paṁ, {{note:{index:745,id:UT22084-079-008-2305}}} Is the goddess Parṇaśāvarī, yellow in color and with great splendor. {7.4.67}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2306}} “Each of her three faces has three eyes, And the faces are smiling and angry at the same time. She is beautified by all manner of adornments; She has six arms and is endowed with the freshness of youth. {7.4.68}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2307}} “In her first right hand she holds a vajra scepter; in the second, an axe; and in the third, an arrow. {7.4.69}
“In her first left hand, formed into a threatening gesture, She holds a noose; In the second, a feather chowrie; and in the third, a bow. Her topknot is adorned with flowers. {7.4.70}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2309}} “She stands on a white lotus, Adorned by a red glow. Engulfed in the flames of the fire of rage, She inspires fear with her burning rage. {7.4.71}
“Any grahas that harm living beings are burned. {7.4.72}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2311}} “Ablaze with anger, she is unshakable, {{note:{index:746,id:UT22084-079-008-2312}}} With Akṣobhya mounted on her head. She is nevertheless white {{note:{index:747,id:UT22084-079-008-2313}}} when raining down The five-colored {{note:{index:748,id:UT22084-079-008-2314}}} nectar of the five buddhas. {7.4.73}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2315}} “Her right and left faces {{note:{index:749,id:UT22084-079-008-2316}}} are as previously described. {{note:{index:750,id:UT22084-079-008-2317}}} So should the practitioner meditate for the sake of pacifying all illusion that stems from misapprehension. {{note:{index:751,id:UT22084-079-008-2318}}} Parṇaśāvarī truly is the remover of all illnesses.”
So spoke the blessed tathāgata Great Vajra. {{note:{index:752,id:UT22084-079-008-2320}}} {7.4.74}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2321}} “Listen, O goddess, O very fortunate one, About the meditation on Vajrakrodha! {{note:{index:753,id:UT22084-079-008-2322}}} Assuming his form, [The practitioner] should visualize him, the lord of anger, {7.4.75}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2323}} “As having four arms and four faces, Or up to 100,000 arms and faces. His body is white, he is fiercely angry, and he gazes at Vajravārāhī, Who is of the same color as him and holds her usual implements. {7.4.76}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2324}} “He wears a garland of skulls; His limbs are smeared with ashes. He is adorned with the five mudrās, And his hair, tied in a topknot, is marked with a spear-point. {7.4.77}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2325}} “His face, with fangs showing slightly, is terrible. {{page:{number:135,folio:F.140.b}}} His seat is made of the great preta, {{note:{index:754,id:UT22084-079-008-2326}}} In the center of an eight-petaled lotus. He is red in color, with the same hue all over. {7.4.78}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2327}} “He is adorned with an image of a buddha on top of his head, And accompanied by four wisdom goddesses. Each of the four has the form of a horse, and so forth, Four arms, four faces, and is bedecked with adornments made of serpents. {7.4.79}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2328}} “He is furnished with individual syllables, one at a time, {{note:{index:755,id:UT22084-079-008-2329}}} Stands on a human skull, and is white in color. He is adorned with four faces, And ornamented with the syllables ya, ra, la , and va. {{note:{index:756,id:UT22084-079-008-2330}}} {7.4.80}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2331}} “He should then commence the practice, to the extent possible, according to procedure. Starting from the northwest and following the order of the quarters, he should [visualize the deity {{note:{index:757,id:UT22084-079-008-2332}}} adorned with elements] in the colors of smoke, red, yellow, and white, respectively. Merely by visualizing this in meditation, he can make a woman drip {{note:{index:758,id:UT22084-079-008-2333}}} like an incised milk tree—it cannot be otherwise. {7.4.81}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2334}} “[Alternatively, Vajrakrodha is visualized] as red, With four arms, and marked with the syllable raṁ. He is surrounded by a halo of flames and terrifying; He has four faces and is adorned with an [upper] face of a jackal. {7.4.82}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2335}} “Visualizing tiny vajra scepters, Transformed from the syllable hūṁ And emerging in great numbers from the tip of his nose, He should fill the target’s body with them. {7.4.83}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2336}} “With the target’s body bound At all its joints by the double vajra scepters, His body is set ablaze and gushes blood Through being struck with the vajra scepter. {{note:{index:759,id:UT22084-079-008-2337}}} {7.4.84}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2338}} “He should visualize Vajraḍākinīs Sucking {{note:{index:760,id:UT22084-079-008-2339}}} the target’s blood from every side. {7.4.85}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2340}} “The mantra to recite is:
“ Oṁ , Vajraḍākinī! Please draw the blood of such and such! Hūṁ phaṭ! {{note:{index:761,id:UT22084-079-008-2342}}} {7.4.86}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2343}} “The ultimate way to draw blood Is through this method with its stages. So it has been taught, O goddess! There is no doubt that the target will wither. {7.4.87}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2344}} “Now, he should visualize Vajrakrodha in the terrifying Form of a buffalo, arisen completely from the true essence. He is black and horrible, With four frightening faces. {7.4.88}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2345}} “He has eight arms and four feet. In his four right hands he is holding, respectively, a vajra hammer, a sword, a discus, and a ḍamaru. In the left ones he holds a khaṭvāṅga, a skull cup, a bow, and a noose. {7.4.89}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2346}} “He should then emanate Vajrakrodhas Armed with a variety of weapons. He should mentally remove The target’s protection according to procedure. {7.4.90} {{page:{number:136,folio:F.141.a}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2347}} “He should visualize the target Being bound by those Vajrakrodhas with fetters And dragged in the southern direction, While being struck by other Vajrakrodhas with vajra scepters {7.4.91}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2348}} “And cut open by them with swords, With feces flowing from his ripped entrails. {7.4.92}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2349}} “The mantra to repeat is:
“ Oṁ , Vajrarākṣasa, devour him! Phaṭ! {{note:{index:762,id:UT22084-079-008-2351}}} {7.4.93}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2352}} “He should then meditate on Vajrarākṣasa, visualizing him with a dog’s face. {7.4.94}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2353}} “The following mantra is of Yama in his buffalo-faced form:
“ Oṁ, hrīḥ ṣṭrīḥ ! You with contorted face! Hūṁ hūṁ hūṁ phaṭ! Svāhā! {{note:{index:763,id:UT22084-079-008-2355}}} {7.4.95}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2356}} “He should visualize the target surrounded On all sides by crows, jackals, and vultures; While supplicating, he should visualize The target being torn to pieces by them. {7.4.96}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2357}} “He should then visualize [a camel] {{note:{index:764,id:UT22084-079-008-2358}}} with teeth of diamond, Mounted on a maṇḍala of the element of wind. He should visualize the target Mounted on its back {7.4.97}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2359}} “And tormented by Vajrakrodha, While being led in the southern direction. Using ink made from leaves whirled up by the wind And dust from the target’s footprint, {7.4.98}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2360}} “He should write the target’s name And conceal it in a camel’s hoof. {{note:{index:765,id:UT22084-079-008-2361}}} Employing the visualization as described, He should perform the rite according to procedure. {7.4.99}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2362}} “He will then be able to drive away even Śakra, Let alone ordinary earthly people. {7.4.100}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2363}} “He should obtain the bodily hair of a brahmin and a monk, {{note:{index:766,id:UT22084-079-008-2364}}} And wrap with them [two] feathers of an owl, [one with each]. He should write targets’ names on them, interspersed with the mantra, And bury them in the ground, confining them to obstruct each other. {{note:{index:767,id:UT22084-079-008-2365}}} {7.4.101}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2366}} “He should visualize them As two Vajrakrodhas fighting. Visualizing in this way, the practitioner Will be able to sow enmity between whomever he wants. {7.4.102}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2367}} “By visualizing the deity with the face of a horse In conjunction with the syllable cī, {{note:{index:768,id:UT22084-079-008-2368}}} He will accomplish the ultimate Drawing forth of wine [from the target’s stomach]. {{note:{index:769,id:UT22084-079-008-2369}}} {7.4.103}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2370}} “The great king Hayagrīva Is effectively the supreme master. He is visualized as yellow-green, {{note:{index:770,id:UT22084-079-008-2371}}} With four faces and four hands. {{note:{index:771,id:UT22084-079-008-2372}}} {7.4.104}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2373}} “His main face is dark green with a hint of yellow, and has three eyes. The faces on the right and left are black and white respectively. The upper face is that of a horse; it is yellow-green {{note:{index:772,id:UT22084-079-008-2374}}} and terrible looking with bared fangs. With his first right hand he displays the mudrā of three outstretched fingers; {{page:{number:137,folio:F.141.b}}} in the second, he holds a double vajra scepter; in the third, a sword; and in the fourth, an arrow. In his first left hand he holds a multicolored lotus; in the second, a spear; in the third, a mirror; and in the fourth, a bow. He is standing on a sun disk with his left leg outstretched and the right slightly bent, and dancing the wild tāṇḍava dance, knocking down Viṣṇu, Śiva, and so forth. {{note:{index:773,id:UT22084-079-008-2375}}} In this way should the follower of the mantra path meditate, following the right procedure. {7.4.105}
“In the target’s navel, he should visualize the syllable māṁ {{note:{index:774,id:UT22084-079-008-2377}}} and, arising from it, the target with a belly full of wine. When he subsequently visualizes him as vomiting, {{note:{index:775,id:UT22084-079-008-2378}}} the target will throw up wine. {7.4.106}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2379}} “As for the next rite, the wise practitioner should walk toward the northwest and create there a maṇḍala with four corners. Using perfume, he should prepare seven drops and store them in an earthenware vessel. He should visualize that this transforms into Sumeru, with eight peaks arranged in a circle, surmounted with a flashing vajra scepter, with the seven seeds— yaṁ syllables—of wind inside it, {{note:{index:776,id:UT22084-079-008-2380}}} confining thus the in-breath of the Great Indra in its interior, and marked at the top with the syllable laṁ. {{note:{index:777,id:UT22084-079-008-2381}}} When this rite is performed in this way, he will stop the wind as if it were annihilated. {7.4.107}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2382}} “As for the next rite, he should visualize an eight-petaled lotus, placing the eight nāgas on the petals, and a peacock, blazing with flames, in the center. {{note:{index:778,id:UT22084-079-008-2383}}} Assuming the form of Vajrakrodha, he should squeeze the serpents with the heel of his foot, causing them to vomit rainclouds. Should he squeeze a nāga while reciting the syllable hūṁ in pairs, with the seed syllable of the nāgas {{note:{index:779,id:UT22084-079-008-2384}}} thrown in between, he will cause rain to fall. {7.4.108}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2385}} “As for the next rite, he should visualize in the sky a gaping mouth, as red as the light of the sun that causes the dissolution of the world. {{note:{index:780,id:UT22084-079-008-2386}}} Its tongue, bright with the syllable hūṁ , licks the clouds filled with the seven waters, summoning them. Through its inhaling and exhaling, the mouth then scatters the clouds like tufts of cotton wool. He should then send forth a multitude of replicas {{note:{index:781,id:UT22084-079-008-2387}}} of himself. He will instantly rend the sky and cause it to open, threatening it with the syllable hūṁ . {7.4.109} {{page:{number:138,folio:F.142.a}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2388}} “As for the next rite, he should visualize Acalaceṭa with the color of an autumn sky, standing on a fiery disk, emerging from the center of [the practitioner’s] forehead. He is equal to Vairocana and has six hands which hold a sword, a noose, an arrow, a bow, a bell, and a vajra scepter. {{note:{index:782,id:UT22084-079-008-2389}}} Sending down rain, and surrounded by countless Krodhavajras, he vanquishes Māras, frightens away all troublemakers, and destroys even the entire triple universe by filling it with the resonance of hūṁ . {7.4.110}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2390}} “As for the next rite, he should sculpt a human effigy from human blood mixed with soil from the footprint of the target. He should nail it through the eyes with a spike made of human bone and incant it twenty times with the mantra of Mārīcī. Immediately after chanting the mantra, he should place the effigy in the mouth of an image of Gaṇapati and smash it from behind with a vajra cudgel, while repeating the mantra:
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2391}} “ Oṁ , smother, smother! {{note:{index:783,id:UT22084-079-008-2392}}} Reduce the obstacle makers to dust with your vajra cudgel! Hūṁ phaṭ! {{note:{index:784,id:UT22084-079-008-2393}}}
“Through this meditative act he will instantly {{note:{index:785,id:UT22084-079-008-2395}}} ward off human miscreants. {7.4.111}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2396}} “As for the next rite, he should visualize the deity with silver-colored eyes, {{note:{index:786,id:UT22084-079-008-2397}}} with his body adorned by hundreds of thousands of nāgas, issuing a command to the eight nāgas. These nāgas, for their part, should be visualized situated in the sky, with hundreds of thousands of faces. Upon hearing the command, they avert the rain with cloud masses. {7.4.112}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2398}} “As for the next rite, he should visualize a garuḍa blowing out fire by making wind with its wings, while creating a river with a stroke of its beak. {{note:{index:787,id:UT22084-079-008-2399}}} Visualizing thus, he should recite the mantra:
“ Oṁ , Vajranārāyaṇa! Extinguish the fire by bringing new water-bearing clouds! Hūṁ! {{note:{index:788,id:UT22084-079-008-2401}}} {7.4.113}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2402}} “In the middle of the sky, [he should visualize Kurukullā Tārā {{note:{index:789,id:UT22084-079-008-2403}}} ] with three faces, each of them with three eyes. She is adorned with all types of jewelry and wears a tunic of tiger skin. She is red, intensely brilliant, with the same brightness as the rising sun. {7.4.114}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2404}} “She holds a sword, a khaṭvāṅga, A bow, and an arrow, As well as a skull cup with human flesh, A ḍamaru, {7.4.115}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2405}} “A noose, and a goad. [In her fifth pair of hands] She is graced, in the left hand, with a lotus, And displays the mudrā of fearlessness with the right. {{note:{index:790,id:UT22084-079-008-2406}}} {7.4.116}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2407}} “Terrifying, she stands on a sun disk with her left leg outstretched and the right slightly bent, Dancing the wild tāṇḍava dance, and enveloped in red flames. {{page:{number:139,folio:F.142.b}}} [With her remaining pair of hands] she spreads above a canopy of a “great garment.” {{note:{index:791,id:UT22084-079-008-2408}}} She performs these acts in a charnel ground. {7.4.117}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2409}} “She is the goddess arising from the syllable hrīṁ, Tārā, the one who delivers from saṃsāra. By merely visualizing in this way, The practitioner will attain awakening, Not to mention other siddhis. {7.4.118}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2410}} “Now, if he wishes to enthrall someone, he should, on the eighth day of the first half of the month Caitra, go under the canopy of an aśoka tree {{note:{index:792,id:UT22084-079-008-2411}}} and, dressed in red and adorned with all kinds of adornments, recite the mantra. He should visualize himself as red with three faces. Then, he should emanate from his body a two-armed red goddess with a goad and a noose in her hands. He should then visualize this goddess piercing the target through the heart with the goad and leading him into his own body. She makes him enter there in a state of confusion. In his heart one should place the ten-syllable mantra, {{note:{index:793,id:UT22084-079-008-2412}}} visualized in red. He should further cause the target to enter, in his mental body form, into these syllables, and visualize him merging with them. Through this meditative method he will be able, after seven days, to enthrall even a universal monarch for as long as he lives—there is no doubt about this.” {7.4.119}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2413}} Now, to help ward off the dangers of lightning, the Blessed One said:
“He should visualize himself in the form of the glorious primordial lord with three faces, four feet, four arms, and a luminous red glow. He is surrounded by four goddesses whose names begin with [or include the word] vajra —they are Vajrāstrā, Vajrakelīkilā, {{note:{index:794,id:UT22084-079-008-2415}}} Snehavajrā, and Vajragarvā. They each raise a vajra scepter with one of their right hands and hold an arrow with the other, proudly resting one of their left hands on the hip, while holding a bow with the other. {{note:{index:795,id:UT22084-079-008-2416}}} He should visualize, emanating from the lord’s body, clouds composed of buddhas adorned with all kinds of jewelry. Staying in the middle of the sky, they display the gesture of fearlessness with their right hand, and hold a jeweled, dripping initiation vase with the other. {{note:{index:796,id:UT22084-079-008-2417}}} Such will avert lightning. {7.4.120} {{page:{number:140,folio:F.143.a}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2418}} “The mantra to recite is:
“ Oṁ , Mahāsukhavajratejaḥ! Hūṁ! {{note:{index:797,id:UT22084-079-008-2420}}} {7.4.121}
“When the same rite involves binding sexual ecstasy, it is said to bring about the state of the highest yoga.” {{note:{index:798,id:UT22084-079-008-2422}}} {7.4.122}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2423}} Concerning the rite of killing, the Blessed One taught the following:
“He should leave out the syllables used in the rite of pacifying, Namely the final ya , the two ni syllables, And then the middle ya syllable, And use the remaining syllables as one likes. {7.4.123}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2425}} “By having explained such, O goddess, All rites will be accomplished. {7.4.124}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2426}} “If he wants to enthrall a wanton woman, he should once again {{note:{index:799,id:UT22084-079-008-2427}}} assume, on the eighth day of the bright fortnight, the identity of Kurukullā and do her meditation. He should consume a fruit of downy datura, and then respectfully give {{note:{index:800,id:UT22084-079-008-2428}}} the target a tilaka on the forehead using juice of black nightshade. He should then recite the following mantra:
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2429}} “ Oṁ , may such and such a woman, hrīṁ , become enthralled with me! {{note:{index:801,id:UT22084-079-008-2430}}}
“When he has completed 10,000 recitations, she will arrive. {7.4.125}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2432}} “Now, if he wants to revive someone bitten by a black cobra, he should visualize in his heart an eight-petaled lotus, and above it, on each of the eight petals, distinctly visualize the third vowel ( i ), white in color. He should visualize himself in the form of the nāga Śeṣa, white in color and oozing ambrosia from the letter i [in his heart]. He should mentally send forth ambrosia from the two eyes of this nāga and visualize it falling into the body of the patient. By this meditative method he could neutralize the amount of poison that would fill the entire triple universe. {7.4.126}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2433}} “Now, if he wants to arrest the moon and the sun, he should make a moon and a sun from rice flour and submerge them in vajra water. He should recite the following mantra:
“ Oṁ , moon and sun! Do not move, do not move! Stop stop! Svāhā to Hevajra! {{note:{index:802,id:UT22084-079-008-2435}}} {7.4.127}
“He should recite this mantra sixty million times and then commence the actual rite. The moon and the sun will stop in their tracks regardless of whether it is night or day. {7.4.128}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2437}} “If he wants to destroy an enemy army, he should procure a piece of chalk. Having ground the chalk, he should prepare a pill by adding the five ambrosias together with axe filings. {{note:{index:803,id:UT22084-079-008-2438}}} {7.4.129}
“The mantra to repeat is:
“ Oṁ , vajra knife! Svāhā to Hevajra! {{note:{index:804,id:UT22084-079-008-2441}}} {7.4.130}
“In order to ensure a successful outcome, he should recite this mantra ten million times. He will then succeed. {{page:{number:141,folio:F.143.b}}} Having completed the recitations, if he ties the aforementioned pill onto the neck of a pitcher and then breaks the neck, all the enemies will be decapitated. {7.4.131}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2443}} “Should he wish to cause [hostile] gods to burst, he should ritually prepare a tilaka compound. He should procure the ‘flower’ of a possessor of a vajra {{note:{index:805,id:UT22084-079-008-2444}}} produced through constricting the vajra, {{note:{index:806,id:UT22084-079-008-2445}}} mix {{note:{index:807,id:UT22084-079-008-2446}}} it with axe filings, and grind this together with urine during a solar eclipse. Having ground them together, he should mold the paste into the shape of an axe and, stepping on it with his foot, recite the mantra:
“ Oṁ , vajra axe! Make them burst, do! Svāhā! {{note:{index:808,id:UT22084-079-008-2448}}} {7.4.132}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2449}} “In order to ensure success, he should recite this mantra ten million times. Afterward, he should respectfully give the target {{note:{index:809,id:UT22084-079-008-2450}}} a tilaka on the forehead. Whomever he does this to, will burst. {7.4.133}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2451}} “Now I will teach a rite for producing rain.
“He should make an effigy of Ananta according to the oṁ āḥ phuḥ ritual procedure, {{note:{index:810,id:UT22084-079-008-2453}}} bathe it in the five ambrosias, and offer to it black flowers. Having smeared it with mugwort juice and inuncted its head with the rut fluid from the temples of an elephant, he should place it inside a double-chambered earthenware vessel, fill the vessel with milk from a black cow, and twine around it a cord spun by a black virgin. He should then dig a pond in an area toward the northwest and place Ananta next to it, by drawing a maṇḍala on its bank as prescribed and placing Ananta in its center. He should draw Hevajra standing astride Ananta, visualizing the former as having eight faces, four feet, sixteen arms, and, in all, twenty-four eyes. Later, the officiating master, in a proud and cruel frame of mind, {{note:{index:811,id:UT22084-079-008-2454}}} should recite the following mantra in a secluded place: {7.4.134}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2455}} “ Oṁ , rumble rumble! Ghaḍa ghaḍa ! Destroy them, destroy! Strike, strike! O lord of nāgas who causes Ananta to tremble! He-he ru-ru ka! Summon the nāgas who dwell in the seven subterranean paradises and make them send rain! Threaten them and make them send thunder! Phuḥ phuḥ phuḥ puḥ phuḥ phuḥ phuḥ phuḥ! {{note:{index:812,id:UT22084-079-008-2456}}} Hūṁ hūṁ hūṁ! Phaṭ phaṭ phaṭ! Svāhā! {{note:{index:813,id:UT22084-079-008-2457}}} {7.4.135}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2458}} “If they do not send rain, he should recite the same mantra backward. They will then comply. If they still do not send rain, their heads will burst like a basil blossom. {7.4.136}
“If he wants to burst a cloud, {{page:{number:142,folio:F.144.a}}} he should write on a rag from a charnel ground the following mantra:
“ Oṁ , threaten threaten! To the one fond of cemeteries, phaṭ svāhā !” {{note:{index:814,id:UT22084-079-008-2461}}} {7.4.137}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2462}} This concludes the sovereign chapter called “The Benefits Derived from All the Rites and Their Meditations,” {{note:{index:815,id:UT22084-079-008-2463}}} the seventh in the great tantra, the glorious “ Emergence from Sampuṭa .”
Chapter 8
Part 1
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2464}} Vajragarbha said:
“I want to hear, O Blessed One, About the attributes signified by other things. I do not know the four principles, So please explain them, O Blessed One.” {8.1.1}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2466}} The Blessed One said:
“Listen, Vajragarbha, how it really is regarding The attributes of delivery from saṃsāra: The vajra scepter signifies the first principle, And the bell, the second. {8.1.2}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2468}} “The third is the rosary, and the fourth is The attribute of knowledge. The waves of these four principles Carry beings to the desired other shore. {8.1.3}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2469}} “On the central prong of the vajra scepter is Lord Vairocana; On the eastern, Akṣobhya himself. Ratnasambhava is on the southern prong, Whereas Amitābha should be visualized on the western. {8.1.4}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2470}} “On the northern prong there is Amoghasiddhi— These are the main deities on the five prongs. On the lotus below one should install, in their allotted places, The eight bodhisattvas representing the eight ancillary aspects of awakening: {8.1.5}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2471}} “Padmapāṇi (Avalokiteśvara), Maitreya, Gaganagañja (Ākāśagarbha), Samantabhadra, The lord of yakṣas (Vajrapāṇi), Mañjuśrī, Sarvanivaraṇaviṣkambhin, and Kṣitigarbha. {8.1.6}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2472}} “One should distribute these eight principal deities In their respective places. The wisdom deity is nestled In the center, {{note:{index:816,id:UT22084-079-008-2473}}} the place of origin of the thirteen deities. {{note:{index:817,id:UT22084-079-008-2474}}} {8.1.7}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2475}} “On the other lotus petals one should add The following eight goddesses in their respective places: The four goddesses beginning with Vajrāṅkuśī {{note:{index:818,id:UT22084-079-008-2476}}} in the cardinal directions, And the other cavorting ladies in the intermediate directions. {8.1.8}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2477}} “On the five prongs of the vajra scepter there are five ḍākinīs: On the central one, there is the eponymous jñānasattva —Jñānaḍākinī; On the eastern, there is Vajraḍākinī; On the northern, there is the one called Ghorī; {8.1.9}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2478}} “On the western one, there is Vetālī; And Caṇḍālī is the goddess on the southern prong. The wise practitioner should know These deities to be the principles of the vajra. {8.1.10}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2479}} “Since the principles of the vajra are present As the nature of the vajra within one’s own mind, The practitioners, by employing the vajra scepters, Can bring on the realization of the vajra mind. {8.1.11}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2480}} “He should firmly ascertain {{note:{index:819,id:UT22084-079-008-2481}}} that vajra is purity; {{page:{number:143,folio:F.144.b}}} This vajra [mind] is construed as identical with phenomena. Vajra is all of these principles, And it extends also to ritual action. {8.1.12}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2482}} “The vajra scepter, by emitting light, Delivers beings from saṃsāra. He who knows the method can use it In the acts of summoning and paralyzing. {8.1.13}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2483}} “Just as the afflictions are likened to darkness, So does gnosis accord with a lamp. Should he destroy the afflictions with the vajra of gnosis, He will attain the dimension of light. {8.1.14}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2484}} “Everything that is accomplished with the vajra Is taught to be the nature of vajra. Vajra is the essence of phenomena; Vajra is being concerned with liberation. {8.1.15}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2485}} “By mounting the vajra onto the lotus {{note:{index:820,id:UT22084-079-008-2486}}} He will realize the nature of reality in its entirety. By submerging the vajra in the lotus, {{note:{index:821,id:UT22084-079-008-2487}}} The wise practitioner will succeed. {8.1.16}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2488}} “Listen, O King Vajradhara, {{note:{index:822,id:UT22084-079-008-2489}}} about The characteristics of the vajra bell. {{note:{index:823,id:UT22084-079-008-2490}}} All the deities listen to the bells, Whose very nature is to sound wisdom. {{note:{index:824,id:UT22084-079-008-2491}}} {8.1.17}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2492}} “The bell should be clearly understood as consisting of three parts. It is adorned with a girding band; It is as tranquil as the blossoms of blue or white lotuses, And arrayed with jewels and lotus flowers. {{note:{index:825,id:UT22084-079-008-2493}}} {8.1.18}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2494}} “[On the nine-pronged vajra handle] there are eight deities In the cardinal and intermediate directions, with the Buddha {{note:{index:826,id:UT22084-079-008-2495}}} as the ninth in the center. As there are nine deities, and so forth, {{note:{index:827,id:UT22084-079-008-2496}}} He should consecrate the prongs with these nine. {8.1.19}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2497}} “Eight of the prongs emerge from the mouth of a sea monster And are each situated on light rays and a moon. This is the vajra scepter of wisdom that liberates the world; {{note:{index:828,id:UT22084-079-008-2498}}} It is called ‘The Nine Prongs.’ {8.1.20}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2499}} “Established as the seat of awakening, It is present throughout the reaches of space, With all the infinite world spheres Throughout the ten directions being fields of knowledge. {8.1.21}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2500}} “[On the petals of the lotus at the top of the bell], {{note:{index:829,id:UT22084-079-008-2501}}} In the eight directions, eight goddesses are famed to reside. They arise from their respective seed syllables And are each placed in one of the eight sectors. {8.1.22}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2502}} “On the eastern petal there is Tāriṇī; On the northern, there is Pāṇḍarā. On the western, there is Māmakī, And on the southern, there is Buddhalocanā. {8.1.23}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2503}} “The intermediate directions are occupied by Sauvarṇā, Madhurā, Kānti, and Vajramālā—the four of them. Inside they are like space, And outwardly they are receptacles of beauty and radiance. {8.1.24}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2504}} “They each arise from a lotus in full bloom. {{page:{number:144,folio:F.145.a}}} [Inside the bell,] resembling a vase of wisdom ambrosia, Is the place of formless existence. In the center of this place of wisdom ambrosia is the mind. {{note:{index:830,id:UT22084-079-008-2505}}} {8.1.25}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2506}} “The bell is the goddess Prajñāpāramitā, Beautiful in form and endowed with qualities. As for the vajra [prongs] above the lotus, He should visualize there the set of deities as before. {8.1.26}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2507}} “The middle part {{note:{index:831,id:UT22084-079-008-2508}}} is called ‘the staff of gnosis’— There takes place all emanating and absorbing. He should cause the bell clapper to swing in the eight directions, Employing the visualization of the vowels and consonants. {8.1.27}
