{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2509}} “Through this method involving the vowels and the consonants He can cut through all of saṃsāric existence. The vajra scepter and bell are means, And as means, they are in the middle. {{note:{index:832,id:UT22084-079-008-2510}}} {8.1.28}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2511}} “Stretching out both hands, he should, in this ritual, Perform the gesture of ‘the turning of the lotus’ {{note:{index:833,id:UT22084-079-008-2512}}} five times. On his right palm he should visualize the sun, And on his left, the moon. {8.1.29}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2513}} “As the skillful means for embodied beings, He should visualize his chosen deity. The wise practitioner should raise up {{note:{index:834,id:UT22084-079-008-2514}}} the vajra scepter And then place it upon the bell. {8.1.30}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2515}} “He should chant the syllable hūṁ And delight all the buddhas by singing:
“ ‘Adorned by the raised vajra scepter, Delusional beings are liberated. As the fruition of liberation through Dharma, One holds the pleasing vajra scepter. {{note:{index:835,id:UT22084-079-008-2517}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2518}} “ ‘ Hūṁ hūṁ hūṁ! Ho ho ho !’ {8.1.31}
“When sounding the wisdom and the means (i.e., the bell and the vajra scepter) The wisdom and the means consist of his hands. {8.1.32}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2520}} “He should recite further:
“ Oṁ , the vajra sound of phenomena! Spreading and reverberating! You reach all the buddhafields. Your nature is the sound of the perfection of wisdom. You delight the heart of Vajrasattva. Hūṁ hūṁ hūṁ! Ho ho ho! Svāhā! {{note:{index:836,id:UT22084-079-008-2522}}} {8.1.33}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2523}} “And further:
“ Oṁ , please stand by the vajra pledge to bring about the realization of all the tathāgatas! I uphold you. Hiḥ hi hi hi hi! Hūṁ hūṁ hūṁ! Phaṭ! Svāhā! {{note:{index:837,id:UT22084-079-008-2525}}} {8.1.34}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2526}} “By the Dharma of wisdom and means All living beings are awakened. He should sound the bell in order to awaken to buddhahood Those beings wallowing in the swamp of unknowing. {8.1.35}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2527}} “He should truly grasp the vajra scepter, And truly sound the bell. Being a practitioner, he should work for the benefit of beings, Following the procedure of wisdom and means. {8.1.36}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2528}} “The bell of the practitioner who does not have This truth in his heart {{note:{index:838,id:UT22084-079-008-2529}}} sounds like an elephant bell. The accomplishment of someone who does not Possess the truth of yoga appears to be far off.” {8.1.37} {{page:{number:145,folio:F.145.b}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2530}} This concludes the first part of the eighth chapter on the principles of the bell.
Part 2
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2531}} “Listen, Vajragarbha, as is proper, About the characteristics of a rosary, By the correct application of which, One will succeed without doubt. {8.2.1}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2532}} “Crystal, pearl, Bone, {{note:{index:839,id:UT22084-079-008-2533}}} or another white material Are the characteristics of a rosary Particularly suited for rites of appeasement. {8.2.2}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2534}} “Gold, silver, or copper, And, in particular, lotus seeds, Are regarded by a wise practitioner As the rosary materials for rites of enriching. {8.2.3}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2535}} “Saffron, sandalwood, and similar substances, Or any especially fragrant materials, Should be used for making beads Famed to be effective in rites of enthralling. {8.2.4}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2536}} “Rudrākṣa seeds, soapberry seeds, And human bone Should be used in violent rites, As they are famed to be effective in assaulting. {8.2.5}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2537}} “The seeds of lucky bean tree can be used in all rites— Pacifying, enriching, enthralling, and assaulting. For the accomplishment of the mantra the number of beads should be fifty; In rites of enthralling, it should be half of that. {8.2.6}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2538}} “For rites of pacifying, there should be one hundred beads; In rites of enriching, one hundred and eight. In rites of assaulting, there should be sixty— These are the numbers used in specific rites. {8.2.7}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2539}} “One should prepare a rosary and other implements According to the type of ritual being performed. With eight deities in the cardinal and intermediary directions, And the Buddha being the ninth in the center, {8.2.8}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2540}} “One should install the nine deities In the nine-threaded cord of the nine deities, and so forth. All of the beads are arhats— They should be threaded above the stūpa-bead. {8.2.9}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2541}} “The stūpa-bead is regarded as the beholder of phenomena, And the beads above it, the sphere of phenomena. {{note:{index:840,id:UT22084-079-008-2542}}} One should visualize on the palm of one’s [right] hand a sun disk With the first vowel, a , and so forth. {8.2.10}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2543}} “If one is a practitioner, he should visualize in the center of the [left] hand The syllable of ambrosia, a, With a white central part, Radiating multiple rays of light. {{note:{index:841,id:UT22084-079-008-2544}}} {8.2.11}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2545}} “He should visualize the fingers of the right hand as the prongs of a vajra scepter, And the fingers of the left as lotus petals. He should join the lotus with the vajra to form a hemisphere, And place the rosary in the center. {8.2.12}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2546}} “He should visualize this as completely real, {{note:{index:842,id:UT22084-079-008-2547}}} And consecrate the rosary in this way. Afterward, the mantra practitioner should recite the mantras, According to the specifics of how to use his fingers, and so forth. {8.2.13} {{page:{number:146,folio:F.146.a}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2548}} “The [left] hand then also becomes vajra, Assuming the nature of nonduality of the vajra. {{note:{index:843,id:UT22084-079-008-2549}}} In rites of pacifying he should use the index finger; In those of enriching, he employs the principle of the middle finger. {8.2.14}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2550}} “The ring finger is said to be used in rites of enthralling, And the little finger in rites of assaulting. The thumb is used to form a vajra hook With the power to summon the deities. {8.2.15}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2551}} “By reciting and meditating with focus, He will succeed without a doubt. When the practitioner does not possess suchness, His mantra recitation and meditation will be, likewise, without suchness. {8.2.16}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2552}} “He will lack the principles of the vajra scepter and bell, And likewise will not give rise to the principle of gesture. However, once the practitioner attains suchness, {{note:{index:844,id:UT22084-079-008-2553}}} He will be able to manifest all principles. {8.2.17}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2554}} “Since suchness is the cause of all syllables, It is also the essence of mantras with exquisite forms. Thus by counting the mantras that are meant to be counted, He will realize the essence of the yoginīs. {{note:{index:845,id:UT22084-079-008-2555}}} {8.2.18}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2556}} “The mantra to recite is:
“ Oṁ , stage by stage, I will attain the great knowledge of all the buddhas. Hūṁ hūṁ hūṁ! Ho ho ho! Aḥ! Svāhā! {{note:{index:846,id:UT22084-079-008-2558}}} {8.2.19}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2559}} “By reciting these mantras that purify through the principle of the rosary, He will accomplish whatever he desires. The rites rooted in suchness will be successful. But if suchness is not fully manifested, success will be far off. {8.2.20}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2560}} “Listen well, O [Vajragarbha], one of great knowledge, As this is particularly about the essential reality of wisdom. Fully collected, he should offer a gaṇacakra feast, Assuming, as the mental categories go, the mind of sameness. {{note:{index:847,id:UT22084-079-008-2561}}} {8.2.21}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2562}} “He should visualize, transformed from the seed syllable of gnosis Placed in the center of a moon disk, [Vairocana], white in color And sitting on a lotus throne. {8.2.22}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2563}} “He has two arms and sits in the sattvaparyaṅka posture; He is adorned with all kinds of jewelry. His consort , the great seal, Is held to his heart with his two hands. {8.2.23}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2564}} “Brilliantly white and very beautiful, She resembles the noble lord Vairocana. With clouds composed of buddhas {{note:{index:848,id:UT22084-079-008-2565}}} flashing forth, He is surrounded on all sides by multicolored light. {8.2.24}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2566}} “Simultaneously, he should recite the mantra Following the right procedure, which involves Turning the rosary with either the left or the right hand. {{note:{index:849,id:UT22084-079-008-2567}}} This will please the ḍākinīs. {8.2.25}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2568}} “The seeds of vowels and consonants Are threaded on the thread whose principle is the syllable hūṁ. {{page:{number:147,folio:F.146.b}}} Should the practitioner visualize this seed syllable [of Vairocana], He will swiftly attain buddhahood.” {8.2.26}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2569}} This concludes the second part of the eighth chapter on mantra recitation and visualization.
Part 3
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2570}} “Listen Vajragarbha, as is proper, to the explanation Of the practice of consciousness transference. I will teach you about the beautiful destiny Arrived at through the auspicious path of practitioners. {8.3.1}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2571}} [Vajragarbha said:]
“I want to hear it, O master of gnosis! What are the nine gates? What are the good qualities and faults, According to the classification of the gates of consciousness?” {8.3.2}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2573}} [The Blessed One said:]
“Listen about the proper method, Which is to be relied upon at the time of passing away. When the path {{note:{index:850,id:UT22084-079-008-2575}}} is right, one will reach a pleasant destiny; The wrong path will lead to unfavorable forms of existence. {{note:{index:851,id:UT22084-079-008-2576}}} {8.3.3}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2577}} “The nine gates are specified as The ‘drop’ between the eyebrows, the navel, The fontanelle above, {{note:{index:852,id:UT22084-079-008-2578}}} the eyes, the nostrils and so forth, {{note:{index:853,id:UT22084-079-008-2579}}} the ears, And the gates for passing water and for evacuation. {{note:{index:854,id:UT22084-079-008-2580}}} {8.3.4}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2581}} “The gate at the navel leads to the gods’ realm of desire. By leaving through the ‘drop,’ one will enter the realm of form. The ‘above’ gate leads to still higher destinies. These three gates have been proclaimed as leading to higher destinies. {8.3.5}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2582}} “The realm of yakṣas is entered through the nostrils; That of the divine siddhas, through the ears. The consciousness that escapes through the eyes Will proceed to the realm of humans. {8.3.6}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2583}} “The gate of existence, the mouth, leads to the realm of hungry ghosts, While the urinary passage leads to the animal realm. When the gate is the anus, the destiny is hell with its eight divisions. So are described, O sons of noble family, the passages into different existences. {{note:{index:855,id:UT22084-079-008-2584}}} {8.3.7}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2585}} “Since the emergence of the different saṃsāric destinations Happens according to the specificities of the gates, The practitioners must focus [at the time of death] On the type of gate they are going to pass through. {8.3.8}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2586}} “When the time of death arrives, A sign of death will be perceived. It is best to practice transference Before the separation of body and mind is caused by old age, and so forth. {{note:{index:856,id:UT22084-079-008-2587}}} {8.3.9}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2588}} “To start, one should block all the gates By performing the breath retention called kumbhaka. The visualization involves five syllables placed inside the subtle channels, [Each of the syllables blocking one of] the five gate-orifices. {{note:{index:857,id:UT22084-079-008-2589}}} {8.3.10}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2590}} “The seed syllable at the gate below them Should be white as the element water. {{note:{index:858,id:UT22084-079-008-2591}}} The seed syllable of fire at the urethral and anal gates Should be visualized as blazing like fire. {{note:{index:859,id:UT22084-079-008-2592}}} {8.3.11}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2593}} “One should do this visualization with complete collectedness While performing the same breathing as mentioned before. {{note:{index:860,id:UT22084-079-008-2594}}} {{page:{number:148,folio:F.147.a}}} One’s body is visualized as being the color of the element wind, And the consciousness as being the maṇḍala of wind. {{note:{index:861,id:UT22084-079-008-2595}}} {8.3.12}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2596}} “The roots of the seed syllable of wind ( yūṁ ) Are rooted in the edges of the wind below. {{note:{index:862,id:UT22084-079-008-2597}}} One should pull [the consciousness] with the visualized syllables, Each joined with the ‘sound’ ( u ) and the anunāsika. {{note:{index:863,id:UT22084-079-008-2598}}} {8.3.13}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2599}} “One should attach the hook of Ghorā ( kṣuṁ ), And so forth, to the syllable of Vajrī ( suṁ ). One should imagine Ghorā pulling [the consciousness] Through the twenty-four places in the ten directions. {{note:{index:864,id:UT22084-079-008-2600}}} {8.3.14}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2601}} “It should be drawn upward from its resting place, one step at a time, Through the nine junctures, until it reaches the top point (i.e., the fontanelle). {{note:{index:865,id:UT22084-079-008-2602}}} With the seed syllable at the tuft of ūrṇā, {{note:{index:866,id:UT22084-079-008-2603}}} One should purify the syllable(s) of the body. {{note:{index:867,id:UT22084-079-008-2604}}} {8.3.15}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2605}} “One should pronounce, with a terrible sound ( i ), The final syllable of the eight ( ha ). It should be joined with the half-syllable Of the first ferocious letter of the first ferocious group ( k ). {{note:{index:868,id:UT22084-079-008-2606}}} {8.3.16}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2607}} “One should propel [the consciousness with] The wind-syllable below by repeating the sound ( hik ). {{note:{index:869,id:UT22084-079-008-2608}}} Joined with the syllable of wind ( yuṁ ) As the maṇḍala of wind, {8.3.17}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2609}} “The consciousness should be propelled upward Through the twenty-four places, higher and higher. {{note:{index:870,id:UT22084-079-008-2610}}} If the practitioner should start greying, He should consume the ‘upper letter.’ {{note:{index:871,id:UT22084-079-008-2611}}} {8.3.18}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2612}} “When the consciousness reaches the highest Of the nine junctions, it suddenly escapes upward. {{note:{index:872,id:UT22084-079-008-2613}}} Even if one has killed a god {{note:{index:873,id:UT22084-079-008-2614}}} or a brahmin, Or committed one of the five sins of instant retribution, {8.3.19}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2615}} “Engaged in stealing, or indulged in the pleasures of the senses, One will be liberated by this method. Untainted by past sins, one will be far removed From the shortcomings of cyclic existence. {8.3.20}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2616}} “Just as the beauty of a lotus, Growing out of mud, is completely immaculate, So will the wisdom-body be, through one’s own will, When propelled from bodies of mud and the like. {8.3.21}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2617}} “The transference can be performed only when the time has arrived; Otherwise it is equal to the slaying of a god. Therefore the wise practitioner should commence This practice only when the body has manifested signs of death. {8.3.22}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2618}} “Listen, Vajra, {{note:{index:874,id:UT22084-079-008-2619}}} about this practice particularly important to accomplish, Explained in conformity with the truth. One should visualize, with the mind in the state of equanimity And with all the characteristics as previously described, {8.3.23}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2620}} “In one’s heart, in the center of the maṇḍala, {{note:{index:875,id:UT22084-079-008-2621}}} The syllable of the five buddhas. {{note:{index:876,id:UT22084-079-008-2622}}} Bright as the sun, it emits light rays Whose nature is reflected by the mind. {{note:{index:877,id:UT22084-079-008-2623}}} {8.3.24} {{page:{number:149,folio:F.147.b}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2624}} “Following the previous instructions on emptiness And the accompanying characteristics, {{note:{index:878,id:UT22084-079-008-2625}}} One should break up all forms, and so forth, With the mind abiding as the syllable hūṁ . {8.3.25}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2626}} “From this seed syllable one generates The form of the deity in the center of a moon disk, Sitting on a lotus seat—one should thus Visualize oneself as Jñānaḍākinī. {8.3.26}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2627}} “She has three faces and six arms. Each face has three eyes and each head is adorned with a diadem. She displays the sentiments of mirth, anger, and erotic love, And is adorned with all types of jewelry. {8.3.27}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2628}} “Her color is white like jasmine flowers or the moon, And she is dressed in very beautiful clothes. She sits in the sattvaparyaṅka posture Surrounded by clouds of buddhas flashing rays of light. {8.3.28}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2629}} “In her first [right] hand she holds an arrow, And in the second, a goad. In her third hand, she brandishes a vajra scepter. With her first left hand she makes a threatening gesture and holds a noose. {8.3.29}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2630}} “In the second, she holds a wish-fulfilling creeper; With the third, she raises a bow nocked with an arrow. Around her there are multiple halos of light. One should visualize all this with the breath unmoving. {{note:{index:879,id:UT22084-079-008-2631}}} {8.3.30}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2632}} “One should then place the letters on her body, Forming with them the eight seed syllables, Just as such syllables are formed— Through combining the vowels and the consonants. {8.3.31}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2633}} “All of them are white And suffused with moonlight. In her heart, on a lotus in the center of a plantain flower, One should place the universe. {8.3.32}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2634}} “In its center one should visualize The consciousness combined with gnosis. {{note:{index:880,id:UT22084-079-008-2635}}} Unwavering and untroubled, {{note:{index:881,id:UT22084-079-008-2636}}} One should meditate merging with the essence. {{note:{index:882,id:UT22084-079-008-2637}}} {8.3.33}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2638}} “Then the wise practitioner should observe The external practices related to Reading the thoughts of others in different places, By employing the mind as the maṇḍala of wind. {{note:{index:883,id:UT22084-079-008-2639}}} {8.3.34}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2640}} “In the center of the maṇḍala of wind is the maṇḍala of fire. In the center of the maṇḍala of fire is a sun disk. It is decked with the vowels and the consonants, which transform into A sun and a moon respectively, with a red seed syllable between them. {{note:{index:884,id:UT22084-079-008-2641}}} {8.3.35}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2642}} “It is particularly recommended that the practitioner Combines the recitation of the mantra with exhaling and inhaling. With the outgoing breath he should strike the target In the center of his body with the syllable of gnosis ( hūṁ ). {{note:{index:885,id:UT22084-079-008-2643}}} {8.3.36}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2644}} “When inhaling, the one reciting the mantra In combination with exhaling and inhaling Should strike, as if with a flower, The gnosis at his heart. {8.3.37} {{page:{number:150,folio:F.148.a}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2645}} “By reciting in combination with exhalation and inhalation, The practitioner externalizes his nature. {{note:{index:886,id:UT22084-079-008-2646}}} He should observe the characteristics of exhalation, And observe the characteristics of inhalation. {8.3.38}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2647}} “This practice of exhaling and inhaling Involves the cultivation of the state of equality. Through merging thus with the essence while fully collected, He will reach accomplishment, there is no doubt. {8.3.39}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2648}} “Then the external bodies of others will become The practitioner’s own magical manifestation. {{note:{index:887,id:UT22084-079-008-2649}}} Reading the thoughts of others, The wise one will be able to reveal them. {8.3.40}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2650}} “If, with his mind fully immersed In the visualization and recitation as specified, He thinks of positive migrations, This will be achieved without doubt. {8.3.41}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2651}} “Therefore, having become the nature of gnosis, {{note:{index:888,id:UT22084-079-008-2652}}} the wise practitioner should perform the rites with his mind blazing brightly like a lamp. {{note:{index:889,id:UT22084-079-008-2653}}} {8.3.42}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2654}} “The suchness as experienced by hearers, and so forth, Has been skillfully presented and explained. {{note:{index:890,id:UT22084-079-008-2655}}} Having first, as a listener, stabilized the crystal-like mind Until it blazes forth like a lamp, {8.3.43}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2656}} “He should observe {{note:{index:891,id:UT22084-079-008-2657}}} his every conceptual elaboration Until conceptuality becomes nonconceptual. {{note:{index:892,id:UT22084-079-008-2658}}} Relying {{note:{index:893,id:UT22084-079-008-2659}}} thus on the method of the innate nature, He should completely discard all concepts.” {{note:{index:894,id:UT22084-079-008-2660}}} {8.3.44}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2661}} [The goddess asked], {{note:{index:895,id:UT22084-079-008-2662}}} “Venerable One! How is the [mundane] {{note:{index:896,id:UT22084-079-008-2663}}} consciousness differentiated?” {{note:{index:897,id:UT22084-079-008-2664}}} {8.3.45}
The Blessed One said:
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2666}} “Consciousness is said to be fivefold: {8.3.46}
“(1) The secret {{note:{index:898,id:UT22084-079-008-2668}}} mirror-consciousness of the gods, (2) The anger-consciousness of the demigods, (3) The wretched {{note:{index:899,id:UT22084-079-008-2669}}} consciousness of the hungry spirits, (4) The ‘screaming in fear’ consciousness of hell beings, {8.3.47}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2670}} “And (5) the deluded consciousness of animals. Inanimate objects and the like do not possess consciousness. {{note:{index:900,id:UT22084-079-008-2671}}} So is the consciousness taught following this fivefold division. {8.3.48}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2672}} “The immature consciousness of dumb beings Who are obscured by dullness May be elevated in its essence Thanks to the excellence of yoga treatises. {{note:{index:901,id:UT22084-079-008-2673}}} {8.3.49}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2674}} “It is once in a thousand million lifetimes That, because of me, one becomes inspired by gnosis. {{page:{number:151,folio:F.148.b}}} Therefore the wise one should generate faith with ardor And diligently study yoga treatises. {{note:{index:902,id:UT22084-079-008-2675}}} {8.3.50}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2676}} “The words, and so forth, of the outer treatises Are like the makeup of a dancer. He should therefore strive to attain fulfilment and liberation Through pursuing the teachings of yoga tantra. {8.3.51}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2677}} “Yoga tantra, more essential than the essence itself, Has been taught to you, O fair-faced one.” {8.3.52}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2678}} This concludes the third part of the eighth chapter, called “The Rejection of the Knowledge of Non-Buddhists.”

“ Oṁ khaṁ nī rī hūṁ khaḥ! {{note:{index:974,id:UT22084-079-008-2885}}} {8.4.43}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2886}} “The mantra of perfume, food items, and other offerings is:
“ Oṁ dhvaṁ dhvaṁ ! {8.4.44}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2888}} “The mantra of the Great Seal is:
“ Oṁ ha ho hrīḥ svāhā ! {8.4.45}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2890}} “The mantra of summoning is:
“ Oṁ , master of the samaya! Act, act! Hūṁ jaḥ, svāhā! {{note:{index:975,id:UT22084-079-008-2892}}} {8.4.46}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2893}} “The mantra to be placed on the six limbs is:
“ Ha hi hu {{note:{index:976,id:UT22084-079-008-2895}}} he ho haṁ !” {8.4.47}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2896}} This concludes the eighth sovereign chapter in the glorious “ Emergence from Sampuṭa ” on the advantages of all the rituals. {{page:{number:155,folio:F.150.b}}}
Chapter 9
Part 1
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2897}} Now the great bodhisattvas, headed by Vajragarbha, along with all the tathāgatas, made offerings and prostrated themselves to the Blessed One, then said: {9.1.1}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2898}} “Please give us, O Blessed One, O divine being, A detailed exposition of the state of nirvāṇa. In which place does one abide, Playing within the animate and inanimate universes?” {9.1.2}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2899}} The Blessed One said:
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2900}} “Listen! I will explain the nature of The mind fixating on concepts as it really is. This nature, which has already been taught earlier, Is always present in everybody. {{note:{index:977,id:UT22084-079-008-2901}}} {9.1.3}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2902}} “The body is said to be the maṇḍala, With four doors, as has been described. In the navel center there is a great lotus, Which is famed to be the seat of omniscient gnosis. {9.1.4}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2903}} “In that place dwells the valiant one. Without constituent parts he is indivisible. {{note:{index:978,id:UT22084-079-008-2904}}} He plays within embodied beings, being himself Beyond any embodiment and completely pure. {{note:{index:979,id:UT22084-079-008-2905}}} {9.1.5}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2906}} “Possessed of the great magical power of all the buddhas, He can magically transform himself— Sometimes into the great bodhicitta, Sometimes {{note:{index:980,id:UT22084-079-008-2907}}} into the conduct that accompanies it. {9.1.6}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2908}} “Sometimes he dwells among the gods of the Tuṣita realm. At some point he makes the supreme {{note:{index:981,id:UT22084-079-008-2909}}} descent to earth. At some point he takes a pure birth, And at some point he definitively renounces worldly life. {9.1.7}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2910}} “At some point he makes a great peregrination for the sake of awakening, {{note:{index:982,id:UT22084-079-008-2911}}} And at some point he defeats Māra. At some point he attains complete and perfect awakening, And at some point he turns the wheel of Dharma. {9.1.8}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2912}} “At some point he defeats in debate the followers of other creeds, Using in his arguments truths acceptable to both parties. At some point he becomes the master of all attainments, And at some point he conquers the triple universe. {{note:{index:983,id:UT22084-079-008-2913}}} {9.1.9}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2914}} “At some point he attains the unexcelled powers Of accomplishment that last throughout all the ages. {{note:{index:984,id:UT22084-079-008-2915}}} Such infinite and supreme acts as these and others Are performed by those partaking of the nature of all buddhas, {{note:{index:985,id:UT22084-079-008-2916}}} {9.1.10}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2917}} “Since {{note:{index:986,id:UT22084-079-008-2918}}} they are free from both existence and nonexistence. Thus, one should abandon all delusion. {{page:{number:156,folio:F.151.a}}} ‘The set of vowels is the bee,’ {{note:{index:987,id:UT22084-079-008-2919}}} they say; The bee is Vajrabhairava. {{note:{index:988,id:UT22084-079-008-2920}}} {9.1.11}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2921}} “The set of vowels extends to the end of space, Since by its nature it is the sphere of phenomena. {{note:{index:989,id:UT22084-079-008-2922}}} It is the secret container of animate and inanimate elements Of every being that has evolved a body. {{note:{index:990,id:UT22084-079-008-2923}}} {9.1.12}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2924}} “It is the ‘ambrosia’ of the aggregates, the sense-fields, and the elements That constitutes all their vital power. {{note:{index:991,id:UT22084-079-008-2925}}} Therefore, one should draw all {{note:{index:992,id:UT22084-079-008-2926}}} the ambrosia inward And dissolve it in the middle of the root. {{note:{index:993,id:UT22084-079-008-2927}}} {9.1.13}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2928}} “With the vajra sound of Bhairava, Taking the form of the fluid of the completion yoga, {{note:{index:994,id:UT22084-079-008-2929}}} One should join the seven winds and fires {{note:{index:995,id:UT22084-079-008-2930}}} With the syllable of Vajrī. {{note:{index:996,id:UT22084-079-008-2931}}} {9.1.14}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2932}} “Surmounted with the anunāsika, this seed syllable Is known as ‘the torrent of rain.’ {{note:{index:997,id:UT22084-079-008-2933}}} One should hold at the center of the [lotus at the navel] The first and original vowel ( a ). {{note:{index:998,id:UT22084-079-008-2934}}} {9.1.15}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2935}} “The consonant syllabary ( kāli ) is the flower king; {{note:{index:999,id:UT22084-079-008-2936}}} The flower is the body of vajra holders. {{note:{index:1000,id:UT22084-079-008-2937}}} It is the origin of cyclic existence for all And the mother all over the earth. {{note:{index:1001,id:UT22084-079-008-2938}}} {9.1.16}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2939}} “In that ocean with the water of gnosis There are sea monsters and fishes of insight. Right in the middle of the swamp of nonduality Sprouts the sprout of skillful means. {{note:{index:1002,id:UT22084-079-008-2940}}} {9.1.17}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2941}} “This receptacle of honey and ambrosia {{note:{index:1003,id:UT22084-079-008-2942}}} Resembles an open bandhūka flower. The mixing of consonants with the ambrosia Is like the mixing of ‘flower’ and ‘water.’ {{note:{index:1004,id:UT22084-079-008-2943}}} {9.1.18}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2944}} “Since the body is born from both {{note:{index:1005,id:UT22084-079-008-2945}}} the blood and the semen, The method of ‘ambrosia-water’ is supreme. {{note:{index:1006,id:UT22084-079-008-2946}}} The ‘ambrosia-water’ {{note:{index:1007,id:UT22084-079-008-2947}}} is said initially To have a fivefold nature. {{note:{index:1008,id:UT22084-079-008-2948}}} {9.1.19}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2949}} “Fire imparts its heat through contact, {{note:{index:1009,id:UT22084-079-008-2950}}} Wind is perceived as smoke, {{note:{index:1010,id:UT22084-079-008-2951}}} Water has the nature of fluidity, And because of the element earth, shapes can be discerned. {{note:{index:1011,id:UT22084-079-008-2952}}} {9.1.20}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2953}} “Wisdom consecrated by the vajra Becomes fivefold. {{note:{index:1012,id:UT22084-079-008-2954}}} To elaborate, water can assume every shape; Fire, for its part, brings destruction; {{note:{index:1013,id:UT22084-079-008-2955}}} {9.1.21}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2956}} “Wind is the continual breathing; And earth, for its part, is the nature of the witness. {{note:{index:1014,id:UT22084-079-008-2957}}} All the yoginīs are pleased With the song in the form of the syllable hūṁ. {{note:{index:1015,id:UT22084-079-008-2958}}} {9.1.22}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2959}} “By chanting the following song, one will become a son of the victorious ones.
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2960}} “ ‘O vajra, lord {{note:{index:1016,id:UT22084-079-008-2961}}} of bliss, Who perceives with the five eyes! You are the nature of letters Who plays in emptiness. {{note:{index:1017,id:UT22084-079-008-2962}}} {9.1.23}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2963}} “ ‘Being devoid of existence and nonexistence, You are known as the essence. May you destroy all letters {{page:{number:157,folio:F.151.b}}} And all thoughts. {9.1.24}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2964}} “ ‘The practitioner of the coupling embrace, Performed for the purpose of producing the fluids, Attains the nondual Dharma, Which, quintessentially, is liberation. {9.1.25}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2965}} “ ‘For the sake of those deluded by the pleasures of saṃsāra You forestall your own liberation. In the nature of emptiness {{note:{index:1018,id:UT22084-079-008-2966}}} You play with the mantra of the yoginīs. {9.1.26}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2967}} “ ‘You show that the five yoginīs Are in reality the five buddhas. With magical displays of manifold forms You bring beings to spiritual maturity. {9.1.27}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2968}} “ ‘The purpose of extending the vajra Is to remove delusion about phenomena. May you bow to this teaching, good in its essence, For the sake of liberating the yoginīs.’ {{note:{index:1019,id:UT22084-079-008-2969}}} {9.1.28}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2970}} “By chanting this song, O sons of noble family, one will become a son of all the victorious ones—so said every blessed tathāgata.” {{note:{index:1020,id:UT22084-079-008-2971}}} {9.1.29}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2972}} This concludes the first part of the ninth chapter, “The Genesis of Every Tathāgata.”
Part 2
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2973}} “Listen, Vajragarbha, O mighty king, About how to do the oblation ritual according to procedure. One should delineate a circle of red sandalwood {{note:{index:1021,id:UT22084-079-008-2974}}} paste Measuring one cubit in diameter, {9.2.1}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2975}} “And then draw a white {{note:{index:1022,id:UT22084-079-008-2976}}} triangle surrounding it. Along with the honors such as the welcome offering of water and flowers and the five articles—fish, meat, and so forth—one should include wine that inspires amorous passion. On the left side one should place all the ritual implements, and on the right, a dish with water. In front there should be the welcome-offering dish. Having purified all these substances with the five ambrosias, {{note:{index:1023,id:UT22084-079-008-2977}}} one should enter the absorption of Vajrasattva or, alternatively, assume the identity of Heruka. {9.2.2}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2978}} “One should summon the wisdom ambrosia {{note:{index:1024,id:UT22084-079-008-2979}}} By means of gesture and mantras, observing the ritual procedure. One should offer red flowers, Lamps, and so on, and also perfume. {{note:{index:1025,id:UT22084-079-008-2980}}} {9.2.3}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2981}} “One should mentally summon all five ambrosias To the lotus dish {{note:{index:1026,id:UT22084-079-008-2982}}} marked with the syllable oṁ, In particular through hūṁ , the principle of the tongue, {{note:{index:1027,id:UT22084-079-008-2983}}} According to the divisions of the hooks of gnosis.” {{note:{index:1028,id:UT22084-079-008-2984}}} {9.2.4}
[Vajragarbha asked:]
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2986}} “What, O Blessed One, are the so-called ‘hooks of gnosis’?” {9.2.5} {{page:{number:158,folio:F.152.a}}}
The Blessed One said:
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2988}} “Prajāpati is said to be the first one. The second in this listing is Tārā. Pravarā is thought to be the third. The fourth is Bahulojātā. The fifth is Bālā. {{note:{index:1029,id:UT22084-079-008-2989}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2990}} “These names are mantras of the five families, following the division of the five wisdoms. {{note:{index:1030,id:UT22084-079-008-2991}}} {9.2.6}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2992}} “These five great gnoses Have been taught for your benefit. One should employ them in all activities, {{note:{index:1031,id:UT22084-079-008-2993}}} Following the division into the five ‘hooks of gnosis.’ {9.2.7}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2994}} “Should one wish these activities to occur incessantly, {{note:{index:1032,id:UT22084-079-008-2995}}} One should please all the yoginīs, But without sexual addiction; One should not become attached to bliss. {9.2.8}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2996}} “In order to benefit all beings, the practitioner Should arrange offerings of every kind. That which is famed as the moon Arises out of the thirteen vowels. {{note:{index:1033,id:UT22084-079-008-2997}}} {9.2.9}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-2998}} “Then, in the center of the moon, he should gratify all the deities with syllables, by uniting the vowels and the consonants. {{note:{index:1034,id:UT22084-079-008-2999}}} {9.2.10}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3000}} “He should generate {{note:{index:1035,id:UT22084-079-008-3001}}} a blaze of light Distinguished by the arising of heat. He should visualize it in the form of a crystal {{note:{index:1036,id:UT22084-079-008-3002}}} And then distribute all of it. {{note:{index:1037,id:UT22084-079-008-3003}}} {9.2.11}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3004}} “Having extracted the ambrosia in its {{note:{index:1038,id:UT22084-079-008-3005}}} center, He should have [the lord of the maṇḍala and his retinue] taste of it. And with all the other articles, such as the remainder of ambrosia, He should satiate the members of the outer maṇḍala. {{note:{index:1039,id:UT22084-079-008-3006}}} {9.2.12}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3007}} “Holding the skull cup with the left hand, He should display the gesture of wrath with the right. With feet wide apart {{note:{index:1040,id:UT22084-079-008-3008}}} and upward gaze, The syllable pheṭ should emerge from his head. {{note:{index:1041,id:UT22084-079-008-3009}}} {9.2.13}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3010}} “Making his offerings on the fourteenth day, Or especially the eighth day, of the dark fortnight, Or also on the tenth day of the bright fortnight, He should himself become the inner offerings. {{note:{index:1042,id:UT22084-079-008-3011}}} {9.2.14}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3012}} “Under {{note:{index:1043,id:UT22084-079-008-3013}}} solitary trees, in charnel grounds, Mountains, wilderness, Caves, outskirts of villages, Empty fields, or, especially, in empty houses— {9.2.15}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3014}} “In particular, in places containing living beings, On dry land as well as on water— He should invoke Black Rudra and Great Rudra In union with their consort goddesses; {{note:{index:1044,id:UT22084-079-008-3015}}} {9.2.16}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3016}} “Black Kapālin, Bībhatsa, Nandātīta and Vināyaka; {{note:{index:1045,id:UT22084-079-008-3017}}} Caṇḍālī, {{note:{index:1046,id:UT22084-079-008-3018}}} {{page:{number:159,folio:F.152.b}}} Ghorarūpā, And Umādevī, in places all around; {{note:{index:1047,id:UT22084-079-008-3019}}} {9.2.17}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3020}} “Jayā, Vijayā, Ajitā and Aparājitā; Bhadrakālī, Mahākālī, And the yoginī Śūlakālī; {9.2.18}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3021}} “Indrī, Candrī, Ghorī, Duṣṭī, Lampakī, Tridaśeśvarī, Kambojī, Dipinī, Cūṣaṇī, And the yoginīs dwelling in villages. {9.2.19}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3022}} “All these goddesses have terrible, huge forms. Baring their formidable fangs, they each wear a garland of human skulls And hold khaṭvāṅgas in their hands. They are all endowed with great powers. {{note:{index:1048,id:UT22084-079-008-3023}}} {9.2.20}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3024}} “They hold in their hands a sword, An axe, a vajra scepter, and a bow. He should also summon the five {{note:{index:1049,id:UT22084-079-008-3025}}} ḍākinīs Of the five great elements who accomplish every type of activity, {9.2.21}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3026}} “And the great queen {{note:{index:1050,id:UT22084-079-008-3027}}} of the maṇḍala of the union, Along with the mighty vajra lord. {{note:{index:1051,id:UT22084-079-008-3028}}} In the great assembly of the tathāgatas She {{note:{index:1052,id:UT22084-079-008-3029}}} is the stainless emanation from the union. {{note:{index:1053,id:UT22084-079-008-3030}}} {9.2.22}
“By the command of the vajra queen, {{note:{index:1054,id:UT22084-079-008-3032}}} he should invoke all of them {{note:{index:1055,id:UT22084-079-008-3033}}} from all their respective places. {9.2.23}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3034}} “He should recite:
“ Oṁ , p-pp-pull, b-bb-bind, d-dd-devour! Kill, kill all the evil ones! S-ss-strike! Appease all negativity for such and such! Hūṁ hūṁ! Phaṭ phaṭ! Jaḥ, svāhā! {{note:{index:1056,id:UT22084-079-008-3036}}} {{note:{index:1057,id:UT22084-079-008-3037}}} {9.2.24}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3038}} “Relying on the contemplation of ambrosia {{note:{index:1058,id:UT22084-079-008-3039}}} and filling thereby the mouths of the deities {{note:{index:1059,id:UT22084-079-008-3040}}} with it, he should meditate on yogins and yoginīs as the executors of any activity he can think of. He will then succeed in every type of activity. {{note:{index:1060,id:UT22084-079-008-3041}}} {9.2.25}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3042}} “The syllable ha removes the ambrosia’s ordinary {{note:{index:1061,id:UT22084-079-008-3043}}} color, The syllable ho neutralizes its ordinary {{note:{index:1062,id:UT22084-079-008-3044}}} odor, And the syllable hrī removes its ordinary {{note:{index:1063,id:UT22084-079-008-3045}}} potency— This is the prescribed order of reciting these three syllables. {9.2.26}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3046}} “Repeating these three syllables thrice, He should meditate on them as the three deities. {{note:{index:1064,id:UT22084-079-008-3047}}} {9.2.27}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3048}} “Padmeśvara (Amitābha) possesses the beauty and loveliness of gold; The beautifully lucent one (Vairocana) possesses an incorruptible perfume; And Vajrapāṇi (Akṣobhya) is the vajra lord of good flavor. {{note:{index:1065,id:UT22084-079-008-3049}}} These three deities are known as the above three syllables. {9.2.28}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3050}} “ ‘See all phenomena here as pure! Discard nihilist meditation! {{note:{index:1066,id:UT22084-079-008-3051}}} Since brahmins, dogs, and outcastes are Of the same nature, eat [everything]!’ {9.2.29}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3052}} “Reciting the lines of this verse, he should offer [the ambrosia oblation], {{page:{number:160,folio:F.153.a}}} And then display the gesture of “turning the lotus” {{note:{index:1067,id:UT22084-079-008-3053}}} {9.2.30}
“With his left and right hands, Playfully and with supreme grace. He should proceed according to instruction Through the practice of his personal deity. {{note:{index:1068,id:UT22084-079-008-3055}}} {9.2.31}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3056}} “ ‘The Sugata’s teaching is priceless; It is free from the stains of passion And from grasping and non-grasping. Let us pay homage to it with devotion.’ {{note:{index:1069,id:UT22084-079-008-3057}}} {9.2.32}
“With this verse, he should receive [the ambrosia]. This is the principle of the yogin’s proper practice, pure in every respect. {9.2.33}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3059}} “He should then recite the following as he wishes:
“ ‘Let us pay homage to the one who is free from becoming And supplicate him that beings may reach pleasant destinies. May they be adorned with the magical display Of the coupling embrace, hūṁ hūṁ hūṁ !’ {{note:{index:1070,id:UT22084-079-008-3061}}} {9.2.34}
“He should sing this song of benediction To the accompaniment of the bell. {9.2.35}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3063}} “Folding his hands in the vajra gesture of añjali, He should position them at his heart. Then, he should make a dedication For the sake of all sentient beings, and so forth, reciting: {9.2.36}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3064}} “ ‘May all beings be happy! May all beings be well! May they traverse the path By which they will attain awakening! {9.2.37}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3065}} “ ‘I will deliver those who have not been delivered. I will release those who have not been released. I will be compassionate toward them in their present condition, Acting consistently with the teachings of yoga.’ {9.2.38}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3066}} “He should form the ‘vajra fist’ with both hands. Placing the left fist at his heart, He should extend the right one forward and, Placing it on the ground, dismiss the deities {{note:{index:1071,id:UT22084-079-008-3067}}} by saying: {9.2.39}
“ Oṁ , Please remain in my body! Hūṁ svāhā! {{note:{index:1072,id:UT22084-079-008-3069}}} {9.2.40}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3070}} “Subsequently, the deities {{note:{index:1073,id:UT22084-079-008-3071}}} are absorbed Into his body with his breath. In an instantaneous union, he should make offerings, Visualizing himself as the deity. {{note:{index:1074,id:UT22084-079-008-3072}}} {9.2.41}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3073}} “He should recite:
“ Oṁ , seize, seize the evil ones and depart! Hūṁ phaṭ! {{note:{index:1075,id:UT22084-079-008-3075}}} {9.2.42}
“He should snap his fingers three times and dismiss the outer deities.” {{note:{index:1076,id:UT22084-079-008-3077}}} {9.2.43}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3078}} This concludes the second part of the ninth chapter, about the offering of oblation.
Part 3
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3079}} While the Blessed One, ever-present in every body, Was abiding within the secret lotus, the pleasure realm of Sukhāvatī, The goddess who, for her own part, abides in secrecy, {{page:{number:161,folio:F.153.b}}} Requested the following: {9.3.1}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3080}} “Please tell me everything, O lord! Tell me about the hidden domain of sublime reality, {{note:{index:1077,id:UT22084-079-008-3081}}} About the maṇḍala of all the tathāgatas, And also about the wrathful ones and the deities. {9.3.2}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3082}} “I do know the ultimate reality Which is present within myself, But I am not certain regarding the methods Of making the painting and writing the manuscript. {9.3.3}
“I do not know that, so please tell me, O Great Bliss!” {9.3.4}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3083}} The Blessed One said:
“The painter should be a young person with a pure heart, Steadfast, gentle, and free of discursive thinking. He should be free of deceit and anger, well trained, Dexterous, {{note:{index:1078,id:UT22084-079-008-3086}}} and full of faith and compassion. {9.3.5}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3087}} “Alternatively, to do the painting, one should commission a painter who has been given the samaya. Such a sublime practitioner should paint Tārā, Mārīcī, or Parṇaśāvarī on cloth from a fallen war hero, cloth that wrapped a corpse, cloth used during childbirth, cloth stained with human blood, or cloth soaked with menstrual blood. {9.3.6}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3088}} “This is the procedure to follow. Staying at a secret location, one should have a well-focused person do the painting; he should paint the frightening form {{note:{index:1079,id:UT22084-079-008-3089}}} with a brush of a corpse’s hair, using the five colors as explained, mixed with olibanum, camphor, and other ambrosias, placed in a human skull. {{note:{index:1080,id:UT22084-079-008-3090}}} {9.3.7}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3091}} “First, the teacher, well focused, united in embrace with the consort (prajñā), adorned with all manner of jewelry, and abiding in union with the glorious Sampuṭa, should take off his clothes, while visualizing himself as wearing bone ornaments. {{note:{index:1081,id:UT22084-079-008-3092}}} {9.3.8}
“The wise should not have the painting done with leftover or impure materials.” {9.3.9}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3093}} [The goddess asked:]
“O Blessed One, if the paints are infused with olibanum (menstrual blood), how then would they not be impure?” {{note:{index:1082,id:UT22084-079-008-3096}}} {9.3.10}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3097}} The Blessed One said:
“The first purity is the messenger lady, {{note:{index:1083,id:UT22084-079-008-3099}}} Moon {{note:{index:1084,id:UT22084-079-008-3100}}} is regarded as the second, {{page:{number:162,folio:F.154.a}}} And all the dainty foodstuffs together {{note:{index:1085,id:UT22084-079-008-3101}}} Are said to be the third purity. {{note:{index:1086,id:UT22084-079-008-3102}}} {9.3.11}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3103}} “These purities should be undertaken By those who enjoy external yoga. {{note:{index:1087,id:UT22084-079-008-3104}}} Should one’s mind become impure, Of what use would be ritual ablutions? {{note:{index:1088,id:UT22084-079-008-3105}}} {9.3.12}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3106}} “Anyone who lives by a perverse Dharma, Desiring all kinds of sense pleasures, Will be born one hundred times as a dog, And later be reborn among the outcastes. {9.3.13}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3107}} “Just as someone who wants ghee But naively churns water, Does not obtain ghee But only physical exhaustion, {9.3.14}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3108}} “So too will the concentration and veneration Of those with other such aims be futile— If it is for the sake of vitality, They should rather resort to other types of yoga. {{note:{index:1089,id:UT22084-079-008-3109}}} {9.3.15}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3110}} “Who would disparage the skull That embodies the dharmakāya— The skull arisen from the material cause Common to the triad of conch, oyster shell, and pearl? {{note:{index:1090,id:UT22084-079-008-3111}}} {9.3.16}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3112}} “The means of purification of those invested with the sacred cord Is said to be their conduct {{note:{index:1091,id:UT22084-079-008-3113}}} conforming to the true Dharma. Since the purity is found in the glorious Heruka, One should worship with all perseverance Together with one’s consort (mudrā). {9.3.17}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3114}} “The practitioner should thus place his personal consort (mudrā) to his left. She should have a beautiful face and fine figure, be compassionately disposed, be graced with beauty and youth, and be fond of the practitioner. One should consecrate the brush and give it to the painter. {9.3.18}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3115}} “The painter should make a painting that inspires Dread and bounteously grants all accomplishments. It should be viewed by the painter and the practitioner, Without being shown to anyone else. {9.3.19}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3116}} “Listen, O goddess of great fortune! I will now teach you about the writing of the manuscript. One who has been given the samaya Should write it either on birchbark or palm leaf. {9.3.20}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3117}} “One should make the folios Twelve fingers long And use ‘great honey’ {{note:{index:1092,id:UT22084-079-008-3118}}} as ink. It should be written with a stylus of human bone. {9.3.21}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3119}} “Should an inappropriate person see Either the manuscript or the painting, No accomplishment will be had in this life, Nor in the domains of the afterlife. {9.3.22}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3120}} “One should never allow others To see the samayasattva. {{note:{index:1093,id:UT22084-079-008-3121}}} {{page:{number:163,folio:F.154.b}}} When in public view, one should hide The book in one’s hair or under the armpit. {9.3.23}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3122}} “One can, however, lend it to those who share the same samaya, So that they can copy it prior to performing the ritual.” {{note:{index:1094,id:UT22084-079-008-3123}}} {9.3.24}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3124}} This concludes the third part of the ninth chapter, called “The Codification of the Painting and the Manuscript.”
Part 4
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3125}} “Listen, O goddess, I will now teach the music {{note:{index:1095,id:UT22084-079-008-3126}}} Characteristic ( lakṣaṇa ) of sampuṭa. {9.4.1}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3127}} “The mantra of Vajradhara {{note:{index:1096,id:UT22084-079-008-3128}}} (as sampuṭa) and the others is:
“ Ara ara, jeṁ jeṁ ! Recollect recollect! Caṭa! Vaṁ, hoḥ hoḥ! Hulu hulu! Rulu rulu! Hūṁ, jaḥ jaḥ! Ala ala! Hūṇu Hūṇu! Hraṁ hraṁ hraṁ! Hū taṁ, ghai ghai, yai yai! Ta ṭa, gho gho, ṣeṁ ṣeṁ, taṁ taṁ, ghe ghe, hondo hondo, do! Hūṁ hūṁ! Kaka kaka, kau kau kau, vaiṃ vaiṃ, kaiṃ kaiṃ, krauṁ krauṁ krauṁ, vaiṁ! Vajra vajra, vajrīṁ vajrīṃ, vaiḥ, kaiṁ kaiṃ kaiṁ, hūṁ! Bhyo bhyo bhyo! {{note:{index:1097,id:UT22084-079-008-3130}}} {9.4.2}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3131}} “The mantra of Līlāgati {{note:{index:1098,id:UT22084-079-008-3132}}} is as follows:
“ Ṭaki, hūṁ, jaḥ jaḥ jaḥ! {{note:{index:1099,id:UT22084-079-008-3134}}} {9.4.3}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3135}} “The mantra of Hayagrīva is:
“ Taḍava taḍava! {{note:{index:1100,id:UT22084-079-008-3137}}} To the steed, the steed! {{note:{index:1101,id:UT22084-079-008-3138}}} {9.4.4}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3139}} “The mantra of Yamarāja is:
“ Hrīṁ ṣṭrīṁ, hrīṁ ṣṭrīṁ, ṣṭrīṁ ṣṭrīṁ ṣṭrīṁ, hrīṁ ṣṭrīṁ, hrīṁ ṣṭrīṁ, hrīṁ ṣṭrīṁ! {{note:{index:1102,id:UT22084-079-008-3141}}} {9.4.5}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3142}} “The mantra of Tārā is:
“ Hrīṁ hrīṁ, kuṁ hrīṁ, kuṁ hrīṁ, khe khe, kheṁ kheṁ kheṁ, padmaṃ padmaṃ, hrīṁ, padmaṃ padmaṃ padmaṃ, trīṁ trāṁ, trīṁ trāṁ, trīṁ trāṁ, hrīṁ hrīṁ hrīṁ, hrī taṁ, hrī taṁ, hrīṁ hrīṁ hrīṁ! {{note:{index:1103,id:UT22084-079-008-3144}}} {9.4.6}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3145}} “I will now describe the characteristics of the small hand drum {{note:{index:1104,id:UT22084-079-008-3146}}} used for these mantras.
“One should make this drum from the root of a sandal tree {{note:{index:1105,id:UT22084-079-008-3148}}} Belonging to the red variety found in the Himālayas, {{note:{index:1106,id:UT22084-079-008-3149}}} And also any other articles That are pleasing to the mind.” {9.4.7}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3150}} Then the Blessed One specified the following measurements:
“It should be twelve or ten finger-widths in length, {{note:{index:1107,id:UT22084-079-008-3152}}} With a drumhead that is six or five finger-widths in diameter. It can also be nine or eleven finger-widths in length, With the drumhead being half of that. {9.4.8}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3153}} “Optionally, to make a different kind of drum,
“One should stretch monkey skin on a human skull, So that it forms its drumhead. Inside each of the two hollows of the skull one should draw a lotus. To make it beautiful, one should draw it with menstrual blood. {9.4.9}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3155}} “One should tie together the two pieces of skull bone With a string twined from human hair recovered from a cemetery. Then, using only ‘secret flower,’ {{note:{index:1108,id:UT22084-079-008-3156}}} one should draw a maṇḍala On the pericarp of each of the two lotuses in the hollows of the skull. {9.4.10}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3157}} “One should go at nighttime to a crossroads and draw, With the big toe of one’s left foot, A vajra hook in each of the corners Of a four-sided maṇḍala. {9.4.11} {{page:{number:164,folio:F.155.a}}}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3158}} “Stepping there with one’s left heel, one should recite kheṁ hūṁ, Preceded by the summoning formula with the target’s name. While reciting kheṁ hūṁ, One should stomp one’s left foot in the manner of a lapwing. {{note:{index:1109,id:UT22084-079-008-3159}}} {9.4.12}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3160}} “In this way, all the six Kambojīs Will be summoned without a doubt. {{note:{index:1110,id:UT22084-079-008-3161}}} If they do not come, All these ḍākinīs will die. {9.4.13}
“So they will certainly respond to the ritual; There is no doubt about what I have said. {9.4.14}
“If the master plays the ḍamaru when agitated, {{note:{index:1111,id:UT22084-079-008-3164}}} the ḍākinīs will cry a torrent of tears. {9.4.15}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3163}} “[The following is a password song to get admitted to a gaṇacakra feast:]
“ ‘Your samaya conduct shines brightly, O Blue Angry One! {{note:{index:1112,id:UT22084-079-008-3167}}} In your hand you hold a staff set with precious stones. {{note:{index:1113,id:UT22084-079-008-3168}}} Behold me, O hero, amidst the yoginīs, entering the door to the assembly, The assembly that is the liberated saṃsāra.’ {{note:{index:1114,id:UT22084-079-008-3169}}} {9.4.16}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3170}} “Listen, O goddess, O greatly fortunate one, About the excellent {{note:{index:1115,id:UT22084-079-008-3171}}} things offered at the gaṇacakra. If one partakes of them, the accomplishment will follow— One that will bring the fulfillment of all wishes. {9.4.17}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3172}} “In a charnel ground, a mountain thicket, On the shore of a great ocean, In a deserted place or wilderness, One should prepare the following articles of enjoyment: {9.4.18}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3173}} “Flowers, incense, and lamps, And also hard and soft foodstuffs. The liquor is said to be a playful woman; The wine is said to be a wanton woman. {9.4.19}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3174}} “The rum is said to be the god of love; This best of alcohols is ambrosia. {{note:{index:1116,id:UT22084-079-008-3175}}} Through the outcaste of all buddhas, Ambrosia is the eightfold path. {{note:{index:1117,id:UT22084-079-008-3176}}} {9.4.20}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3177}} “The sweet grape wine {{note:{index:1118,id:UT22084-079-008-3178}}} is the Sole Hero; The oyster shell is the One with Harsh Desire. {{note:{index:1119,id:UT22084-079-008-3179}}} The rice brew (masculine) is said to be a sensualist, {{note:{index:1120,id:UT22084-079-008-3180}}} And the rice brew (feminine) {{note:{index:1121,id:UT22084-079-008-3181}}} is said to be a female slave. {9.4.21}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3182}} “By having the good fortune to partake, In this way, of such delicacies As various foods, alcoholic beverages, and fish, One will attain the level of glorious Vajrasattva. {9.4.22}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3183}} “Ripe mangoes, breadfruit, Grapes, coconuts, plums, and so forth— One should offer, at the gaṇacakra gathering, An assortment of different fruits. {9.4.23}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3184}} “A special dance should be performed, along with gestures and singing: {{page:{number:165,folio:F.155.b}}}
“ Ka ka ka ka ka, hi hi hi hi, hīṁ hīṁ hīṁ hīṁ, hūṁ hūṁ hūṁ, hūṁ hūṁ hūṁ, hūṁ hūṁ hūṁ, hā hā hā hā, hā hā hā hā, hā hā hā hā, i hā hā, i hā hā, ḍā ḍā ḍā, jāṁ jāṁ jāṁ jāṁ, a i u, jaṁ jāṁ, iṁ jāṁ, iṁ jāṁ, iṁ iṁ, jeṁ jeṁ jeṁ, iṁ teṁ traṁ, hi hi hi hi, hīḥ hīḥ hīḥ, hi hi hi, hī hī hī, hī hī hī, hī hī hī, kajjaṃ, hi hī. {{note:{index:1122,id:UT22084-079-008-3186}}} {9.4.24}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3187}} “Singing thus, an outcaste woman shakes to this song. The dance, and in particular the ritual gestures, Should be performed while in meditative union with Heruka. {9.4.25}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3188}} “Since the gazes correspond with the fist gestures, And both are synchronized with the footsteps of the dance, They express the stages of yoga As performed by all the buddhas. {{note:{index:1123,id:UT22084-079-008-3189}}} {9.4.26}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3190}} “The consort could be one’s mother, Sister, younger sister, or niece. {{note:{index:1124,id:UT22084-079-008-3191}}} One should worship them ardently, And one will gain accomplishment at the gaṇacakra feast. {9.4.27}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3192}} “The pupil should present to his master, O fortunate lady, A human skull cup made from a single piece of bone, Filled with divinely {{note:{index:1125,id:UT22084-079-008-3193}}} delicious wine. Having made obeisance to him, he should drink of it himself. {9.4.28}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3194}} “He should hold it and offer it With the same hand forming a lotus gesture. The officiants should bow at this point To the master again and again.” {9.4.29}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3195}} This concludes the ninth chapter of the glorious “ Emergence from Sampuṭa ” called “The King of the Essence of the Four Rituals.”
Chapter 10
Part 1
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3196}} “Listen, Vajrapāṇi, about the samaya that results In the accomplishments of a vajra master. {{note:{index:1126,id:UT22084-079-008-3197}}} Having prepared the Great Circle, which comes first, One should summon the heart maṇḍala. {{note:{index:1127,id:UT22084-079-008-3198}}} {10.1.1}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3199}} “Through one’s entering the first, the Great Circle, And performing there the elaborate ritual of initiation and so forth, One will attain the unequaled status Of a vajra master, there can be no doubt. {10.1.2}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3200}} “For by being devoted to meditation upon what was learned, One will attain the status of a vajra master. One will fully succeed after reciting The heart mantra of Vajrasattva, and so forth, 100,000 times. {10.1.3}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3201}} “Once one becomes a fully accomplished great master, One’s accomplishment will endure through all the ages. {{note:{index:1128,id:UT22084-079-008-3202}}} By this means sentient beings become the victorious buddhas {{note:{index:1129,id:UT22084-079-008-3203}}} — Can there be any doubt about this? {10.1.4}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3204}} “Those who make an effort to abide in nonduality Don their armor and adhere to reality. {{note:{index:1130,id:UT22084-079-008-3205}}} {10.1.5}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3206}} “Whatever female consort (mudrā) has been prescribed to whatever male By the omniscient ones based on the [buddha] family association of the two, {{page:{number:166,folio:F.156.a}}} Such a consort (mudrā) should be procured through the prescribed means Only by such a partner, who will practice only with her. {10.1.6}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3207}} “If he whose nature is delusion obtains the mother, {{note:{index:1131,id:UT22084-079-008-3208}}} Or a learned brahmin woman, Such a meditator, after purifying his delusion, Will in actuality become Vairocana. {10.1.7}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3209}} “The mother is the ultimate consort (vidyā), Especially if she was just before enjoyed by the father. She will definitely grant an accomplishment, As has been declared by the lord Great Bliss. {10.1.8}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3210}} “If he whose nature is hatred obtains An outcaste woman’s daughter, or a yakṣa girl, Such a meditator will, after purifying his hatred, Attain, in actuality, the state of Akṣobhya. {10.1.9}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3211}} “If he whose nature is passion obtains a dancer’s daughter, His own younger sister, or a nāga or asura girl, Such a meditator, after purifying his lust, Will become, in his nature, {{note:{index:1132,id:UT22084-079-008-3212}}} Amitābha. {10.1.10}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3213}} “If he whose nature is envy obtains A lovely apsaras, expert in crafts, or one’s own niece, Such a meditator will become, After purifying his envy, the hero Amoghasiddhi. {10.1.11}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3214}} “If he whose nature is arrogance obtains a king’s daughter, Or perhaps a daughter or a wife of a vidyādhara, {{note:{index:1133,id:UT22084-079-008-3215}}} Such a meditator will become, after purifying his arrogance, Ratnasambhava, and will join the jewel family. {10.1.12}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3216}} “Consorting with Locanā, he becomes Tathāgata Buddha; With Māmakī, he attains the state of Tathāgata Akṣobhya; With Pāṇḍaravāsinī, Amitābha of the lotus family; And with Tārā, he will attain the state of Amoghasiddhi. {10.1.13}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3217}} “Alternatively, he can become Ratnasambhava by consorting with Ratnolkā. In this way has the union of the two partners been taught. Through this union he can attain also the state of other deities, Such as wrathful deities or divine daughters of the victorious ones. {{note:{index:1134,id:UT22084-079-008-3218}}} {10.1.14}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3219}} “Wrathful deities can be accomplished by fierce rites; Peaceful deities, only by peaceful rites. Impassioned deities are accomplished by passionate rites; Haughty deities, by the rites of enriching. {10.1.15}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3220}} “Such methods, which are free of hardship, Have been praised by the omniscient and compassionate masters. These methods are for attaining extraordinary bliss, Without severe precepts or austere practices. {10.1.16}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3221}} “If someone, having obtained the taste of ambrosia in this way, Does not make effort for the sake of removing his afflictions, {{page:{number:167,folio:F.156.b}}} How would he be able to produce awakening By following precepts {{note:{index:1135,id:UT22084-079-008-3222}}} that are difficult to keep? {10.1.17}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3223}} “The fool who does not do anything for his own sake, After having found his personal easy practice, Where will he go next {{note:{index:1136,id:UT22084-079-008-3224}}} after departing from this life? He cannot know where he will be reborn again. {{note:{index:1137,id:UT22084-079-008-3225}}} {10.1.18}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3226}} “Genuine people, once they become realized through this practice, Will always see all activities and their effects as a dream or illusion. He who does not understand the Buddhadharma should do this practice Until he reaches the other shore of the ocean of saṃsāra.” {10.1.19}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3227}} This concludes the first part of the tenth chapter, on the consecration to the position of a master by means of a consort (mudrā).
Part 2
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3229}} “The following powers become unleashed {{note:{index:1138,id:UT22084-079-008-3228}}} When a man becomes accomplished through a consort (vidyā): {{note:{index:1139,id:UT22084-079-008-3230}}} The earth will shake in six different ways As the earth goddess will be filled with ecstatic happiness. {10.2.1}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3231}} “Overjoyed, she will make a sound like the bell-metal cymbals Produced in the country of Magadha. {{note:{index:1140,id:UT22084-079-008-3232}}} Meteor showers will fall throughout the ten directions, Resembling the fire at the end of an eon. {10.2.2}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3233}} “The oceans will roar with turbulence, And hurricanes {{note:{index:1141,id:UT22084-079-008-3234}}} will strike everywhere. Right there, the lights of gnosis will flare up, Resembling the fire during the final destruction. {10.2.3}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3235}} “All the worlds of the triple universe Will become the womb of the consort (vidyā). {{note:{index:1142,id:UT22084-079-008-3236}}} Brahmā, Viṣṇu, Varuṇa, Śakra, Rudra, Agni, the Āśvins, {{note:{index:1143,id:UT22084-079-008-3237}}} Bhānu {{note:{index:1144,id:UT22084-079-008-3238}}} and Candra, {10.2.4}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3239}} “The yakṣas, celestial siddhas, gandharvas, Kiṃnaras, nāgas, {{note:{index:1145,id:UT22084-079-008-3240}}} vidyādharas, Apsarases, and so forth, and those in other places, The gods residing in the Realm of the Thirty-Three, {10.2.5}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3241}} “Having come there, overjoyed, Will throw heaps of flowers in offering. Floating in the sky they will worship {{note:{index:1146,id:UT22084-079-008-3242}}} With the sounds of lutes, flutes, drums, {{note:{index:1147,id:UT22084-079-008-3243}}} {10.2.6}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3244}} “ Madhurīs, {{note:{index:1148,id:UT22084-079-008-3245}}} conches, large drums, {{note:{index:1149,id:UT22084-079-008-3246}}} {{note:{index:1150,id:UT22084-079-008-3247}}} Piccolo flutes, kettle drums, and tambourines. {{note:{index:1151,id:UT22084-079-008-3248}}} The apsaras girls will dance and so too will All the young daughters of vidyādhara kings. {{note:{index:1152,id:UT22084-079-008-3249}}} {10.2.7}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3250}} “The kiṃnaras will sing songs And play various instruments. {{page:{number:168,folio:F.157.a}}} The yakṣas will shout, “Victory! Victory!” Playing around and making merry. {{note:{index:1153,id:UT22084-079-008-3251}}} {10.2.8}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3252}} “Rejoicing at this event, the celestial siddhas will extend their congratulations. {{note:{index:1154,id:UT22084-079-008-3253}}} The gods from the Tuṣita Realm, the most eminent gods from places near and far, the divine and semi-divine sons, the celestial vidyādharas—all will bow in reverence, filling space as far as the realm of Akaniṣṭha. {{note:{index:1155,id:UT22084-079-008-3254}}} {10.2.9}
“With great devotion they will offer heaps of different kinds of flowers, rains of different fragrances, and different kinds of prime quality incense. Of what need would a detailed description of other offered items be to you? Whatever articles are worth offering in the three realms for merit to be gained, they will offer them.” {10.2.10}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3256}} This concludes the second part of the tenth chapter, called “The Worship and Homage on the Occasion of the Accomplishment of Great Bliss.”
Part 3
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3257}} [The goddess asked:]
“Where does the man accomplished by means of a consort (vidyā) go, and where does he remain? I am not certain about this. Please tell me, O Great Bliss.” {10.3.1}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3259}} The Blessed One said:
“A man accomplished by means of a consort (vidyā) does not go anywhere, nor does he remain anywhere. He is the light of the triple universe, which is nondual and has no beginning, middle, or end. He is everywhere, he is omniscient, he is universal, and he is all things. {{note:{index:1156,id:UT22084-079-008-3261}}} He abides in the consciousness of all beings and is free of all negativity. Adorned with all good qualities, he is endowed with everything. He brings happiness, {{note:{index:1157,id:UT22084-079-008-3262}}} and is a peerless, perpetually arising {{note:{index:1158,id:UT22084-079-008-3263}}} lord and protector, free of conceptual thinking. Devoid of shape and color, he is the king {{note:{index:1159,id:UT22084-079-008-3264}}} beyond the purview of even the victorious ones. {10.3.2}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3265}} “Being unbreakable, {{note:{index:1160,id:UT22084-079-008-3266}}} he is the vajra. Free from the burning torment of afflictions, he is the cool-rayed moon. Free of doubt, he is like a lion. Difficult to fathom, he is like an ocean. {10.3.3} {{page:{number:169,folio:F.157.b}}}
“In this way he is described by yogins using the comparisons just given. He alone fulfills the interests of every sentient being. {10.3.4}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3268}} “Even though he is devoid of conceptual thought, he displays the great deeds, including (1) birth which is his final one, (2) leaving home, {{note:{index:1161,id:UT22084-079-008-3269}}} (3) the playful exploits of his childhood, (3) leaving his household, (4) the solitary peregrinations of a religious mendicant, {{note:{index:1162,id:UT22084-079-008-3270}}} (6) reaching the spot of the vajra seat, (7) defeating Māra, {{note:{index:1163,id:UT22084-079-008-3271}}} (8) attaining an unequaled state of perfect awakening, {{note:{index:1164,id:UT22084-079-008-3272}}} (9) giving instructions that constitute the turning of the wheel of Dharma, (10) enjoying the descent from the realm of gods, (11) performing a great variety of miraculous feats, (12) subjugation of the elephant Dhanapāla, (13) inducting virtuous people into purity, {{note:{index:1165,id:UT22084-079-008-3273}}} (14) refuting opposing doctrines, (15) blameless subsistence by the alms bowl, {{note:{index:1166,id:UT22084-079-008-3274}}} (16) taming the inhabitants of the triple universe, (17) becoming the crown prince of bodhisattvas, {{note:{index:1167,id:UT22084-079-008-3275}}} (18) fulfilling the great aim of parinirvāṇa, {{note:{index:1168,id:UT22084-079-008-3276}}} and (19) becoming the Dharma king of the three realms. {10.3.5}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3277}} “So it is, O sons of the noble lineage! He who is accomplished will in this way display, employing illusory forms, the marvelous play of a buddha for the benefit of all beings—the play extraordinary in many ways and said to be like a dream.” {{note:{index:1169,id:UT22084-079-008-3278}}} {10.3.6}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3279}} This concludes the third part of the tenth chapter called “The Buddha’s Magical Transformations.”
Part 4
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3280}} [The goddess said:]
“You have previously mentioned, O lord, a homa offering consisting of feces, urine, menstrual blood, fish, and meat. {10.4.1}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3282}} “How is it with regard to the wisdom beings, That their mouths should be filled with impurities? How is it that no nonvirtue is committed? Were one in fact nonvirtuous, what would the result be?” {10.4.2}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3283}} The Blessed One said:
“Beings who are deluded by not knowing, And deprived of gnosis and skillful means, Are strongly attached to external objects And are thus confounded by the mass of concepts. {{note:{index:1170,id:UT22084-079-008-3285}}} {10.4.3}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3286}} “To them, sin and merit Seem to be two separate categories. In truth, though, these phenomena are By nature pure—unarisen and without basis. {10.4.4}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3287}} “The buddhas taught the skillful means of merit In order to develop gnosis in beings. {{page:{number:170,folio:F.158.a}}} But if, in terms of the absolute truth, merit is to be abandoned, Why hold on to the concept of demerit? {{note:{index:1171,id:UT22084-079-008-3288}}} {10.4.5}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3289}} “Just as someone crossing to the other shore Of a river filled with water Will build a raft that floats on the surface By assembling logs of wood and bundles of straw, {10.4.6}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3290}} “But after having crossed the river clutching to it, He will discard it and walk on without difficulty, So too someone crossing to the other shore of saṃsāra Will ride upon the distinction between right and wrong. {10.4.7}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3291}} “Once awakening has been safely attained, It is free from the distinction between right and wrong. Consequently, he will develop in the profound Dharma Once he has discarded the network of concepts. {10.4.8}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3292}} “When traveling the path taught by the tathāgatas, The mantra adept {{note:{index:1172,id:UT22084-079-008-3293}}} should not entertain concepts, For concepts are great ignorance— They mire one in the ocean of saṃsāra. {10.4.9}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3294}} “He who abides in nonconceptual samādhi Will shine, stainless as the sky. When the vital powers of the coupling pair combine, Their bodies, speech, and minds likewise coalesce. {{note:{index:1173,id:UT22084-079-008-3295}}} {10.4.10}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3296}} “By this means they attain identity with the deity, Thus becoming reflections of the Victorious One, devoid of all forms. You should cause this gnosis to unfold, Becoming its adepts in this very life. {10.4.11}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3297}} “It has been taught that the bodies of women and men Are a complex result of their actions. One should not, out of ignorance, act waywardly— This is the samaya of vajra body. {{note:{index:1174,id:UT22084-079-008-3298}}} {10.4.12}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3299}} “One should not corrupt their minds By burdening sentient beings with various austerities That give rise to stressful conceptual thinking— This is the samaya of vajra mind. {{note:{index:1175,id:UT22084-079-008-3300}}} {10.4.13}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3301}} “One should not say words that are Slanderous, untrue, or harsh, But only those that are pleasant to the listener— This is the samaya of vajra speech. {{note:{index:1176,id:UT22084-079-008-3302}}} {10.4.14}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3303}} “The buddha who abides in the flesh element Is Vairocana, the seniormost of the five. Akṣobhya dwells in the marrow of the bones; Blood is the domain of Ratnasambhava, adorned with magnificent jewels. {10.4.15}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3304}} “Amitābha is the bones, Understood to be the compactness within all beings. {{note:{index:1177,id:UT22084-079-008-3305}}} Amoghasiddhi, the most eminent of sages, Sustains the network of sinews and tendons. {{note:{index:1178,id:UT22084-079-008-3306}}} {10.4.16}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3307}} “A secret will now be taught to you, The samaya for adepts in gnosis: {10.4.17} {{page:{number:171,folio:F.158.b}}}
“Using the vajra mind, the wise one Should always pay attention to and cultivate Desire, hatred, delusion, craving, And volitions, causing their increase. {{note:{index:1179,id:UT22084-079-008-3309}}} {10.4.18}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3310}} “These five have been taught by the buddhas, the most eminent of sages, as the fivefold effluence of feces, urine, semen, phlegm, and menstrual blood. He should observe {{note:{index:1180,id:UT22084-079-008-3311}}} the samayas through mental cultivation in full, based on embracing the four elements. He should always ingest these samaya substances. {{note:{index:1181,id:UT22084-079-008-3312}}} {10.4.19}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3313}} “Just as a lover delighting in young women’s talk Would extend an invitation to meet one of them for a chat And describe the path to take rather than obstruct it, So too is the excellent path pointed out to a yogin, in the like manner.” {{note:{index:1182,id:UT22084-079-008-3314}}} {10.4.20}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3315}} Then, everyone in the audience—the yogins and yoginīs, the eighty crores of ḍākas and ḍākinīs, many bodhisattvas and the numerous congregations of tathāgatas—pleased and with minds filled with joy, obtained the gnosis of all the tathāgatas completely. All the great bodhisattva beings, headed by Vajragarbha, and all the gods, nāgas, yakṣas, and gandharvas—the entire assembly—rejoiced at the words of the Blessed One. {10.4.21}
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-3316}} This concludes the tenth great sovereign chapter of the glorious “ Emergence from Sampuṭa ,” the emergence that is the foundation of all tantras.
Colophon
Tibetan Colophon
{{milestone:UT22084-079-008-8102}} This king of tantras was translated by the paṇḍita Gayādhara and the great personage Drokmi Śākya Yeshé. Based on this, the venerable omniscient Butön subsequently [re-]wrote it by filling in the gaps and expertly revising it in consultation with Indian manuscripts of the basic text and commentaries.
